Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Author’s Purpose and Method in al-Tarweeh
Author explains his motivation and method for writing the commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author’s motivation for writing al-Tarweeh, explain the issue of corrupted copies, and define the rhetorical device iham as used in the opening.

Core Idea
The author wrote al-Tarweeh to correct corrupted copies of his earlier work and to unveil deeper meanings through precise lexical analysis.

This passage opens the commentary al-Tarweeh on Tanqih al-Usul. The author, Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, explains why he wrote a second work: early copies of his first book were altered without his authorization. He therefore produced this commentary with a corrected text and expanded explanations, emphasizing the logical and linguistic depth of his work. The Urdu commentary further examines the dual meanings of key words and the rhetorical device iham, setting the stage for rigorous usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his earlier work
Note that the author is Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud, known for Tanqih al-Usul. He begins with the standard Islamic scholarly opening (basmala, hamd, salawat).
The phrase 'jadd' in his lineage is used with iham (ambiguity).
2
Understand the problem prompting the commentary
After Tanqih al-Usul spread, unauthorized changes and errors crept into copies. The author felt compelled to restore accuracy.
This reflects the usul concern for textual authenticity (tahammul al-'ilm).
3
Learn the author's solution
He wrote a commentary (al-Tarweeh) with a corrected version of the matn, clarifying difficult points and avoiding unnecessary verbosity.
The commentary includes definitions, proofs, logical foundations, and elegant arrangement.
4
Examine the lexical analysis of the opening
The Urdu commentary dissects words like 'musalliyan' (blessing / second in a race) and 'jadd' (grandfather / fortune), and defines the rhetorical term iham.
Iham: using a word with two meanings where the listener takes the proximate, but the speaker intends the distant.
5
Appreciate the scholarly ambition
The author claims his work contains subtle investigations not reached by previous scholars in this field, reflecting his high estimation of his contribution.
This is common in scholarly introductions; it asserts the work's value.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله حامدا ومصليا ومستمطرا ومترجما ومسلما ومصليا على أشرف رسله محمد وآله. بعد حمد الله والصلاة على رسوله فإن العبد المتوسل إلى الله بالسبب الوثيق عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة سعد جده وأنجح جده يقول لما وفقني الله بتأليف تنقيح الأصول أردت أن أشرح مشكلاته وأفتح معلقاته معرضا عن شرح المواضع التي من لم يحلها بغير إطناب لا يحل له النظر في ذلك الكتاب. واعلم أنى لما سوّدت كتاب التنقيح وسارع بعض الأصحاب إلى ابتساخه ومباحثته وانتشر النسخ في بعض الأطراف ثم بعد ذلك وقع فيه قليل من التغييرات وشيء من المحو والإثبات فكتبت في هذا الشرح عبارة المتن على النمط الذي تقرر عندي لتغير النسخ المكتوبة قبل التغييرات إلى هذا النمط ثم لما تيسر إتمامه وفض بالاحتمام ختامه مشتملا على تعريفات وحجج مؤسسة على قواعد المعقول وتفريعات مرصعة بعد ضبط الأصول وترتيب أنيق لم يسبقني على مثله أحد مع تدقيقات غامضة لم يبلغ فرسان هذا العلم إلى هذا الأمد.
ترجمہ: ابتداء کرتا ہوں میں اس حال میں کہ برکت حاصل کرنے والا ہوں میں اللہ تعالیٰ کے نام کے ساتھ جو بڑا مہربان نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے۔ (اور ابتداء کرتا ہوں ) میں اس حال میں کہ تعریف کرنے والا ہوں اللہ تعالیٰ کی پہلی مرتبہ اور دوسری مرتبہ اور تعریف کی لگام کو اس کی طرف پھیر نے والا ہوں۔ اور اس کے رسولوں میں سے افضل رسول پر جو کہ محمد صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہیں اور آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی اولاد پر درودوسلام بھیجنے والا ہوں ، اور درود سلام کے میدان میں پہلے نمبر پر اور دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا ہوں ۔ بعد حمد وصلوٰۃ کے پس تحقیق بندو جو وسیلہ پکڑنے والا ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف مضبوط ذریعہ کے ساتھ جو کہ عبید اللہ بن مسعود بن تاج الشرعیہ ہے۔ نیک بخت ہو اس کا نصیبہ اور کامیاب ہو اس کی کوشش کہتا ہے کہ جب تو فیق دی مجھے کو اللہ تعالٰی نے تنقیح الاصول لکھنے کی تو ارادہ کیا میں نے کہ شرح کروں میں اس کی مشکلات کی اور کھول دوں اس کے پیچیدہ مضامین کو اعراض کرتے ہوئے ان جگہوں کی وضاحت سے جن کو اگر کوئی شخص ) حل نہ کر سکے بغیر طوالت کالام کے تو نہ حلال ہو اس کے لئے اس (میری) کتاب میں دیکھنا۔ اور جان لو کہ جب لکھی کی میں نے یہ کتاب التنقیح تو جلدی کی بعض اصحاب نے لو لی اس کے نقل کرنے کی طرف اور اس کے بحث و مباحثہ کی طرف اور پھیل گئے نسخے بعض شہروں میں۔ پھر اس کے بعد واقع ہوئیں اس میں تبدیلیاں تھوڑی سی۔ اور کچھ نا اور کچھ باقی رہنا۔ پس لکھی میں نے اس شرح میں متن کی عبارت اس طریقہ پر جو پختہ ہو چکا تھا میرے ہاں تا کہ تبدیل کر دے ان نسخوں کو جو لکھے ہوئے تھے اس تبدیلی سے پہلے اس طریق کی طرف ۔ پھر جب آسان ہوا اس کا پورا ہونا اور ٹوٹ گئی اس کے ختم ہونے کے ساتھ اس کی مہر جو مشتمل ہے ایسی تعریفات اور دلائل پر جن کی بنیاد رکھی گئی ہے علم منطق کے قواعد پر اور مشتمل ہے ایسی تفریحات پر جو مزین کی گئی ہیں اصول کے یاد کرنے کے بعد اور عمدہ ترتیب پر کہ نہیں سبقت لے گیا کوئی ایک مجھ پر ان کے مثل لانے کے ساتھ ۔ ساتھ باریک تدقیقات کے کہ نہیں پہنچا کوئی ایک اس علم کے شاہ سواروں میں سے اس مقصود تک ۔
تشریح: لغوی تحقیق:۔ ثانیا کے دو معنی آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ۔ دوسرا نمبر ۲۔ پھیرنے والا مصلیا کے بھی دو معنے آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ا۔ درود و سلام بھیجنے والا نمبر ۲۔ دوڑ کے میدان میں دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا۔ طلبہ دوڑ کے میدان کو کہتے ہیں ۔ جلیا دوڑ کے میدان میں پہلے نمبر پر آنے والا مصلیا دوڑ کے میدان میں دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا ۔ جد بالفتح کے دو معنی آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ا ۔ دادا نمبر ۲ - نصیبہ ۔ یہاں جد میں ایہام ہے۔
تعریف ایہام : ۔ ایہام کہتے ہیں کہ ذو معنیین لفظ استعمال کیا جائے ۔ کہ مخاطب اس لفظ کا قریبی معنی سمجھے اور متکلم بمعنی بعیدی معنی مراد ہے۔ سودت باب تفعیل کا صیغہ ہے۔ اس کا معنی ہوتا ہے کسی چیز کو مسودہ کی شکل دینا۔ انتساخ ایک نسخہ سے دوسرا نسخہ نقل کرنا۔ انتشر بمعنی پھیلنا اطراف طرف کی جمع ہے۔ بمعنی کنارہ لیکن یہاں مراد شہر ہیں ۔ الجو معنی من النمط بمعنی طریقہ فض بمعنی قض اس کا معنی ہے پردہ بکارت کو توڑنا۔ گویا مصنف نے اس سے اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے کہ جس طرح بکارة توڑنے سے پہلے وہ محل متصرف نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہ کتاب بھی پہلے کسی کے تصرف میں نہیں تھی کس نے اس کو دیکھا نہیں تھا۔ ختام اس مٹی کو کہتے ہیں جس سے مہر لگائی جاتی ہے۔ مرصعہ باب تفعیل سے بمعنی مزین کرنا ۔ انیق عمدہ فرسان فارس کی جمع ہے بمعنی شاہ سوار - الالہ بمعنی غایت اور مقصود ۔
قوله حامد الله : عبارت کے اس حصہ میں چار امور بیان ہو نگے امراول غرض ماتن ۔
ماتن کی غرض یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتاب کو تحمد اللہ اور تصلیہ علی النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے شروع کر رہے ہیں۔
امر ثانی ترکیبی تحقیق:۔ پہلا حمل بسم اللہ یہ جار محروم کر متعلق ہے متیمنا کے۔ جو کہ اسم فاعل ہے اور ابتدئی کی ان ضمیر سے حال ہے اور حامد ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے دوسرا حال ہے اور باقی جملوں کا عطف حامد اللہ پر ہے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ یہ حال ہے الرحیم کے مفعول سے اصل عبارت ہوگی الرحیم ایا کی حامد امعنی ہوگا شروع کرتا ہوں اللہ کے نام سے جو بڑا مہربان نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے خاص مجھ پر اس حال میں کہ میں حمد بیان کرنے والا ہوں۔ تیسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ حامد االرحیم کا مفعول
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, praising, sending blessings, seeking rain, translating, greeting, and sending blessings upon the most honorable of His messengers, Muhammad and his family. After praising Allah and sending blessings upon His messenger, indeed the servant seeking means to Allah through the firm rope, Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, may his grandfather be fortunate and his effort successful, says: When Allah enabled me to compose Tanqih al-Usul, I intended to write a commentary on its difficulties and open its locked points, turning away from explaining the places that whoever does not solve them without verbosity may not look into that book. And know that when I drafted the book al-Tanqih, some of the companions hastened to copy it and discuss it, and copies spread in some regions. Then after that, few changes and some erasures and additions occurred in it. So I wrote in this commentary the wording of the matn according to the pattern that was settled with me, so that the copies written before the changes would be changed to this pattern. Then when its completion was facilitated and its seal was broken with completion, containing definitions and proofs founded on the rules of logic, and well-arranged derivations after mastering the principles, and an elegant arrangement that no one preceded me in its like, along with subtle investigations that the knights of this science have not reached this extent.
Translation: I begin in a state of seeking blessing with the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. (And I begin) in a state of praising Allah firstly and secondly, and turning the reins of praise to Him. And upon the most excellent of His messengers, Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his family, I send blessings and peace, and I am the first and second in the field of sending blessings and peace. After praise and blessings, indeed the servant who holds fast to the means to Allah with the firm rope, Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, may his fortune be good and his effort successful, says: When Allah granted me success in writing Tanqih al-Usul, I intended to write a commentary on its difficulties and open its complicated topics, turning away from explaining those places that if someone cannot solve them without verbosity, it is not permissible for him to look in this (my) book. And know that when I wrote the book al-Tanqih, some companions hastened to copy it and discuss it, and copies spread in some cities. Then after that, few changes occurred in it, and some erasures and additions. So I wrote in this commentary the wording of the matn according to the pattern that was settled with me, so that the copies written before the changes would be changed to this pattern. Then when its completion was facilitated and the seal was broken with its completion, containing such definitions and proofs that are founded on the rules of logic, and such derivations that are adorned after memorizing the principles, and with an excellent arrangement that no one preceded me in producing its like, along with subtle investigations that none of the knights of this science have reached this goal.
Commentary: Lexical investigation: 'Thaniyan' has two meanings: 1. Second, 2. Turner. 'Musalliyan' also has two meanings: 1. One who sends blessings and peace, 2. One who comes second in the racecourse. 'Talabah' means racecourse. 'Jaliyan' means one who comes first in the racecourse. 'Musalliyan' means one who comes second. 'Jadd' with fatha has two meanings: 1. Grandfather, 2. Fortune. Here 'jadd' has an ambiguity (iham).
Definition of Iham: Iham is when a word with two meanings is used so that the listener understands the proximate meaning while the speaker intends the distant meaning. 'Sawwadtu' is a form of taf'il, meaning to give something the form of a draft. 'Intisakh' is copying from one copy to another. 'Intashara' means to spread. 'Atraf' is plural of taraf, meaning side, but here meaning cities. 'Al-namti' means method. 'Fadda' means to break, its meaning is to break the veil of virginity. As if the author indicated by this that just as before breaking the hymen, that place is not subject to disposal, similarly this book was not previously in anyone's disposal, no one had seen it. 'Khitam' refers to the clay used for sealing. 'Murassa'ah' from taf'il meaning adorned. 'Aniq' means excellent. 'Fursan' is plural of faris, meaning knight. 'Al-alah' means goal and purpose.
His saying 'Hamidallahi': In this part of the expression, four matters will be mentioned. The first matter: The purpose of the matn author. The matn author's purpose is that he begins his book with praising Allah and sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The second matter: Syntactic investigation. The first analysis: 'Bismillah' is a prepositional phrase related to 'mutayammanan', which is a participle and is a hal (circumstantial accusative) from the implied pronoun of 'abtadi', and 'hamid' is a second hal from the pronoun of 'ana', and the remaining sentences are conjoined to 'hamidallah'. The second probability: that it is a hal from the object of 'al-rahim', the original phrase would be 'al-rahim iyyaka hamid', meaning I begin with the name of Allah who is especially most gracious and merciful to me, in the state of my praising. The third probability: that 'hamid' is the object of 'al-rahim'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary (sharh) on his own work, Tanqih al-Usul. He begins with the basmala, hamd, and salawat, following the standard Islamic scholarly practice. He identifies himself as 'Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah' and explains his motive: having written Tanqih al-Usul, he realized the need to clarify its difficult points, especially since early copies were corrupted by unauthorized modifications. He therefore produced this commentary (Altarweeh) with a corrected version of the matn. He emphasizes that the work is founded on logical principles and contains deep investigations that previous scholars had not achieved. The Urdu commentary then provides lexical and grammatical analysis of the Arabic terms, including the dual meanings of 'musalliyan' (blessing vs. second in a race) and 'jadd' (grandfather vs. fortune), and defines the rhetorical device 'iham' (ambiguity). It also explains the author's usage of 'fadda' (breaking the seal) as a metaphor for unveiling the book. The passage sets the stage for the usul discussions to follow, highlighting the author's care in preserving textual accuracy and his high estimation of his own contribution.

Key Terms
إِيهام (īhām): Using a word with two meanings such that the listener understands the proximate meaning while the speaker intends the distant meaning.
ثَانِيًا (thāniyan): Has two meanings: 'second' (in order) and 'turner' (one who turns back). Here used in the hamd to indicate both meanings.
جَدّ (jadd): With fatha, has two meanings: 'grandfather' (jadd) and 'fortune' (jadd). Used in the author's lineage with iham.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What prompted the author to write this commentary (al-Tarweeh)?
A) He wanted to earn more fame.
B) He found errors and changes in the early copies of Tanqih al-Usul and wanted to correct them.
C) He was ordered by the caliph.
D) He wanted to refute the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
The author wrote al-Tarweeh to provide a corrected and clarified version of Tanqih al-Usul, emphasizing the importance of textual accuracy in usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Preface Analysis: Rhetorical Devices and Grammatical Investigation in Hanafi Usul
Commentator explains the preface and linguistic details of the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device 'iiham' and the explicit metaphor 'isti'ararah tasrihiyah' in the preface and explain how they clarify the author's intended meaning.

Core Idea
Iiham and isti'ararah tasrihiyah are analytical tools for resolving ambiguity in legal texts.

Commentaries on Hanafi usul works often begin with a detailed linguistic analysis of the author's words. This preface from 'Altarweeh' explains key terms and rhetorical devices used to ensure precise understanding. By examining the commentator's method, we learn how subtle ambiguities are identified and resolved before diving into substantive legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that this is the opening of a commentary (sharh) on 'Al-Tawdih', explaining the author's own preface. The commentator is setting the stage for the usul discussions to follow.
2
Define key rhetorical terms
Extract the definition of 'iiham' (ambiguity with two meanings, listener takes proximate, speaker intends remote) and 'isti'ararah tasrihiyah' (explicit metaphor where the likened object is mentioned but the comparison is intended).
These terms are from Arabic rhetoric (bayan) but are used in usul to analyze textual evidence.
3
Analyze the grammatical possibilities
The commentator offers multiple grammatical analyses of the opening sentence ('hamid Allah'), showing how different parsing leads to different interpretations. Note the depth of grammatical investigation typical in Hanafi usul.
This demonstrates that language precision is foundational to legal derivation.
4
Trace the metaphor
Examine the metaphor 'wa li'annani al-thana' ilayhi thaniyan' where praising is compared to a rein. The commentator identifies it as 'isti'ararah tasrihiyah' and explains how it allows directing praise as desired.
Metaphors are not merely decorative; they carry legal-hermeneutical weight.
5
Understand the author's purpose
The commentator explains the author's reason for writing: to clarify difficult passages in 'Tanqih'. This orients the reader to the book's intended use.
Preface always serves a pedagogical function in Hanafi works.

الترويج لحَلَ التَّوْضِيح والتنويج
جو پختہ ہو چکا تھا میرے ہاں تا کہ تبدیل کر دے ان نسخوں کو جو لکھے ہوئے تھے اس تبدیلی سے پہلے اس طریق کی طرف ۔ پھر جب آسان ہوا اس کا پورا ہونا اور ٹوٹ گئی اس کے ختم ہونے کے ساتھ اس کی مہر جو مشتمل ہے ایسی تعریفات اور دلائل پر جن کی بنیاد رکھی گئی ہے علم منطق کے قواعد پر اور مشتمل ہے ایسی تفریحات پر جو مزین کی گئی ہیں اصول کے یاد کرنے کے بعد اور عمدہ ترتیب پر کہ نہیں سبقت لے گیا کوئی ایک مجھ پر ان کے مثل لانے کے ساتھ ۔ ساتھ باریک تدقیقات کے کہ نہیں پہنچا کوئی ایک اس علم کے شاہ سواروں میں سے اس مقصود تک ۔ تشریح: لغوی تحقیق:۔ ثانیا کے دو معنی آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ۔ دوسرا نمبر ۲۔ پھیرنے والا مصلیا کے بھی دو معنے آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ا۔ درود و سلام بھیجنے والا نمبر ۲۔ دوڑ کے میدان میں دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا۔ طلبہ دوڑ کے میدان کو کہتے ہیں ۔ جلیا دوڑ کے میدان میں پہلے نمبر پر آنے والا مصلیا دوڑ کے میدان میں دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا ۔ جد بالفتح کے دو معنی آتے ہیں۔ نمبر ا ۔ دادا نمبر ۲ - نصیبہ ۔ یہاں جد میں ایہام ہے۔
تعریف ایہام : ۔ ایہام کہتے ہیں کہ ذو معنیین لفظ استعمال کیا جائے ۔ کہ مخاطب اس لفظ کا قریبی معنی سمجھے اور متکلم بمعنی بعیدی معنی مراد ہے۔ سودت باب تفعیل کا صیغہ ہے۔ اس کا معنی ہوتا ہے کسی چیز کو مسودہ کی شکل دینا۔ انتساخ ایک نسخہ سے دوسرا نسخہ نقل کرنا۔ انتشر بمعنی پھیلنا اطراف طرف کی جمع ہے۔ بمعنی کنارہ لیکن یہاں مراد شہر ہیں ۔ الجو معنی من النمط بمعنی طریقہ فض بمعنی قض اس کا معنی ہے پردہ بکارت کو توڑنا۔ گویا مصنف نے اس سے اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے کہ جس طرح بکارة توڑنے سے پہلے وہ محل متصرف نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہ کتاب بھی پہلے کسی کے تصرف میں نہیں تھی کس نے اس کو دیکھا نہیں تھا۔ ختام اس مٹی کو کہتے ہیں جس سے مہر لگائی جاتی ہے۔ مرصعہ باب تفعیل سے بمعنی مزین کرنا ۔ انیق عمدہ فرسان فارس کی جمع ہے بمعنی شاہ سوار - الالہ بمعنی غایت اور مقصود ۔
قوله حامد الله : عبارت کے اس حصہ میں چار امور بیان ہو نگے امراول غرض ماتن ۔
ماتن کی غرض یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتاب کو تحمد اللہ اور تصلیہ علی النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے شروع کر رہے ہیں۔
امر ثانی ترکیبی تحقیق:۔ پہلا حمل بسم اللہ یہ جار محروم کر متعلق ہے متیمنا کے۔ جو کہ اسم فاعل ہے اور ابتدئی کی ان ضمیر سے حال ہے اور حامد ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے دوسرا حال ہے اور باقی جملوں کا عطف حامد اللہ پر ہے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ یہ حال ہے الرحیم کے مفعول سے اصل عبارت ہوگی الرحیم ایا کی حامد امعنی ہوگا شروع کرتا ہوں اللہ کے نام سے جو بڑا مہربان نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے خاص مجھ پر اس حال میں کہ میں حمد بیان کرنے والا ہوں۔ تیسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ حامد االرحیم کا مفعول
ہوگا۔ معنی ہوگا جو نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے حامد للہ پر ۔ چوتھا احتمال یہ ہے کہ مفعول مقدم ہواللہ کے متعلق ( بالفتح) سے اصل
عبارت ہو گی انا كائن حامد الله -
امر ثالث مرادی تحقیق:۔ اول و ثانیا کی مراد میں چار احتمال ہیں۔
احتمال اول:۔ اول سے مراد جو کتاب کے شروع میں تعریف کی اورثانی سے مراد جو کتاب کے آخر میں تعریف کی۔ ر احتمال ثانی: اولا سے مراد وہ تعریف ہے جو نقیح میں کی اور ثانیا سے مراد وہ تعریف ہے جو تو ضیح میں کی ہے۔ احتمال ثالث: اولا سے مراد اول عمر کی تعریف اور ثانیا سے مراد آخر عمر کی تعریف ۔ احتمال رابع: اولا سے مراد اللہ تعالی کی تعریف کرتا ہوں اس کی تخلیق اولیٰ پر ۔ (ارواح کے پیدا کرنے پر ) او د ثانیا سے
مراد یہ ہے کہ اس کی تعریف کرتا ہوں تخلیق ثانوی پر ۔ (اجساد کے پیدا کرنے پر مزید احتمالات تلویح میں مذکور ہیں۔ امر رائع استعارات: ولعنان الثناء الیہ ثانیا۔ اسمیں بعض استعارے تو صاحب تلویح نے بیان کیے ہیں ۔ ان پر بحث و ہیں ہوگی۔ ان کے علاوہ ایک احتمال اور بھی ہے کہ یہاں استعارہ تصریحہ پایا جاتا ہے کہ ارادہ ثناء کو تشبیہ دی ہے۔ عنان کے ساتھ کہ جس طرح عنان اور لگام سے گھوڑے کو جس طرف چاہیں موڑ سکتے ہیں اسی طرح ثناء کے ارادہ کو جس ممدوح کی طرف چاہیں موڑ سکتے ہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ ذکر مشبہ بہ کا ہے مراد مشبہ ہے یہ استعارہ مصرحہ ہے۔
وجہ تصدیف توضیح
قولہ وبعد : قول ماتن و بعد ۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے وجہ تصنیف ذکر کی ہے کہ میں نے تنقیح کی شرح توضیح کیوں لکھی ہے؟ اس لیے کہ تنقیح کے بعض مقامات مشکل اور بعض مطالب الفاظ میں بند تھے اس لیے میں نے مشکل مقامات کی وضاحت
کر دی ہے۔ عبید اللہ : اس میں دو احتمال ہیں۔ (۱) یہ مرفوع ہو اس وقت یہ خبر ہوگی ھو مبتداء محذوف کی ۔ (۲) یہ منصوب ہو اس وقت یا تو اعنی فعل محذوف کا مفعول یہ ہوگا یا پھر العبد سے عطف بیان ہوگا۔
کیفیت مصنف
قولہ معرضا:۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے کیفیت مصنف کا تذکرہ کیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس کتاب میں مندرجہ
The book 'Altarweehurdusharhaltaozeehwattalweeh' begins. The author writes: 'That which had been firmly established with me, so that it changes the written copies before this change to that method. Then when its completion became easy and its seal was broken at its conclusion, which contains definitions and proofs founded upon the rules of logic, and contains branches adorned after memorizing the principles, in a beautiful order such that no one preceded me in bringing its like, along with subtle investigations which none of the knights of this science attained.' Explanation: Linguistic research: 'Thaniyan' has two meanings: 1. second number, 2. turner. 'Musalliyan' also has two meanings: 1. one who sends blessings and peace, 2. one who comes second in the racecourse. 'Tulbah' means racecourse. 'Jaliya' is the one who comes first in the racecourse, 'Musalliya' is the one who comes second. 'Jadd' (with fatha) has two meanings: 1. grandfather, 2. fortune. Here there is 'iiham' (ambiguity) in 'jadd'. Definition of 'iiham': It is using a word with two meanings such that the listener understands the proximate meaning while the speaker intends the distant meaning. 'Sawwada' is a form of taf'eel, meaning to make something into a draft. 'Intisakh' is copying from one copy to another. 'Intashara' means to spread. 'Atraf' is plural of 'taraf' meaning edge, but here it means cities. 'Al-jaw' meaning from 'al-namat' meaning method. 'Fadda' meaning 'qadda', it means to tear the hymen. As if the author indicated by this that just as the place is not used before breaking the hymen, similarly this book was not previously used by anyone, no one had seen it. 'Khitam' is the clay used for sealing. 'Murassa'ah' from taf'eel, meaning adorned. 'Aniq' means excellent. 'Fursan' is plural of 'Faris' meaning knight. 'Ilah' means goal and purpose. His saying: 'Hamid Allah': In this part of the expression, four matters will be explained: First: The goal of the author. The author's goal is that he begins his book with praising Allah and sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him). Second: Compositional analysis: First, 'bismillah' is a prepositional phrase related to 'mutayammanan' which is a participle, and it is in the accusative state as a hal (circumstantial) from the implied 'ana', and 'hamid' is a second hal from 'ana', and the remaining sentences are conjoined to 'hamid Allah'. Second possibility: it is a hal from the object of 'al-Rahim', the original phrase would be 'al-Rahim iyyaka hamid', meaning 'I begin with the name of Allah, who is most merciful, especially to me, while I am praising.' Third possibility: 'hamid' is the object of 'al-Rahim', the meaning would be 'Who is most merciful, praising Allah.' Fourth possibility: the object is fronted to 'hiya' related to 'Allah' (with fatha), the original phrase would be 'ana kainun hamid Allah'. Third: Research on intended meanings: Regarding 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan', there are four possibilities: First: 'awwalan' refers to the praise at the beginning of the book, and 'thaniyan' to the praise at the end. Second: 'awwalan' refers to the praise in 'Tanqih' and 'thaniyan' in 'Tawdih'. Third: 'awwalan' refers to praise in the first part of life, and 'thaniyan' in the latter part. Fourth: 'awwalan' means 'I praise Allah for His first creation (creation of souls)' and 'thaniyan' for His second creation (creation of bodies). More possibilities are mentioned in 'Talwih'. Fourth: Metaphors: 'Wa li'annani al-thana' ilayhi thaniyan'. Some metaphors have been explained by the author of 'Talwih', there will be discussion on them. Besides, there is another possibility that there is 'isti'ararah tasrihiyah' here, where intention of praise is compared to 'inan' (rein), just as a horse can be turned in any direction by the rein, similarly the intention of praise can be directed towards any praised one. In summary, the mention is of the likened object, the intended is the simile, and this is a literal metaphor. The reason for authoring 'Tawdih': His saying 'wa ba'd': In this expression, the author mentions the reason for authoring: 'Why did I write a commentary on 'Tawdih' for 'Tanqih'? Because some places in 'Tanqih' were difficult and some meanings were locked in words, so I clarified the difficult places.' 'Ubayd Allah': There are two possibilities: (1) It is nominative, then it would be the predicate of a deleted subject 'huwa'. (2) It is accusative, then it would be an object of a deleted verb 'a'ni' or an appositive of 'al-'abd'. The author's state: His saying 'mu'ridan': In this expression, the author mentions his state; the summary is that what is contained in this book.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary 'Altarweehurdusharhaltaozeehwattalweeh', where the commentator, likely Sadr al-Shariah or Taftazani, explains the preface of the matn (base text) 'Al-Tawdih'. The passage begins with a linguistic analysis of key terms used in the author's introduction, such as 'thaniyan' (second) and 'musalliyan' (one who sends blessings), showing multiple meanings to clarify potential ambiguities. The commentator then defines 'iiham' (ambiguity) as a rhetorical device where a word with two meanings is used, with the listener understanding the immediate meaning while the speaker intends the remote one. This is followed by explanations of words like 'sawwada' (to draft) and 'intisakh' (copying), linking them to the author's method. The central part of the passage examines the author's statement 'Hamid Allah' (praising Allah), breaking it into four aspects: the author's goal, compositional analysis, intended meanings, and metaphors. The composer's analysis offers multiple grammatical interpretations of how 'bismillah' and 'hamid' relate in the sentence, showing the depth of grammatical insight in Hanafi usul works. The intended meanings section proposes four interpretations of 'first' and 'second' in the praise, ranging from placement in the book to life stages and creation types. The passage then discusses the metaphor 'wa li'annani al-thana' ilayhi thaniyan', explaining it as an 'isti'ararah tasrihiyah' (explicit metaphor) where the intention of praise is compared to a rein, allowing the author to direct praise as desired. Finally, the reason for authoring the commentary is given: to clarify difficult passages in 'Tanqih'. This passage is typical of front matter in scholarly Hanafi works, setting the stage for the technical discussions to follow.

Key Terms
ايهام (Iiham): Using a word with two meanings such that the listener understands the proximate meaning while the speaker intends the distant meaning.
استعاره تصريحه (Isti'ararah Tasrihiyah): A metaphor where the word for the likened object is mentioned but the intended meaning is the object of comparison.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the definition of 'Iiham' (ايهام) as used in this preface?
A) Using a word with multiple meanings that are all intended simultaneously.
B) Using a word with two meanings, where the listener understands the immediate meaning but the speaker intends the remote meaning.
C) Using a word that is ambiguous and can be interpreted in any way.
D) Using a word in a metaphorical sense without a clear connection.

Key Takeaway
Preface analysis in Hanafi usul works is a rigorous exercise in linguistic precision, employing rhetorical concepts like iiham and isti'ararah tasrihiyah to clarify the author's intended meaning.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Author's Purpose and Characteristics of His Commentary
Author's preface: reasons and features

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's reasons for writing Tawdih and list the five distinguishing features of his commentary.

Core Idea
A commentary should clarify difficulties without redundancy, base proofs on logic, and offer novel arrangements.

This passage from the supercommentary Talwih explains why Sadr al-Sharia (or his commentator) wrote Tawdih al-Tanqih. He describes his method: he clarifies difficult passages, avoids over-explaining what is clear, ensures the matn text is error-free, bases definitions on logical principles, introduces unique arrangements, and includes subtle points. Understanding these features helps us appreciate the scholarly values of clarity, conciseness, logical rigor, and originality in Hanafi usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated reason for writing
The author says some passages of Tanqih were difficult and some meanings were bound in words, so he wrote the commentary to clarify those difficult passages.
2
List the five distinguishing features of the commentary
The text enumerates five matters: (1) avoiding explanation of already clear passages to prevent redundancy; (2) the matn text is error-free; (3) definitions and proofs are based on logical rules; (4) derivations and unique arrangements; (5) subtle points beyond ordinary scholars.
These features reflect the author's methodological priorities.
3
Distinguish between itnab and hashw
The author defines itnab as beneficial elaboration, while hashw (and tatwil) is useless verbosity. He emphasizes that his work avoids unnecessary length.
This rhetorical distinction is central to his approach.
4
Recognize the grammatical argument about deletion
The author argues that the relative clause after the mawsul was deleted because its substitute (man lam yahulluha) exists later, similar to the deletion of a conditional clause's result when the substitute is present.
This shows the author's engagement with Arabic grammar and rhetorical theory.
5
Understand the dedication to a patron
The author dedicates the work to a king of Islam, praising his jihad, pilgrimage, and revival of Hanafi customs. This indicates the work's context and intended audience.
Such dedications were common in classical scholarship.

قولہ وبعد : قول ماتن و بعد ۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے وجہ تصنیف ذکر کی ہے کہ میں نے تنقیح کی شرح توضیح کیوں لکھی ہے؟ اس لیے کہ تنقیح کے بعض مقامات مشکل اور بعض مطالب الفاظ میں بند تھے اس لیے میں نے مشکل مقامات کی وضاحت کر دی ہے۔ عبید اللہ : اس میں دو احتمال ہیں۔ (۱) یہ مرفوع ہو اس وقت یہ خبر ہوگی ھو مبتداء محذوف کی ۔ (۲) یہ منصوب ہو اس وقت یا تو اعنی فعل محذوف کا مفعول یہ ہوگا یا پھر العبد سے عطف بیان ہوگا۔
كیفیت مصنف: قولہ معرضا:۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے کیفیت مصنف کا تذکرہ کیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس کتاب میں مندرجہ ذیل امور پائے جاتے ہیں (۱) اس کتاب کے وہ مقامات جس کو حل کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کی شرح اطناب کے قبیل سے ہے میں نے ان مواضع کی شرح سے اعراض کیا ہے (۲) اس شرح میں متن کا جو نسخہ ہے وہ تمام غلطیوں سے مبراً ہے (۳) یہ کتاب ایسی تعریفات اور دلائل پر مشتمل ہے جن کی بنیاد منطقی قواعد پر رکھی گئی ہے (۴) اس کتاب میں تفریعات اور عمدہ عمدہ ترتیبات ذکر کی ہیں کہ میرے علاوہ کسی نے ایسی ترتیب قائم نہیں کی (۵) میں نے ایسے ایسے باریک نکات ذکر کیسے ہیں کہ وہاں تک کسی صاحب علم کی رسائی نہیں ہوئی ۔
فائدہ :۔ معرضا الخ معرضا یہ حال ہے اشرح کی انا ضمیر سے لم یجلہا یہ حل حلاً سے ہے ان کا معنی ہے گرہ کھولنا اطناب اس زیادتی کو کہتے ہیں جو کسی فائدہ پر مشتمل ہو اور حشو و تطویل اس زیادتی کو کہتے ہیں جو کسی فائدہ پر مشتمل نہ ہو تقدیر عبارت ہے عن شرح مواضع التي لا يحتاج في حلها الى الاطناب يشرحها من لم يحلها بغیر اطناب الخ معنی یہ ہے کہ ایسی جگہوں کی شرح کرنے سے میں نے اعراض کیا ہے جن کی شرح کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ وہ خود واضح ہیں بلکہ ان کی شرح طوالت کے سوا کچھ بھی نہیں ہے اور جو ایسی جگہوں کی شرح بغیر طوالت کے نہیں کرتے ان کو میری کتاب میں دیکھنا بھی حلال نہیں ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ لایحتاج الخ جوالتی کا صلہ ہے اس کو حذف کردیا کیونکہ اس کا بعد میں قائم مقام یعنی من لم يحلبا الخ موجود ہے اور یہ اس طرح ہے کہ جس طرح قائم مقام کی وجہ سے شرط کی جزا کو حذف کیا جاتا ہے كما قال الله تعالى اذا قيل لهم اتقوا ما بين ايديكم وما خلفكم لعلكم ترحمون تو یہ شرط ہے اور اس کی جزا محذوف ہے وہ ہے اعرضوا اور اس کو اسلئے حذف کیا گیا کیونکہ اس کا قائم مقام ہونے پر اگلی آیت کا نوا عنہا معرضین قرینہ ہے اس کی تائید علامہ زمخشری کے قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ کبھی کبھی اہل عرب اسم موصول کے بعد شعر صلہ یا کامل صلہ کو حذف کر دیتے ہیں اور تماما علی الذی احسن کی قراءت بھی اسی پر محمول ہے کہ یہاں شعر صلہ کو حذف کیا گیا اصل میں تھا علی الذی ہو احسن۔ وَجَعَلْتُهُ عُرَاضَةٌ بَلْ بِضَاعَةٌ مُزْجَاةً لِحَضْرَةِ مَنْ حُقَّ أَنْ يُو شَحَ بِذِكْرِهِ صُدُورَ الكُتُبِ وَالْاَسْفَارِ وَيُسْتَغَاتُ بِاسْمِهِ الْعَالِى فِي الْأَحْضَارِ وَالْاَسْفَارِ أَعْنِي حَضْرَتَ مَلِكِ مُلُوكِ الْإِسْلَامِ الْمُشَرَّفِ بِجِهَادٍ فِى سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَزِيَارَةِ بَيْتِهِ الْحَرَامِ الَّذِي تَضَعْضَعَ بِصَدْمَتِهِ مَبَانِى الْهِرْمَانِ وَاهْتَزَّ بِحُسْنِ شَعَائِرِهِ الْمَشَاعِرُ وَالْحَرَمَانِ رَافِعِ لِوَاءِ الشَّرِيعَةِ الْغَرَّاءِ مُحْيِ مَرَاسِمِ الْحَنِيفِيَّةِ النَّقِيَّةِ الْبَيْضَاءِ غَيَّاتِ الْحَقِّ وَالدِّينِ شَمْسِ الإِسْلامِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ الْمُوَّتِدَ بِالايْدِ الْمَتِيْنِ فِي إِعْلَاءِ كَلِمَةِ الدِّينِ الْمُبِينِ
His saying: 'After (وبعد)': the matn's saying 'wa ba'd'. In this expression, the author mentions the reason for writing: why did I write the commentary on Tanqih called Tawdih? Because some passages of Tanqih were difficult and some meanings were bound in words, so I clarified the difficult passages. 'Ubaydullah': there are two probabilities for it: (1) it is marfu' (nominative), then it would be the predicate of a deleted subject 'huwa'; (2) it is mansub (accusative), then either it is the object of a deleted verb 'a'ni' or it is an explanatory conjunction to 'al-'abd'. The condition of the author: his saying 'a'ridan' (turning away). In this expression, the author mentions the condition of the author. The summary is that this book contains the following matters: (1) those passages of this book which do not need solving but their explanation is of the type of redundancy, I have turned away from explaining them; (2) in this commentary, the text of the matn is free from all errors; (3) this book contains definitions and proofs based on logical principles; (4) I have mentioned derivations and excellent arrangements that no one besides me has established; (5) I have mentioned such subtle points that no scholar has reached there. Benefit: 'a'ridan' etc. 'a'ridan' is a state from 'ashrahu' with the pronoun 'ana'. 'lam yajulha' is from 'halla' meaning to untie a knot. 'itnab' is that excess which contains a benefit, and 'hashw wa tatwil' is that excess which contains no benefit. The estimated phrase is: 'عن شرح مواضع التي لا يحتاج في حلها الى الاطناب يشرحها من لم يحلها بغير اطناب الخ'. The meaning is: I have turned away from explaining those places which do not need explanation because they are clear, but their explanation is nothing but length. And whoever does not explain such places without length, it is not even permissible for them to look at my book. In summary, 'la yahtaju' etc. is the relative clause of the relative pronoun (al-mawsul). It has been deleted because later its substitute 'man lam yahulluha' etc. exists. And this is just as the conditional clause is deleted due to the presence of the substitute, as Allah said: 'when it is said to them: fear what is before you and what is behind you, so that you may receive mercy'. So this is the condition and its result is deleted, and it is 'they turn away'. And it was deleted because the next verse 'and they turn away from it' is evidence for the substitute. This is supported by the statement of Zamakhshari that sometimes Arabs delete the poetry or the full relative clause after the relative noun, and the recitation 'tamaman 'ala alladhi ahsana' is also interpreted as such: here the relative clause was deleted, originally it was 'allaahi huwa ahsana'. And I have made it a gift, rather a paltry commodity, for the presence of one who deserves that the opening pages of books and writings be adorned with his mention, and whose high name is sought for help in settled and traveling places, meaning the presence of the king of kings of Islam, honored with jihad in the path of Allah and with visiting His sacred House, whose impact shook the buildings of idolatry, and the ritual sites and the two sanctuaries trembled at the beauty of his rites, the raiser of the banner of the brilliant Sharia, reviver of the pure white Hanafi customs, the help of truth and religion, the sun of Islam and the Muslims, supported by the mighty hand in elevating the clear word of religion.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from the commentary expands on the author's preface. It begins by giving the reason for writing the book: to clarify difficult passages in Tanqih. Then it discusses the grammatical analysis of 'Ubaydullah'. Next, it lists five distinguishing features of the book: (1) the author avoided explaining already clear passages to avoid redundancy; (2) the matn text is error-free; (3) definitions and proofs are based on logic; (4) unique arrangements; (5) subtle points. Then a 'benefit' (fa'idah) explains the word 'a'ridan' and the concept of 'itnab' (beneficial elaboration) vs. 'hashw wa tatwil' (useless verbosity), and gives a grammatical argument for deletion of the relative clause. Finally, a dedication to a patron, describing him with grand titles. This section reveals the author's scholarly methodology: he values clarity, conciseness, logical consistency, and novelty.

Key Terms
اطناب (itnab): Elaboration that contains a benefit, as opposed to حشو (hashw) which is useless verbosity
تنقیح (Tanqih): The base text (matn) for which this commentary (Tawdih) and its supercommentary (Talwih) were written

Key Takeaway
The author's preface reveals five key characteristics of his commentary: clarity, textual accuracy, logical foundations, original arrangements, and subtle insights.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Iṭnāb and Ḥashw: The Hanafi Criteria for Prolixity in Legal Commentary
Author details his commentary's features and praises a ruler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between iṭnāb (beneficial prolixity) and ḥashw (useless filler) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and apply the author's criterion to evaluate a legal text.

Core Idea
Prolixity is permitted only if it serves a purpose; filler is rejected — Hanafi commentary is guided by utility.

In the preface to his commentary al-Tarwīḥ, the author lists five distinctive features of his work. Among them is his avoidance of unnecessary explanation, which he classifies as iṭnāb (beneficial prolixity) versus ḥashw (useless filler). He also emphasizes that his definitions and proofs are founded on logical principles (qawāʿid manṭiqiyya). These points are essential for understanding how Hanafi usul scholars approach the composition of legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the five features
Identify the numbered list in the passage. The author states five matters that characterize his book: (1) avoidance of explaining already clear passages, (2) error-free text of the matn, (3) definitions and proofs based on logical principles, (4) original arrangements and derivations, (5) inclusion of subtle points.
This is a standard way authors introduce their methodology.
2
Focus on feature 1 and the benefit
Read the author's statement: he avoided explaining places that do not need solving, because such explanation would be from the category of iṭnāb. He considers that unnecessary.
Iṭnāb here is used in a neutral sense – beneficial prolixity – but the author chooses to avoid it anyway.
3
Define iṭnāb and ḥashw from the fāʾida
The author provides a grammatical note where he explicitly defines iṭnāb as 'an increase that contains a benefit' and ḥashw as 'an increase that does not contain a benefit'. This is the core distinction.
Iṭnāb is permissible; ḥashw is blameworthy. The author applies this to determine which explanations to include.
4
Analyze the relative clause omission
The author discusses the grammatical justification for omitting the relative clause (ṣila) of 'allatī'. He compares it to the omission of the consequent of a condition, citing Quran 2:171 and Zamakhshari's opinion. This demonstrates his linguistic expertise and his view that such omission is an example of iṭnāb (beneficial conciseness).
This step is more advanced but shows how usul scholars blend grammar with fiqh.
5
Connect to logical foundations
Feature 3 says definitions and proofs are based on logical principles (qawāʿid manṭiqiyya). This reflects the Hanafi usul methodology that employs rational argumentation alongside textual evidence.
This is a hallmark of the Hanafi school in usul.

ذیل امور پائے جاتے ہیں (۱) اس کتاب کے وہ مقامات جس کو حل کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کی شرح اطناب کے قبیل سے ہے میں نے ان مواضع کی شرح سے اعراض کیا ہے (۲) اس شرح میں متن کا جو نسخہ ہے وہ تمام غلطیوں سے مبراً ہے (۳) یہ کتاب ایسی تعریفات اور دلائل پر مشتمل ہے جن کی بنیاد منطقی قواعد پر رکھی گئی ہے (۴) اس کتاب میں تفریعات اور عمدہ عمدہ ترتیبات ذکر کی ہیں کہ میرے علاوہ کسی نے ایسی ترتیب قائم نہیں کی (۵) میں نے ایسے ایسے باریک نکات ذکر کیسے ہیں کہ وہاں تک کسی صاحب علم کی رسائی نہیں ہوئی ۔

وَجَعَلْتُهُ عُرَاضَةٌ بَلْ بِضَاعَةٌ مُزْجَاةً لِحَضْرَةِ مَنْ حُقَّ أَنْ يُو شَحَ بِذِكْرِهِ صُدُورَ الكُتُبِ وَالْاَسْفَارِ وَيُسْتَغَاتُ بِاسْمِهِ الْعَالِى فِي الْأَحْضَارِ وَالْاَسْفَارِ أَعْنِي حَضْرَتَ مَلِكِ مُلُوكِ الْإِسْلَامِ الْمُشَرَّفِ بِجِهَادٍ فِى سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَزِيَارَةِ بَيْتِهِ الْحَرَامِ الَّذِي تَضَعْضَعَ بِصَدْمَتِهِ مَبَانِى الْهِرْمَانِ وَاهْتَزَّ بِحُسْنِ شَعَائِرِهِ الْمَشَاعِرُ وَالْحَرَمَانِ رَافِعِ لِوَاءِ الشَّرِيعَةِ الْغَرَّاءِ مُحْيِ مَرَاسِمِ الْحَنِيفِيَّةِ النَّقِيَّةِ الْبَيْضَاءِ غَيَّاتِ الْحَقِّ وَالدِّينِ شَمْسِ الإِسْلامِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ الْمُوَّتِدَ بِالايْدِ الْمَتِيْنِ فِي إِعْلَاءِ كَلِمَةِ الدِّينِ الْمُبِينِ

اَعَزَّ اللَّهُ الإِسْلامَ وَالْمُسْلِمِيْنَ بِدَوَامَ دَوْلَتِهِ وَبَقَائِهِ وَشَدَّ بِأَوْتَادِ الْخُلُودِ أَطْنَابَ عِزَّتِهِ وَإِعْلَائِه فَهُوَ الَّذِى قَامَ بِتَقْوِيَّةِ الدِينِ الْقَوِيمِ فِى زَمَانِ ضُعْفِهِ وَفُتُورِهِ وَاسْتَقَلَّ بِكَمَالِهِ بِرَفْعِ قُصُورِ الشَّرْعِ فِي أَوَانِ قُصُورِهِ وَأَوْقَدَ بَعْدَ الْعُمُودِ لِاشْتِعَالِ نُورِ الْحَقِّ نَارًا وَأَظْهَرَ بَعْدَ الإِنْمِحَاءِ فِى طَرِيقِ الدِّينِ الْقَوِيمِ سُلَّمًا وَ مَنَارًا وَاِخْتِصَاصُهُ بِهَذِهِ الكَرَامَاتِ الدِّينِيَّةِ اَوْجَبَنِي التَّوَجُهَ إِلى جَنَابِهِ وَتَزييُن دِيُبَاجَةِ هذَ الْكِتَابِ بِشَرَائِفِ. الْقَابِهِ فَإِنِّي بِمَعْزَلٍ عَنِ الْاِلْتِفَاتِ إِلَى أَبْنَاءِ الدُّنْيَا وَمُزَخْرَفَاتِهِمْ فَضْلًا أَنْ اَذْكُرَ فِي كُتُبِ الشَّرِيعَةِ شَيْئًا مِنْ أَسْمَائِهِمْ وَصِفَاتِهِمُ سَمَّيتُ هَذَا الكِتَابَ بِالتَّوضِيح فى حَلْ غَوَامِضِ التَّنقِيح وَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَسئُولٌ أَن يَعْصِمَ عَن الخَطَأُ وَالخَلَلِ كَلَامَنَا وَعَن السَّهِوِ وَالزَّلَلِ أَقَلمَنَا وَأَقدَامَنَا .
ترجمہ :۔ اور بنایا میں نے اس کتاب کو تحفہ بلکہ ناقص پونجی اس شخص کے دربار میں جو مستحق ہے اس بات کا کہ مزین کیا جائے اس کے ذکر کے ساتھ چھوٹی سمتابوں کے اوائل کو اور بڑی بڑی کتابوں کے مقدموں کو اور مدد طلب کی جائے اس کے بلند نام کے ساتھ وطنوں میں اور سفروں میں ۔ مراد لیتا ہوں میں اسلام کے بادشاہوں کے بادشاہ کے دربار کو جو مشرف ہے جہادفی سبیل اللہ کے ساتھ ۔ اور اللہ کے با قدمت گھروں کی زیارت کے ساتھ ایسا بادشاہ کہ کمزور ہو گئیں اس کے ٹکرانے سے عقل کی بنیاد میں اور خوش ہو گئے اس کے حسن اخلاق کی وجہ سے اسلامی شعائر اور حرمین شریفین ۔ اور بلند کرنے والا ہے۔ روشن شریعت کے جھنڈے کو اور زندہ کرنے والا ہے سفید خالص ملت کے نشانات کو ۔ اور مددگار ہے حق اور دین کا ، اسلام اور مسلمانوں کا سورج ہے جو تائید کیا گیا ہے مضبوط تائید کے ساتھ ۔ واضح دین کے کلمہ کو بلند کرنے میں ۔ عزت دے اللہ تعالی اسلام اور مسلمانوں کو اس کی بادشاہت کی ہمیشگی کے ساتھ اور اس کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ اور باندھ دے اللہ تعالیٰ ہمیشگی کی میخوں کے ساتھ اس کی عزت اور بلندیوں کی رسیوں کو۔ پس وہ بادشاہ وہ شخص ہے جو کھڑا ہو گیا سید ھے دین کو مضبوط کرنے کے لیے اس کی سستی اور کمزوری کے زمانہ میں اور قائم ہو گیا اپنے کمالات کی وجہ سے شریعت کے محلات کو بلند کرنے کے ساتھ اس کی کوتاہی ہو کے زمانہ میں اور جلا دی سمجھنے کے بعد نور حق کو روشن کرنے کے لیے آگ اور ظاہر کر دیا مٹنے کے بعد سید ھے دین کے راستے میں سیڑھی اور منارے کو ۔ بوجہ خاص ہونے اس بادشاہ کے ان دینی کرامات کے ساتھ ، مجھ پر ضروری کر دیا حضرت کی بارگاہ کی
Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ. From this point [the author lists five matters]: (1) The places in this book that do not need solving, rather their explanation is of the category of prolixity, I have avoided explaining those places. (2) The text of the matn in this commentary is free from all errors. (3) This book consists of definitions and proofs that are founded upon logical principles. (4) In this book I have mentioned derivations and excellent arrangements that no one besides me has established. (5) I have mentioned such subtle points that no scholar has reached there. Benefit: 'muʿriḍan' etc. 'muʿriḍan' is a circumstantial accusative from the pronoun 'anā' of 'ashraḥ'. 'lam yaḥullahā' – 'ḥall' from 'ḥallan', meaning untying a knot. 'Iṭnāb' refers to an increase that contains a benefit, whereas 'ḥashw' and 'ṭaṭwīl' refer to an increase that does not contain a benefit. The implied phrase is 'ʿan sharḥ mawāḍiʿ allatī lā yaḥtāju fī ḥallihā ilā al-iṭnāb yashraḥuhā man lam yaḥullahā bi-ghayr iṭnāb'. The meaning is that I have avoided explaining places whose explanation is not needed because they are clear, rather their explanation is nothing but length. And whoever does not explain such places without prolixity, it is not permissible for him to look at my book. The summary is that 'lā yaḥtāj' etc. is the relative clause of 'allatī'; it has been omitted because later there is its substitute, namely 'man lam yaḥullahā' etc. This is like when the consequence of a condition is omitted due to the substitute, as Allah said: 'When it is said to them: Fear what is before you and what is behind you, that you may receive mercy.' That is the condition and its consequence is omitted, which is 'aʿraḍū'. It was omitted because the substitute is the previous verse's 'nawā ʿanhā muʿriḍīn'. This is supported by the statement of Zamakhshari that sometimes the Arabs omit the relative clause or part of it after a relative pronoun, and the reading of 'tamāman ʿalā alladhī aḥsana' is also interpreted similarly: here the relative clause is omitted, originally it was 'ʿalā alladhī huwa aḥsana'. And I have made it a gift, rather a paltry commodity, for the presence of one who deserves that his mention adorn the beginnings of books and travels, and that his lofty name be sought for help in cities and journeys. I mean the presence of the king of kings of Islam, honored by jihad in the way of Allah and visiting His sacred House, who weakened by his impact the structures of heretical dualism, and by the beauty of his rites the holy sites and the two sanctuaries vibrated. He raises the banner of the radiant Sharia, revives the rites of the pure white Hanafi religion, the helper of truth and religion, the sun of Islam and the Muslims, who is confirmed by the strong hand in elevating the word of the clear religion. May Allah honor Islam and the Muslims with the continuity of his state and his permanence, and strengthen with the pegs of eternity the ropes of his honor and exaltation. For he is the one who rose to strengthen the upright religion at a time of its weakness and lethargy, and stood independently with his perfection in raising the deficiencies of the Sharia at the time of its shortcomings, and after darkness he kindled a fire for the burning of the light of truth, and after destruction he manifested a ladder and a beacon on the path of the upright religion. His special distinction with these religious graces necessitated my turning to his court and adorning the preface of this book with his noble titles. For I am free from paying attention to the people of the world and their ornamentations, let alone mentioning any of their names and attributes in books of Sharia. I have named this book 'al-Tawḍīḥ fī Ḥall Gḥawāmiḍ al-Tanqīḥ'. Allah is asked to protect our speech from error and fault, and our pens and steps from forgetfulness and slip. Translation: And I have made this book a gift, rather a paltry commodity, for the presence of one who deserves that his mention adorn the beginnings of small books and the prefaces of great books, and that his lofty name be sought for help in homelands and travels. I mean the presence of the king of kings of Islam, who is honored by jihad in the way of Allah and visiting His sacred houses, such a king that the foundations of reason became weak by his impact, and the Islamic rites and the two sanctuaries were delighted by his good character. And he is the raiser of the banner of the radiant Sharia, and the reviver of the signs of the white pure religion. And he is the helper of truth and religion, the sun of Islam and the Muslims, who is supported with strong support in elevating the word of the clear religion. May Allah honor Islam and the Muslims with the continuity of his state and his permanence, and may Allah strengthen the ropes of his honor and exaltation with the pegs of eternity. So that king is the person who stood to strengthen the straight religion in the time of its weakness and lethargy, and stood independently by his perfection in elevating the deficiencies of the Sharia in the time of its shortcomings, and lit a fire after darkness to brighten the light of truth, and displayed after destruction a ladder and a beacon in the path of the straight religion. Because of that king's special distinction with these religious graces, it became necessary for me to [turn to] the court of the presence.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This is the preface (front matter) of the book 'Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ'. The author opens by listing five distinctive features of his work. First, he deliberately avoided explaining passages that are already clear, as such explanation would be mere prolixity (iṭnāb). Second, he asserts that the text of the matn in his commentary is free from errors. Third, his definitions and proofs are grounded in logical principles, reflecting the Hanafi usul methodology that employs rational argumentation. Fourth, he claims originality in the arrangement and classification of topics, including beneficial derivations (tafrīʿāt). Fifth, he includes subtle points that no other scholar has reached. Then, under 'Fāʾida', he provides a grammatical explanation of the word 'muʿriḍan' and discusses the concepts of iṭnāb (beneficial prolixity) versus ḥashw (useless filler). He analyzes the implied relative clause structure, citing Quranic usage and the opinion of Zamakhshari to justify his omission. Following this, the author offers a lengthy and ornate praise of a ruler—likely his patron—highlighting his jihad, pilgrimage, support for the Hanafi school, and his role in strengthening Islam. This dedication is customary in classical works. The author explains that he named his book 'al-Tawḍīḥ fī Ḥall Gḥawāmiḍ al-Tanqīḥ', indicating it is a commentary that solves the difficulties of the original matn 'al-Tanqīḥ'. He concludes with a prayer for divine protection from error.

Key Terms
إطناب (iṭnāb): An increase in speech that contains a beneficial meaning; permissible prolixity.
حشو (ḥashw): An increase in speech that contains no benefit; useless filler.
موصل (mawṣūl): Relative pronoun; in this passage, 'allatī' and 'man'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the difference between iṭnāb and ḥashw?
A) Iṭnāb is permissible while ḥashw is forbidden in all cases.
B) Iṭnāb is an increase containing benefit; ḥashw is an increase without benefit.
C) Iṭnāb refers to omitted relative clauses; ḥashw refers to explicit explanations.
D) Iṭnāb is used only in logical definitions; ḥashw in legal rulings.

Key Takeaway
The author's preface establishes a key Hanafi usul principle: speech in legal commentary must be purposeful; only beneficial prolixity (iṭnāb) is allowed, while useless filler (ḥashw) is rejected.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Author's Preface: Purpose and Structure
Author praises the ruler and explains his purpose for writing the commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three-part structure of a Hanafi usul preface and explain the author's dual purpose: praise of a righteous ruler and clarification of his own scholarly integrity.

Core Idea
A Hanafi usul preface honours a righteous ruler for his religious support, while the author distances himself from worldly motives.

This lesson introduces Sadr al-Shariah's preface to al-Tawdih, his commentary on al-Tanqih. We will see how classical Hanafi scholars often began their works with praise of a pious patron, but also took care to assert their independence from worldly scholars. By parsing the passage's structure—Arabic matn, Urdu translation, and tashrih commentary—you will learn how to approach similar front matter in other Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-part structure
Recognize that the passage consists of: (1) the Arabic preface praising the ruler and stating the book's name, (2) an Urdu translation expanding on that praise, and (3) a commentary (tashrih) that breaks down lexical items and the author's intention.
This threefold structure is common in later Indian subcontinent prints of classical texts.
2
Parse the Arabic for key themes
In the Arabic section, look for three elements: praise of the ruler's religious contributions, the book's title 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih', and the author's declaration of being aloof from worldly scholars.
The Arabic is ornate and uses a series of relative clauses describing the ruler.
3
Analyze the author's justification
The author states that the ruler's 'religious graces' (karamat diniyyah) made it necessary to mention him. He then explicitly distances himself from worldly people, stressing that he does not seek their favour.
This is a standard trope in Islamic prefaces to assert scholarly independence.
4
Link the preface to the work's purpose
The book's title 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih' means 'The Clarification on Unraveling the Nuances of al-Tanqih'. The preface sets the tone for a work that aims to clarify obscure points of Hanafi usul.
Al-Tanqih is the author's own base text—a common practice for scholars to write a commentary on their own work.

اَعَزَّ اللَّهُ الإِسْلامَ وَالْمُسْلِمِيْنَ بِدَوَامَ دَوْلَتِهِ وَبَقَائِهِ وَشَدَّ بِأَوْتَادِ الْخُلُودِ أَطْنَابَ عِزَّتِهِ وَإِعْلَائِه فَهُوَ الَّذِى قَامَ بِتَقْوِيَّةِ الدِينِ الْقَوِيمِ فِى زَمَانِ ضُعْفِهِ وَفُتُورِهِ وَاسْتَقَلَّ بِكَمَالِهِ بِرَفْعِ قُصُورِ الشَّرْعِ فِي أَوَانِ قُصُورِهِ وَأَوْقَدَ بَعْدَ الْعُمُودِ لِاشْتِعَالِ نُورِ الْحَقِّ نَارًا وَأَظْهَرَ بَعْدَ الإِنْمِحَاءِ فِى طَرِيقِ الدِّينِ الْقَوِيمِ سُلَّمًا وَ مَنَارًا وَاِخْتِصَاصُهُ بِهَذِهِ الكَرَامَاتِ الدِّينِيَّةِ اَوْجَبَنِي التَّوَجُهَ إِلى جَنَابِهِ وَتَزييُن دِيُبَاجَةِ هذَ الْكِتَابِ بِشَرَائِفِ. الْقَابِهِ فَإِنِّي بِمَعْزَلٍ عَنِ الْاِلْتِفَاتِ إِلَى أَبْنَاءِ الدُّنْيَا وَمُزَخْرَفَاتِهِمْ فَضْلًا أَنْ اَذْكُرَ فِي كُتُبِ الشَّرِيعَةِ شَيْئًا مِنْ أَسْمَائِهِمْ وَصِفَاتِهِمُ سَمَّيتُ هَذَا الكِتَابَ بِالتَّوضِيح فى حَلْ غَوَامِضِ التَّنقِيح وَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَسئُولٌ أَن يَعْصِمَ عَن الخَطَأُ وَالخَلَلِ كَلَامَنَا وَعَن السَّهِوِ وَالزَّلَلِ أَقَلَامَنَا وَأَقدَامَنَا . ترجمہ :۔ اور بنایا میں نے اس کتاب کو تحفہ بلکہ ناقص پونجی اس شخص کے دربار میں جو مستحق ہے اس بات کا کہ مزین کیا جائے اس کے ذکر کے ساتھ چھوٹی سمتابوں کے اوائل کو اور بڑی بڑی کتابوں کے مقدموں کو اور مدد طلب کی جائے اس کے بلند نام کے ساتھ وطنوں میں اور سفروں میں ۔ مراد لیتا ہوں میں اسلام کے بادشاہوں کے بادشاہ کے دربار کو جو مشرف ہے جہادفی سبیل اللہ کے ساتھ ۔ اور اللہ کے با قدمت گھروں کی زیارت کے ساتھ ایسا بادشاہ کہ کمزور ہو گئیں اس کے ٹکرانے سے عقل کی بنیاد میں اور خوش ہو گئے اس کے حسن اخلاق کی وجہ سے اسلامی شعائر اور حرمین شریفین ۔ اور بلند کرنے والا ہے۔ روشن شریعت کے جھنڈے کو اور زندہ کرنے والا ہے سفید خالص ملت کے نشانات کو ۔ اور مددگار ہے حق اور دین کا ، اسلام اور مسلمانوں کا سورج ہے جو تائید کیا گیا ہے مضبوط تائید کے ساتھ ۔ واضح دین کے کلمہ کو بلند کرنے میں ۔ عزت دے اللہ تعالی اسلام اور مسلمانوں کو اس کی بادشاہت کی ہمیشگی کے ساتھ اور اس کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ اور باندھ دے اللہ تعالیٰ ہمیشگی کی میخوں کے ساتھ اس کی عزت اور بلندیوں کی رسیوں کو۔ پس وہ بادشاہ وہ شخص ہے جو کھڑا ہو گیا سید ھے دین کو مضبوط کرنے کے لیے اس کی سستی اور کمزوری کے زمانہ میں اور قائم ہو گیا اپنے کمالات کی وجہ سے شریعت کے محلات کو بلند کرنے کے ساتھ اس کی کوتاہی ہو کے زمانہ میں اور جلا دی سمجھنے کے بعد نور حق کو روشن کرنے کے لیے آگ اور ظاہر کر دیا مٹنے کے بعد سید ھے دین کے راستے میں سیڑھی اور منارے کو ۔ بوجہ خاص ہونے اس بادشاہ کے ان دینی کرامات کے ساتھ ، مجھ پر ضروری کر دیا حضرت کی بارگاہ کی طرف توجہ کرنے کو ، اور اس کتاب کے دیباچہ کو اس کے اچھے اچھے القابات کے ساتھ مزین کرنے کو۔ پس تحقیق میں دور ہوں دنیا داروں کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے اور ان کی رنگینیوں کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے چہ جائیکہ میں ذکر کروں شریعت کی کتابوں میں ان کے ناموں اور ان کی صفات کو اور نام رکھا میں نے اس کتاب کا، توضیح فی حل غوامض التنقیح ،، کے ساتھ اور اللہ تعالٰی سے سوال ہے کہ بچائے غلطی اور خلل سے ہماری کلام کو اور بھولنے اور پھسلنے سے ہماری فلموں اور قدموں کو ۔ تشریح:۔ اس عبارت کے تین حصے ہیں ۔ حصہ اول شروع سے لے کر واختصاصہ تک ہے۔ حصہ ثانی اختصاصہ سے سمہ تک ہے ۔ اور حصہ ثالث سمیت سے لے کر آخر تک ہے۔ حصہ اول کی تشریخ میں دو امر بیان ہوں گے ۔ نمبر الغوی تحقیق۔ نمبر ۲۔ غرض ماتن ۔ اور حصہ ثانی و ثالث میں صرف غرض ماتن بیان ہوگی۔ حصہ اول امراول لغوی تحقیق: عراضه بضم العین تحفہ، بضاعہ پونچی مزجاة ناقص یا کھوٹا ، اسفار بڑی کتا ہیں ،احضار حضر کی جمع ہے بمعنی وطن الاسفار سفر کی جمع ہے۔ تضعضع کمزور ہونا، مبانی بنیادیں، پھر مان عقل ، اهتز خوش ہونا بلواء جھنڈا ، مراسم نشانات، الخلیفیه، ملت، النقيه خالص، بيضاء، سفید، اوتاد جمع و تد بمعنی میخ ، اطناب جمع طنب بمعنی رسی ،فتو رستی ، قصور جمع قصر بمعنی محل یا پھر یہ مفرد ہے بمعنی کوتا ہی۔ پہلا قصور جمع اور دوسرا مفرد ہے۔ الحمود بجھنا، سلما سیڑھی ، منارا مینارہ قدیم زمانہ میں راستہ بتانے کے لئے کسی اونچی جگہ آگ جلائی جاتی تھی اس جگہ کو مینارہ کہتے ہیں۔ امر ثانی شاہ وقت کی تعریف اور اس سے اعتذار غرض ماتن:۔ اس عبارت میں ماتن نے شاہ وقت کی تعریف کی ہے۔ اس بادشاہ سے مراد غیاث الدین بن شمس الدین ہے جو 715ھ میں بادشاہ بنا جس نے شریعت کی ترویج اور خیر کے کاموں میں اور علماء کے احترام میں کوئی دقیقہ فروگزاشت نہ کیا جہاد بالنفس اور جہاد بالکفار دونوں پر خصوصی توجہ دی۔ 721ھ میں حج کیا اور 729ھ میں وفات پائی۔ حصہ ثانی سے غرض ماتن: واختصاصہ تا سمیت ۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے معذرت کی ہے کہ کسی کے ذہن میں یہ بات نہ آئے کہ میں عام درباری مولویوں کی طرح بادشاہ کے دربار میں کتابیں لے گیا اور اس غرض سے اس کی تعریف کی ہے ایسی بات ہر گز نہیں ہے، میں تو دنیا داروں سے دور بھاگتا ہوں لیکن بادشاہ کی دینی کرامات کی وجہ سے کتاب کے شروع میں ان کے کچھ اوصاف ذکر کر دیے ہیں۔ تا کہ برکت حاصل ہو جائے۔
May Allah honor Islam and Muslims with the perpetuity of his state and its endurance, and strengthen with the pegs of eternity the ropes of his glory and exaltation. For he is the one who stood to strengthen the upright religion in the time of its weakness and languor, and undertook with his perfection to elevate the deficiencies of the Shariah in the time of its shortcoming, and kindled after the extinguishing a fire for the ignition of the light of truth, and manifested after the effacement in the path of the upright religion a ladder and a minaret. And his distinction with these religious graces necessitated my turning to his presence and adorning the frontispiece of this book with the noble epithets of his titles. For I am aloof from paying attention to the worldly people and their embellishments, let alone that I mention in the books of the Shariah anything of their names and attributes. I named this book "al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih". And Allah the Exalted is asked to protect our speech from error and flaw, and our pens and steps from forgetfulness and slip.
Translation (Urdu): And I made this book a gift, rather a deficient investment, to the court of that person who is deserving that the beginnings of small books and the prefaces of large books be adorned with his mention, and help be sought through his lofty name in homelands and journeys. I intend the court of the king of kings of Islam, who is honored with jihad in the path of Allah and with visitation of the ancient houses of Allah. Such a king that the foundations of intelligence were weakened by his collision, and the Islamic symbols and the Two Holy Sanctuaries became delighted due to his good character. And he is the raiser of the banner of the bright Shariah and the reviver of the white pure signs of the nation. And he is the helper of truth and religion, the sun of Islam and Muslims, supported with strong support, in raising the word of the clear religion. May Allah honor Islam and Muslims with the perpetuity of his state and its endurance, and may Allah bind with the pegs of eternity the ropes of his glory and exaltation. So that king is the one who stood to strengthen the straight religion in the time of its weakness and languor, and rose with his perfection to elevate the defects of the Shariah in the time of its shortcoming, and kindled a fire after sleeping for the ignition of the light of truth, and manifested a ladder and a minaret after effacement in the path of the straight religion. Due to this king being distinguished with these religious graces, it made necessary for me to turn towards his majesty and to adorn the preface of this book with his noble titles. So indeed I am far from turning towards worldly people and their embellishments, much less that I mention in the books of the Shariah their names and attributes. And I named this book "al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih", and from Allah the Exalted is the request that He protect our speech from error and flaw, and our pens and steps from forgetfulness and slip.
Commentary: This expression has three parts. Part one: from the beginning to 'wa-ikhsisasuhu'. Part two: from 'ikhsisasuhu' to 'sammaytuhu'. Part three: from 'sammaytuhu' to the end. In the commentary of part one, two matters will be explained: first, lexical investigation; second, the author's purpose. In parts two and three, only the author's purpose will be explained. Part one, first matter, lexical investigation: 'arada' (with dammah on 'ayn) means gift; 'bida'ah' means merchandise; 'muzjat' means deficient or bad; 'asfar' means large books; 'ahdar' is plural of 'hadar' meaning homeland; 'asfar' is plural of 'safar'; 'tada'da'a' means to become weak; 'mabani' means foundations; 'thumma man' means intellect; 'ihtazza' means to become delighted; 'bi-liwa' means banner; 'marasim' means signs; 'al-khalifah' means nation; 'al-naqiyyah' means pure; 'bayda' means white; 'awtad' is plural of 'watad' meaning peg; 'atnab' is plural of 'tunub' meaning rope; 'futur' means languor; 'qusur' (first) is plural of 'qasr' meaning palace, or it is singular meaning deficiency; the first 'qusur' is plural and the second is singular; 'al-humud' means extinguishing; 'sullam' means ladder; 'manarah' means minaret—in ancient times, fire was lit in a high place to show the way, that place was called a minaret. Second matter: praise of the king of the time and apology from him. Author's purpose: In this expression, the author praises the king of the time. This king refers to Ghiyath al-Din bin Shams al-Din, who became king in 715 AH. He left no stone unturned in the promotion of the Shariah, good works, and respect for scholars. He gave special attention to both jihad with the soul and jihad against the disbelievers. He performed Hajj in 721 AH and died in 729 AH. Author's purpose from part two: from 'ikhsisasuhu' to 'sammaytuhu'. In this expression, the author apologizes that no one should think that like common court scholars, I brought books to the king's court and praised him for that purpose. That is never the case; I rather flee from worldly people, but due to the king's religious graces, I mentioned some of his attributes at the beginning of the book so that blessing may be obtained.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (dibajah) to his commentary al-Tawdih. It consists of three parts: first, the Arabic matn praising the ruler and explaining the book's name; second, an Urdu translation of that Arabic; third, a detailed commentary (tashrih) breaking down the text lexically and contextually. The author, Sadr al-Shariah (presumably, though not named here), dedicates the work to Sultan Ghiyath al-Din bin Shams al-Din, whom he credits with reviving Islam and the Shariah during a time of weakness. He clarifies that he only praised the ruler because of his religious merits, not for worldly gain. The book's title is 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih', meaning 'The Clarification on Unraveling the Nuances of al-Tanqih'. The commentary explains key Arabic terms like 'aradah' (gift), 'bida'ah' (merchandise), and others, and identifies the ruler as Ghiyath al-Din (r. 715–729 AH). The author apologizes for possibly being seen as a court sycophant, asserting his independence from worldly scholars.

Key Terms
التَّوْضِيح (al-Tawdih): The name of the present commentary, meaning 'The Clarification', written by Sadr al-Shariah to explain al-Tanqih.
التَّنقِيح (al-Tanqih): The base text (matn) on which this commentary is written; a work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh by the same author? Actually, al-Tanqih is by Sadr al-Shariah himself.
غوامض (ghawamid): Nuances or obscure points; the author claims to unravel the 'ghawamid' of al-Tanqih.

Introduction and Front Matter

Resolving Redundancy in Book Titles: A Usul Exercise
Analyzing the author's book title and its logical justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul techniques to distinguish absolute and restricted clarifications and identify different types of ambiguity in scholarly texts.

Core Idea
The title 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih' is not redundant: each term removes a different kind of ambiguity.

Commentators often face questions about the logical consistency of terms in a book title. In this lesson, we analyze the author's naming of his work and the Hanafi response to an apparent circularity. This trains you to see how usul al-fiqh sharpens conceptual precision even in front matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Circularity
The title uses two words meaning 'clarification' – 'Tawdih' and 'Hall' – leading to the charge of 'container containing itself' (ظرفیت الشی فی نفسہ). Recognize this as a potential logical flaw.
2
Examine the First Answer: Absolute vs Restricted Clarification
'Hall' denotes absolute clarification, while 'Tawdih' denotes extra or restricted clarification. Understand that the absolute can serve as a container for the restricted, avoiding circularity.
This distinction mirrors Hanafi usul's treatment of mutlaq and muqayyad.
3
Examine the Second Answer: Different Types of Ambiguity
'Tawdih' clarifies ambiguity in individual words (مفردات), while 'Hall' clarifies ambiguity in composition (ترکیب). They operate on different domains of the text.
This reflects the Hanafi attention to lexical vs. syntactic ambiguity.
4
Apply: Recognizing Non-Redundant Terminology
In Hanafi usul, definitions must be precise and operate at different levels; overlapping terms are allowed if they serve distinct functions. The title is logically sound.
This principle is used when analyzing ahadith or fiqh works with multiple terms.
5
Conclusion: Scholarly Care in Terminology
The author's choice showcases the importance of precise language in Islamic scholarship, a core value in usul al-fiqh.

کروں شریعت کی کتابوں میں ان کے ناموں اور ان کی صفات کو اور نام رکھا میں نے اس کتاب کا، توضیح فی حل غوامض التنقیح ،، کے ساتھ اور اللہ تعالٰی سے سوال ہے کہ بچائے غلطی اور خلل سے ہماری کلام کو اور بھولنے مراد مطلق ایضاح ہے اور توضیح سے مراد زیادتی ایضاح ہے۔ گویا توضیح مقدید بالایضاح ہے اور حل مطلق ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں مطلق مقید کے لیے ظرف بن رہا ہے۔ جو اس مقید اور غیر مقید کو اپنے میں لیے ہوئے ہے تو ہے اور حل سے مراد دوسری قسم کے خفاء کو دور کرنا ہے لہذا ظرفیتہ الشی فی نفسہ کی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی ۔
The author says: I turn to praise the king and adorn the preface of this book with his beautiful titles. Indeed, I am far from turning towards worldly people and their attractions, how much more so from mentioning their names and attributes in books of Shariah. And I named this book 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih'. I ask Allah to protect my speech from error and mistake, and my pen and steps from forgetfulness and slip. Commentary: This statement has three parts. Part one from beginning to 'wa-ikhsisahu', part two from 'ikhsisahu' to 'samahu', and part three from 'samaytuhu' to end. In part one, two matters are explained: lexical research and the author's intent. In parts two and three, only the author's intent. Lexical research: ... Second matter: praise of the king and apology. The author praises Shah Waqt, meaning Ghiyath al-Din ibn Shams al-Din who became king in 715 AH, promoted Shariah, supported good deeds, honored scholars, focused on jihad, performed Hajj in 721 AH, and died in 729 AH. Part two: The author apologizes, saying do not think I brought the book to the king's court like common court scribes; I flee from worldly people, but I mentioned his attributes due to his religious merits for blessing. Part three: The author names the book 'Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih' and prays to avoid mistakes. Question: 'Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih' means clarification, and 'al-Tawdih' also means clarification, which would entail the container containing itself (circularity). Answer (1): 'Hall' means absolute clarification, and 'Tawdih' means extra clarification, so the absolute serves as container for the restricted, thus no circularity. Answer (2): Ambiguity can be in individual words or in composition; 'Tawdih' removes the first type, 'Hall' removes the second, so no circularity.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is the Urdu commentary (sharh) on the author's introduction. The commentator divides the author's opening statement into three parts. Part one includes the lexical explanation of difficult words and the author's praise of the king. The king is identified as Ghiyath al-Din, a pious ruler. Part two is an apology for praising a worldly ruler, clarifying that it is only for religious reasons. Part three is the naming of the book and a prayer. Then a question arises about the apparent redundancy in the book's title: both 'Hall' and 'Tawdih' mean clarification. The commentator gives two answers: first, 'Hall' is absolute clarification while 'Tawdih' is restricted clarification; second, they remove different types of ambiguity. This shows the scholarly care in defining terms.

Key Terms
توضیح (al-Tawdih): The name of the book, meaning 'clarification' but specifically extra clarification as per answer (1).
حل غوامض التنقیح (Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih): Meaning 'solving the ambiguities of al-Tanqih', another work.
خفاء (khafa'): Ambiguity, either in individual words (مفردات) or composition (ترکیب).
ظرفیت الشی فی نفسہ (zarfiyyat al-shay fi nafsih): The logical fallacy of a thing containing itself, here applied to the title's apparent redundancy.

Key Takeaway
Two seemingly synonymous terms can be logically valid if they differ in scope (absolute vs. restricted) or address distinct domains (word-level vs. compositional ambiguity).

Understanding the Book's Dual Title: Tawdih and Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih
Explaining the non-redundancy of the book's dual title

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the dual title 'Al-Tawdih' and 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih' is not redundant by identifying the distinct types of clarification they represent.

Core Idea
A book's title can contain multiple clarifications without self-contradiction when they address different levels of obscurity.

At first glance, it might seem that naming a book both 'Al-Tawdih' and 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih' is redundant, since both mean 'clarification'. However, the author anticipates this objection and provides two sophisticated responses that demonstrate a precise understanding of linguistic and logical nuance. This lesson walks through the objection and its resolution, sharpening your ability to analyze definitions and avoid logical fallacies in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Recognize the logical problem: if both titles mean 'clarification', then the title 'Al-Tawdih' is contained within 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih', implying a thing containing itself (zarfiyat al-shay' fi nafsih).
This is the classical fallacy of self-containment.
2
Analyze the First Answer: Absolute vs. Qualified
Understand the distinction: 'Hal' (absolute clarification) vs. 'Tawdih' (qualified, additional clarification). The absolute can contain the qualified without contradiction.
The absolute (mutlaq) is broader; the qualified (muqayyad) is more specific.
3
Analyze the Second Answer: Types of Obscurity
Recognize that obscurity can be lexical (individual words) or syntactic (composition). 'Tawdih' removes lexical obscurity; 'Hal' removes syntactic obscurity.
These are two distinct domains, so no redundancy.
4
Evaluate the Logical Validity
Confirm that either answer independently resolves the objection. The two answers are complementary, not contradictory.
This demonstrates the author's methodological rigor.
5
Apply to Other Usul Contexts
Consider how similar distinctions (mutlaq/muqayyad, lexical/syntactic) appear in defining usul terms like 'amm', 'khass', or 'mujmal'.
Precision in definition is crucial in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سميتہ سے مصنف نے تسمیۃ الکتاب کو ذکر فرمایا ہے کہ میں نے اس کتاب کا نام توضیح فی فرمایا حل غوامض التنقیح رکھا۔ اور ساتھ ساتھ کتاب لکھنے میں غلطی واقع ہونے سے بچنے کے لئے اللہ رب العزت سے دعا کی ہے۔ سوال : حل غوامض التنقیح سے مراد بھی ایضاح ہے۔ اور التوضیح سے مراد بھی ایضاح ہے تو اس سے تو ظرفیتہ الشی فی نفسہ لازم آتی ہے۔ جواب (۱): حل غوامض التنقیح سے مراد مطلق ایضاح ہے اور توضیح سے مراد زیادتی ایضاح ہے۔ گویا توضیح مقدید بالایضاح ہے اور حل مطلق ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں مطلق مقید کے لیے ظرف بن رہا ہے۔ جو اس مقید اور غیر مقید کو اپنے میں لیے ہوئے ہے تو ظرفیتہ الشی فی نفسہ لازم نہیں آتی ۔ جواب (۲): - معنی و مفہوم میں خفاء کبھی تو الفاظ مفردہ کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور کبھی خفاء علیت ترکیبیہ کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے تو توضیح سے مراد پہلی قسم کے خفاء کو دور کرنا ہے اور حل سے مراد دوسری قسم کے خفاء کو دور کرنا ہے لہذا ظرفیتہ الشی فی نفسہ کی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی ۔
From 'Samaytuhu' the author mentions the naming of the book: I named this book 'Al-Tawdih' and 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih'. And along with that, he prayed to Allah to protect from error in writing the book. Question: 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih' also means clarification, and 'Al-Tawdih' also means clarification, then this entails the thing containing itself. Answer (1): 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih' means absolute clarification, and 'Al-Tawdih' means additional clarification. So 'Tawdih' is qualified by clarification, and 'Hal' is absolute. Thus the absolute becomes a container for the qualified, containing both the qualified and unqualified, so the thing containing itself does not necessarily arise. Answer (2): Concealment in meaning and concept is sometimes due to individual words and sometimes due to compositional structure. So 'Tawdih' refers to removing the first type of concealment, and 'Hal' refers to removing the second type. Therefore the problem of the thing containing itself does not arise.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion from the sharh. It addresses a logical objection regarding the book's double title: both 'Al-Tawdih' and 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih' mean clarification, so the title would be redundant or entail self-containment. The commentator gives two answers. First, 'Hal' denotes absolute clarification while 'Tawdih' denotes a more specific, intensified clarification; thus the absolute contains the qualified without contradiction. Second, concealment operates on two levels: lexical (individual words) and syntactic (composition). 'Tawdih' addresses lexical obscurity, while 'Hal' addresses syntactic obscurity, making the two distinct. This is a typical usul exercise in precision of terminology.

Key Terms
حل غوامض التنقیح (Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih): The author's title meaning 'unraveling the obscurities of Al-Tanqih'.
توضیح (Al-Tawdih): The book's title meaning 'clarification', but specifically for lexical obscurities.
ظرفیتہ الشی فی نفسہ (Zarfiyat al-shay' fi nafsih): The logical fallacy of a thing containing itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's second answer, what is the difference between 'Al-Tawdih' and 'Hal Ghawamid al-Tanqih'?
A) 'Al-Tawdih' is absolute clarification, 'Hal' is qualified clarification.
B) 'Al-Tawdih' removes lexical obscurity, 'Hal' removes syntactic obscurity.
C) 'Al-Tawdih' means clarification, 'Hal' means concealment.
D) Both titles are identical; the author was mistaken.

Key Takeaway
The dual title is not redundant: the two names clarify different types of obscurity (lexical vs. syntactic) or operate at different levels (absolute vs. qualified).
