لیے کہ کلام میں اعجاز یہ ہے کہ معنی کو ایسے طریقہ پر ادا کیا جائے جو اس کے ماسوا تمام طریقوں سے زیادہ بلیغ ہو۔ اور نہیں ہو سکتا اس کا طریق مگر ایک لیکن سحرفی الکلام پس وہ اعجاز سے کم درجہ ہے۔ اور اس کے طرق ایک سے زائد ہیں پس لایا اس میں جمع کے لفظ کو۔ اور نام رکھا میں نے اس کا تنقیح الاصول کے ساتھ اور اللہ تعالیٰ سے سوال ہے یہ کہ نفع دے اس کے ساتھ اس کے مصنف کو اور اس کے کاتب کو اور اس کے پڑھنے والے کو اور اس کے طالب کو اور بنائے اس کو خالص اپنی ذات کریم کے لیے۔ تحقیق وہی نیکی قبول کرنے والا ہے۔ رحم کرنے والا ہے۔ تالیف تنقیح کیلئے اصول فخر الاسلام کو متعین کرنے کی وجہ تشریح: اس عبارت میں ماتن نے علت تعیین متن کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ میں نے تنقیح لکھنے کے لیے فخر الاسلام علی بزدی کی کتاب اصول فقہ کو چند وجوہ سے متعین کیا ہے ۔ (۱) اس وقت کے سارے علماء اس کتاب کی طرف متوجہ تھے۔ (۲) اس کتاب کے معانی اس کی مشکل عبارتوں میں بند تھے ۔ میں نے سوچا کہ تشریح کردوں۔ (۳) بعض علماء اس کتاب کی ظاہری عبارت دیکھ کرطعن کرتے تھے میں نے ان کا رد کرنے کے لیے تنقیح لکھی ہے۔ فحول العلماء: فحول فل کی جمع ہے وہ بیل جو ہل چلائے وجہ تسمیہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح ہل چلا کر زمین کو چیر کر تہہ تک پہنچا جا سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح عالم مسئلہ کو ذبح کر کے مسئلہ کی تہ تک پہنچتا ہے۔ کیفیت مصنف ( تنقیح) اردت تنقیحہ : یہاں سے مصنف نے کیفیت مصنف کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ (۱) اصول فخر الاسلام میں زوائد تھے میں نے تنقیح میں ان کا اختصار کیا ہے نیز اس کے بکھرے ہوئے مضامین کو مرتب کیا ہے۔ (۲) اس کی مراد کو واضح کیا ہے۔ (۳) منطقی قواعد کے مطابق اصول کی بنیاد رکھی اور ان کی تقسیم کی ۔ (۴) محصول نامی کتاب (مصنفہ امام رازی) اور اصول ابن حاجب کا خلاصہ بھی ذکر کیا ہے ۔ (۵) ایسی تحقیقات اور تدقیقات ذکر کیں کہ عام کتابیں اس سے خالی ہیں ۔ (۶) عربی ادب کا ایسا جادو جگایا کہ لوگ اس کی مثل لانے سے عاجز آگئے۔
Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. And precise, profound, and strong investigations that books lack, while following the path of conciseness and brevity, clutching the edges of sorcery and holding fast to the handhold of inimitability. He chose in inimitability the handhold and in sorcery the edges, because inimitability is stronger and more reliable than sorcery. And he chose for the handhold the singular word and for the edges the plural word, because inimitability in speech is that the meaning is conveyed in a way that is more eloquent than all other ways, and this can only be one way. As for sorcery in speech, it is below inimitability and its ways are more than one, so he used the plural word for it. And he named it Tanqih al-Usul. Allah is asketh that He benefit through it its author, its writer, its reader, and its student, and make it purely for His noble face. Indeed, He is the Benign, the Merciful. Translation: After praise and salutations, then indeed the servant who is a seeker of means with a strong rope, who is Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, may his fortune be fruitful and his effort successful. When I saw the great scholars engaged in every era in discussion and debate of Usul al-Fiqh, they are attentive to it. This derives from akkaba 'ala wajhihi, meaning he fell upon it. So indeed the person who is extremely attentive to something falls upon it. (That Usul al-Fiqh book) which is by the leader of great imams, Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali al-Bazdawi, may Allah grant him an abode of peace (Paradise). It is a majestic book, with al-Burhan as its title. Its meanings are buried in the rocks of its difficult expressions, and its fine points are alluded to in the subtleties of its secret indications. And I found some scholars who criticize the apparent words of this book due to the shortness of their sight from the superficial glances of Allama 'Ali al-Bazdawi. That is, they cannot see deeply with the corner of their eye without intending to look at it. So I intended to purify it and arrange it, and I sought to clarify its meaning and explain it, and to base it on logical principles and classify it, while bringing in it summaries of the topics of al-Mahsul and the Usul of the investigator and verifier Jamal al-Din Ibn al-Hajib, along with wonderful investigations and precise, strong verifications that books lack, while following the path of conciseness and brevity, clutching the ropes of sorcery and holding fast to the handhold of inimitability (to its firm knot). He chose in inimitability the handhold and in sorcery the edges, because inimitability is stronger and more reliable than sorcery. And he chose for the handhold the singular word and for the edges the plural word, because inimitability in speech is that the meaning is conveyed in a way that is more eloquent than all other ways, and this can only be one way. As for sorcery in speech, it is below inimitability and its ways are more than one, so he used the plural word for it. And he named it Tanqih al-Usul. And Allah is asketh that He benefit through it its author, its writer, its reader, and its student, and make it purely for His noble face. Indeed, He accepts goodness and is Merciful. Reason for selecting al-Bazdawi's Usul for writing Tanqih: Explanation: In this passage, the author (matn) mentions the reason for selecting the text: that he selected Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali al-Bazdawi's book of Usul for writing Tanqih for several reasons: (1) All scholars of that time were engaged with this book. (2) The meanings of this book were locked in its difficult expressions; I thought to explain them. (3) Some scholars criticized the apparent expressions of this book; I wrote Tanqih to refute them. Fuhul al-'Ulama': Fuhul is the plural of fahl, the bull that plows; the reason for the name is that just as one can plow and reach the depth of the earth, so the scholar dissects the issue and reaches its depth. Method of the author (Tanqih): 'Aradtu tanqihahu': From here the author mentions the method of his work: (1) There were extras in al-Bazdawi's Usul; I summarized them in Tanqih and also organized its scattered topics. (2) I clarified its meaning. (3) I based the principles on logical rules and classified them. (4) I also mentioned summaries from the book al-Mahsul (by Imam al-Razi) and Usul Ibn al-Hajib. (5) I mentioned investigations and verifications that common books lack. (6) I displayed such magic in Arabic rhetoric that people were unable to produce its like.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his work Tanqih al-Usul. It belongs to the genre of front matter, where the author explains his motivation, methodology, and the sources he relied upon. The author, Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud (known as Taj al-Shari'ah), states that he observed scholars of his time deeply engaged with the Usul al-Fiqh work of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. However, he noticed that some scholars misunderstood or criticized the book because they only looked at its surface without grasping its deeper meanings. Therefore, he decided to write a commentary (Tanqih) to purify and arrange the text, clarify its meanings, and base it on logical principles. Additionally, he incorporated summaries from two other major works: al-Mahsul by Imam al-Razi (a Shafi'i-Ash'ari scholar) and Usul Ibn al-Hajib (a Maliki scholar), while adding his own precise investigations. The author's style is notable for its rhetorical flourish—he describes his approach using metaphors of 'sorcery' (sihr) and 'inimitability' (i'jaz), explaining that the most eloquent expression of meaning is unique and cannot be replicated. This preface sets the stage for a work that is not merely a summary but a critical refinement of the Hanafi usul tradition, engaging with other schools and adding original analyses. The Urdu portion provides a detailed paraphrase and expansion, listing six specific aspects of his methodology: condensing superfluous content, organizing scattered material, clarifying intent, structuring based on logic, incorporating external sources, and achieving stylistic excellence. This lesson is important for students to understand the author's scholarly approach and the context of the work they are about to study.

Key Terms
تنقیح (Tanqih): Refinement or comprehensive ordering of a work, involving removal of redundancies and reorganization of content.
عروة الإعجاز ('Urwat al-I'jaz): The strongest handhold of inimitability, referring to the highest form of rhetorical expression that cannot be equaled.
فحول العلماء (Fuhul al-'Ulama'): The leading scholars, likened to plowing bulls, who deeply dissect issues to reach their core.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, besides al-Bazdawi's Usul, which two other works did he incorporate into Tanqih al-Usul?
A) Al-Mahsul by al-Razi and Usul Ibn al-Hajib
B) Al-Mustasfa by al-Ghazali and Al-Muwafaqat by al-Shatibi
C) Al-Burhan by al-Juwayni and Al-Muntakhab by al-Pazdawi
D) Only al-Bazdawi's work, as he was the sole reference

Key Takeaway
Tanqih al-Usul is a refined synthesis of al-Bazdawi's text with additional sources and original insights, demonstrating the author's scholarly ambition and methodological care.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Structure of a Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh Work
Stating the arrangement of the book into a preface and two sections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the bipartite structure (preface + two sections) of a classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh textbook as presented in al-Talwih.

Core Idea
A usul text opens with preliminaries (muqaddimah), then splits into two main sections for core topics.

This passage from al-Talwih introduces the organizational framework of the matn (original text). The commentator states that the book is arranged into a preface (muqaddimah) and two sections (qismayn). The preface contains matters that are not among the core objectives of the discipline, while the two sections cover the substantive topics. Understanding this structure helps you navigate later discussions and know where to locate specific principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
Read the phrase: 'الكِتَابُ مُرَتَّبٌ عَلَى مُقَدِّمَةٍ وَقِسَمَينِ'. This is a clear statement about the book's composition.
The book referred to is the matn of Usul al-Fiqh, likely the one being commented upon by al-Talwih.
2
Distinguish the preface from the sections
The passage distinguishes between what belongs to the core objectives (maqasid al-fann) and what does not. The preface covers the latter – preliminary definitions, classifications, and background.
In Hanafi works, the muqaddimah often includes discussions on the nature of usul, the definition of fiqh, and the sources.
3
Understand the bipartite division
The two sections (qismayn) contain the main subjects. Although the passage cuts off, standard Hanafi usul works typically divide into: (1) al-adillah (sources of law) and (2) al-ahkaam (rulings derived from them) or similar.
This bipartite structure is common but not universal; some authors add more divisions.
4
Apply the structure to other texts
Now that you know the pattern, you can recognize it in other Hanafi usul works like al-Hidayah or al-Usul al-Pazdawi.
Always look for a preface and see if the body splits into two broad parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلويح
قَولُهُ أُصُولُ الفِقهِ الكِتَابُ مُرَتَّبٌ عَلَى مُقَدِّمَةٍ وَقِسَمَينِ ؛ لأنَّ المَذْكُورَ فِيهِ
إمَّامِنُ مَقَاصِدِ الفَنْ أو لا الثَّانِي المُقَدَّمَةُ وَالأوَّلُ إِمَّا أَن يَكُونَ البَحتُ فِيهِ عَن
Al-Talwih: His statement: 'Usul al-fiqh' – the book is arranged upon a preface (muqaddimah) and two sections (qismayn); because what is mentioned in it is either from the objectives of the discipline or not; the second is the preface; and the first is either the research is about...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This is an introductory passage from the commentary al-Talwih. It explains the structure of the matn (original work) which is organized into a preface (muqaddimah) and two main sections (qasman). The commentator notes that whatever is discussed in the book belongs either to the core objectives of the discipline (maqasid al-fann) or to preliminary matters. The preface covers the latter, while the first section deals with the core objectives. The text cuts off, but it clearly outlines a systematic approach to the subject, typical of Hanafi usul works which begin with definitions and then proceed to substantive issues.

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddimah): An introductory section of the book that covers preliminary matters not part of the main objectives.
قسمين (qismayn): Two main sections of the book that treat the core objectives of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Structure of al-Tawdih: Introduction, Two Parts, and Appendices
Explaining the book's arrangement and the two approaches to defining Usul al-Fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the overall structure of al-Tawdih and explain how the book is organized into an introduction and two parts.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh texts are organized: an introduction defining the science, then proofs, then rulings.

When opening a classical usul text, the first thing you encounter is its structure. This lesson breaks down the architecture of Sadr al-Shariah's al-Tawdih: a preface, two main parts (on proofs and rulings), and concluding chapters. Understanding this map will help you navigate the entire discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three major divisions
The book is arranged with an introduction (muqaddima) and two main parts (qismayn). All content falls into one of these three.
2
Understand the content of the introduction
The introduction defines the science of usul and establishes its subject matter. It is presented first because a student must know what the science is about before studying its details.
3
Recognize the first part's four pillars and appendices
The first part deals with proofs (adilla) and is built on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. It is appended with chapters on Tarjih (preponderance) and Ijtihad.
These appendices conclude the discussion of proofs.
4
See the second part's three chapters
The second part covers rulings (ahkam) and is divided into three chapters: the ruling itself (hukm), what it pertains to (al-mahkum bih), and the subject of rulings (al-mahkum 'alayhi).
5
Note the author's justification
The author explains that the discipline only investigates proofs and rulings, nothing else. Thus the division into parts is exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ أُصُولُ الفِقهِ الكِتَابُ مُرَتَّبٌ عَلَى مُقَدِّمَةٍ وَقِسَمَينِ ؛ لأنَّ المَذْكُورَ فِيهِ إمَّامِنُ مَقَاصِدِ الفَنْ أو لا الثَّانِي المُقَدَّمَةُ وَالأوَّلُ إِمَّا أَن يَكُونَ البَحتُ فِيهِ عَن الأَدِلَّةِ وَهُوَ القِسمُ الأوَّلُ اَوْ عَن الأحكام وَهُوَ القِسمُ الثَّانِي إِذ لَا يُبحَثُ فِي هَذَا الفَنْ عَن غَيْرِهِمَا وَالقِسمُ الأوَّلُ مَنِى عَلَى أَربَعَةِ أَركَانِ الكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةُ وَالإجمَاعُ وَالقِيَاسُ وَهُوَ مُذَيّلٌ بِبَابَى التَّرجِيحِ وَالِاجْتِهَادِ وَالثَّانِي عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أبْوَابٍ في الحكم والمحكوم بِهِ وَالمَحكُومٍ عَلَيْهِ وَسَتَعرِفْ بَيَانَ إِلَّانحِصَارِ. وَالمُقَدِّمَةُ مَسُوقَةٌ لِتَعريف هذَا العِلمِ وَتَحقِيقِ مَوضُوعِهِ ؛ لأنَّ مِن حَقِّ الطَّالِبِ لِلكَثرَةِ المَصْبُوطَةِ بِجِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ أَن يَعرِفَهَا بِتِلْكَ الجِهَةِ لِيَامَنَ مِن فَوَاتِ المَقصُودِ وَالاسْتِغَالِ بِغَيْرِهِ وَكُلُّ عِلمٍ هُوَ كَثرَةٌ مَصْبُوطَةٌ بِتَعرِيفِهِ الَّذِي بِهِ يَتَمَيَّزُ عِندَ الطَّالِبِ وَمَوضُوعُهُ الَّذِي بِهِ يَمَتَارُ فِي نَفْسِهِ عَن سَائِرِ العُلُومِ فَحِينَ تَشَوَّقَت نَفسُ السَّامِعِ إِلَى التَّعرِيفِ لِيَتَمَيَّزَ العِلمُ عِندَهُ قَالَ المُصَنِّفُ هَذَا الَّذِى أَذكُرُهُ أُصُولُ الفِقهِ إعْنَاء لِلسَّامِعِ عَن السُّؤَالِ أَوْقَالَ عَن لِسَانِهِ أُصُولُ الفِقِهِ مَا هِيَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ فِي تَعرِيفِهِ وَأُصُولُ الفِقْهِ لَقَبْ لِهَذَا الفَنِّ مَنقُولٌ عَن مُرَكَّبٍ إِضَافِي فَلَهُ بِكُلِّ اعتِبَارٍ تَعرِيف قَدَّمَ بَعضُهم التعريف اللَّقَبِيَّ نَظَرًا إِلَى أَنَّ المَعنَى العِلمِيَّ هُوَ المَقصُودُ فِي الأَعْلَامِ وَأَنَّهُ مِن الإِضَافِي بِمَنزِلَةِ البَسِيطِ مِن المُرَكَّبِ وَالمُصَنِّفُ قَدَّمَ الإِضَافِيَّ نَظَرًا إِلَى أَنَّ المَنقُولَ عَنهُ مُقَدَّمٌ وَإِلَى أَنَّ الفِقَهَ مَاخُوذُ فِي التَّعرِيفِ اللَّقَبِى فَإِن قَدَّمَ تَفسِيرَهُ أَمْكَنَ ذِكرُهُ فِى اللَّقَبِي كَمَا قَالَ المُصنِّفُ هُوَ العِلمُ بِالقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقهِ وَإِلَّا أُحتِيجَ إِلَى إِبْرَادِ تَفسِيرِهِ تَارَةً فِي اللَّقَبِي وَتَارَةً فِى الإِضَافِي كَمَا فِى أُصُولِ ابنِ الحَاجِبِ وَلَمَّا كَانَ أُصُولُ الفِقهِ عِندَ قَصدِ المَعنَى الإِضَافِيّ جَمْعًا وَعِندَ قَصدِ المَعنَى اللَّقَبِيِّ مُفرَدًا كَعَبدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ فَنُعَرِّفُهَا أَوَّلا بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِضَافَةِ بِتَأْنِيثِ الضَّمِيرِ وَقَالَ فَالآنَ نُعَرِّفُهُ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ لَقَبٌ لِعِلمٍ مخصُوص بِتَذْكِيرِهِ وَاللَّقَبُ عَلَمٌ يُشعِرُ بِمَدحٍ أَو ذَمِّ وَأُصُولُ الفِقِهِ عَلَمٌ لِهَذَا الفَنِّ
His statement: 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The book is arranged with an introduction and two parts. Because what is mentioned in it is either from the purposes of the discipline or not; the second is the introduction; the first is either the investigation of proofs (first part) or of rulings (second part), since nothing else is investigated in this discipline. The first part is built upon four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, and it is appended with chapters on Tarjih and Ijtihad. The second part has three chapters: on Hukm, al-Mahkum bih, and al-Mahkum 'alayhi. You will know the explanation of this enumeration. The introduction is presented for defining this science and ascertaining its subject matter, because the student of a collection of particulars unified by a single aspect has the right to know them by that aspect, in order to be safe from missing the purpose and occupying himself with other than it. Every science is a collection of particulars unified by its definition, by which it is distinguished for the student, and its subject matter, by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences. So when the listener's soul yearns for the definition to distinguish the science for him, the author said: 'This that I mention is Usul al-Fiqh', sparing the listener from asking, or he said on his behalf: 'What is Usul al-Fiqh?' Then he began its definition. And 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a title (laqab) for this discipline, transferred from a construct (tarkib idafi). So from each perspective it has a definition. Some have presented the definition as a laqab, considering that the scientific meaning is intended in appellations, and that it is to the construct as the simple is to the compound. The author presented the construct definition, considering that that from which it is transferred is prior, and that fiqh is included in the laqab definition. If he presented its explanation, it could be mentioned in the laqabi definition as the author said: 'It is knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh.' Otherwise, it is necessary to present its explanation once in the laqabi and once in the idafi, as in Ibn al-Hajib's Usul. Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' when intending the idafi meaning is plural, and when intending the laqabi meaning is singular like 'Abdullah', he said: 'So we first define it in consideration of the idafa with a feminine pronoun' and he said: 'Now we define it in consideration that it is a title for a particular science with a masculine pronoun.' And a laqab is a proper name that indicates praise or blame. And Usul al-Fiqh is a proper name for this discipline.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Talwih explaining the structure of al-Tawdih and the definition of Usul al-Fiqh. It opens by stating that the book is organized into a preface (muqaddima) and two major sections (qismayn). The first section deals with proofs (adalila) – the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas – and is concluded with chapters on Tarjih (preponderance) and Ijtihad. The second section covers rulings (ahkam), divided into three chapters: the ruling itself (hukm), what it pertains to (al-mahkum bih – acts of worshipers), and the subject of rulings (al-mahkum 'alayhi – the legally competent person). The introduction is meant to define the science and its subject. The commentator then discusses the definition of 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The term is a laqab (proper name) for this discipline, originally derived from the construct 'usul al-fiqh'. There are two approaches to defining it: (1) as an idafa (construct) – considering the meanings of 'usul' and 'fiqh'; (2) as a laqab – defining it as a single science. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) prefers to begin with the idafi definition, because the source term is prior and because 'fiqh' appears in the laqab definition. He illustrates that if one first defines 'fiqh', then the laqab definition (e.g., 'knowledge of the principles that lead to fiqh') becomes possible. Otherwise, one must explain 'fiqh' both in the laqab and the idafa definitions, as Ibn al-Hajib did. The commentator notes that when meaning the idafa, the word 'usul' is plural; when meaning the laqab, it is singular. Accordingly, the author uses a feminine pronoun for the idafi definition ('nu'arrifuha') and a masculine pronoun for the laqabi definition ('nu'arrifuhu'). The passage concludes that a laqab is a proper name that indicates praise or blame, and 'Usul al-Fiqh' is the proper name for this discipline.

Key Terms
مُذَيّل (mudhayyal): Appended, supplemented with additional chapters.
أركان (arkān): Pillars; here referring to the four main sources of Islamic law as foundational elements of the first part.
قسمان (qismān): Two parts or sections.
مقدمة (muqaddima): Introduction; a preliminary section that defines the science and its subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many parts (qismayn) does the book al-Tawdih have, according to the passage?
A) Three parts: introduction, proofs, rulings
B) Two parts: proofs and rulings
C) Four parts: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas
D) One part: the introduction

Key Takeaway
Al-Tawdih is structured with a preface, two parts (proofs and rulings), and concluding chapters on tarjih and ijtihad.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Two Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh: Idafi and Laqabi
Explaining the two definitions of Usul al-Fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the idafi and laqabi definitions of Usul al-Fiqh and explain why Sadr al-Shariah prioritized the idafi.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh can be defined as a construct or as a proper name; the idafi is foundational for the laqabi.

The term 'Usul al-Fiqh' is both a compound noun and a proper name for this science. This lesson explores the two ways to define it: by breaking down the words (idafi) or by treating it as a title (laqab). The author's choice reveals a deeper methodological preference.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two types of definition
The passage explains that 'Usul al-Fiqh' can be defined either as an idafa (construct) where each word retains its lexical meaning, or as a laqab (proper name) for the discipline.
2
Understand the idafi definition
The idafi definition analyzes the component words: 'usul' (principles) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence). It treats the term as a compound.
This is the original meaning from which the laqab is transferred.
3
Understand the laqabi definition
The laqabi definition treats 'Usul al-Fiqh' as a proper name for a specific science, without analyzing its parts. It is like 'Abdullah' as a single name.
A laqab is a proper name that indicates praise or blame.
4
See why Sadr al-Shariah started with idafi
The author prioritized the idafi because the compound is the origin (manqul 'anhu) from which the laqab is transferred. Also, the laqab definition requires prior understanding of 'fiqh', which the idafi provides.
5
Note the pronoun shift
When defining as idafa, the author uses a feminine pronoun ('nu'arrifuha') because 'usul' is plural and feminine. When defining as laqab, he uses masculine ('nu'arrifuhu') because the laqab is treated as a masculine singular noun.
This grammatical detail reflects the two different conceptual treatments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لِيَامَنَ مِن فَوَاتِ المَقصُودِ وَالاسْتِغَالِ بِغَيْرِهِ وَكُلُّ عِلمٍ هُوَ كَثرَةٌ مَصْبُوطَةٌ بِتَعرِيفِهِ الَّذِي بِهِ يَتَمَيَّزُ عِندَ الطَّالِبِ وَمَوضُوعُهُ الَّذِي بِهِ يَمَتَارُ فِي السُّؤَالِ أَوْقَالَ عَن لِسَانِهِ أُصُولُ الفِقِهِ مَا هِيَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ فِي تَعرِيفِهِ وَأُصُولُ الفِقْهِ لَقَبْ لِهَذَا الفَنِّ مَنقُولٌ عَن مُرَكَّبٍ إِضَافِي فَلَهُ بِكُلِّ اعتِبَارٍ تَعرِيف قَدَّمَ بَعضُهم التعريف اللَّقَبِيَّ نَظَرًا إِلَى أَنَّ المَعنَى العِلمِيَّ هُوَ المَقصُودُ فِي الأَعْلَامِ وَأَنَّهُ مِن الإِضَافِي بِمَنزِلَةِ البَسِيطِ مِن المُرَكَّبِ وَالمُصَنِّفُ قَدَّمَ الإِضَافِيَّ نَظَرًا إِلَى أَنَّ المَنقُولَ عَنهُ مُقَدَّمٌ وَإِلَى أَنَّ الفِقَهَ مَاخُوذُ فِي التَّعرِيفِ اللَّقَبِى فَإِن قَدَّمَ تَفسِيرَهُ أَمْكَنَ ذِكرُهُ فِى اللَّقَبِي كَمَا قَالَ المُصنِّفُ وَلَمَّا كَانَ أُصُولُ الفِقهِ عِندَ قَصدِ المَعنَى الإِضَافِيّ جَمْعًا وَعِندَ قَصدِ المَعنَى اللَّقَبِيِّ مُفرَدًا كَعَبدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ فَنُعَرِّفُهَا أَوَّلا بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِضَافَةِ بِتَأْنِيثِ His statement: 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The book is arranged with an introduction and two parts. Because what is mentioned in it is either from the purposes of the discipline or not; the second is the introduction; the first is either the investigation of proofs (first part) or of rulings (second part), since nothing else is investigated in this discipline. The first part is built upon four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, and it is appended with chapters on Tarjih and Ijtihad. The second part has three chapters: on Hukm, al-Mahkum bih, and al-Mahkum 'alayhi. You will know the explanation of this enumeration. The introduction is presented for defining this science and ascertaining its subject matter, because the student of a collection of particulars unified by a single aspect has the right to know them by that aspect, in order to be safe from missing the purpose and occupying himself with other than it. Every science is a collection of particulars unified by its definition, by which it is distinguished for the student, and its subject matter, by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences. So when the listener's soul yearns for the definition to distinguish the science for him, the author said: 'This that I mention is Usul al-Fiqh', sparing the listener from asking, or he said on his behalf: 'What is Usul al-Fiqh?' Then he began its definition. And 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a title (laqab) for this discipline, transferred from a construct (tarkib idafi). So from each perspective it has a definition. Some have presented the definition as a laqab, considering that the scientific meaning is intended in appellations, and that it is to the construct as the simple is to the compound. The author presented the construct definition, considering that that from which it is transferred is prior, and that fiqh is included in the laqab definition. If he presented its explanation, it could be mentioned in the laqabi definition as the author said: 'It is knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh.' Otherwise, it is necessary to present its explanation once in the laqabi and once in the idafi, as in Ibn al-Hajib's Usul. Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' when intending the idafi meaning is plural, and when intending the laqabi meaning is singular like 'Abdullah', he said: 'So we first define it in consideration of the idafa with a feminine pronoun' and he said: 'Now we define it in consideration that it is a title for a particular science with a masculine pronoun.' And a laqab is a proper name that indicates praise or blame. And Usul al-Fiqh is a proper name for this discipline.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Talwih explaining the structure of al-Tawdih and the definition of Usul al-Fiqh. It opens by stating that the book is organized into a preface (muqaddima) and two major sections (qismayn). The first section deals with proofs (adalila) – the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas – and is concluded with chapters on Tarjih (preponderance) and Ijtihad. The second section covers rulings (ahkam), divided into three chapters: the ruling itself (hukm), what it pertains to (al-mahkum bih – acts of worshipers), and the subject of rulings (al-mahkum 'alayhi – the legally competent person). The introduction is meant to define the science and its subject. The commentator then discusses the definition of 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The term is a laqab (proper name) for this discipline, originally derived from the construct 'usul al-fiqh'. There are two approaches to defining it: (1) as an idafa (construct) – considering the meanings of 'usul' and 'fiqh'; (2) as a laqab – defining it as a single science. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) prefers to begin with the idafi definition, because the source term is prior and because 'fiqh' appears in the laqab definition. He illustrates that if one first defines 'fiqh', then the laqab definition (e.g., 'knowledge of the principles that lead to fiqh') becomes possible. Otherwise, one must explain 'fiqh' both in the laqab and the idafa definitions, as Ibn al-Hajib did. The commentator notes that when meaning the idafa, the word 'usul' is plural; when meaning the laqab, it is singular. Accordingly, the author uses a feminine pronoun for the idafi definition ('nu'arrifuha') and a masculine pronoun for the laqabi definition ('nu'arrifuhu'). The passage concludes that a laqab is a proper name that indicates praise or blame, and 'Usul al-Fiqh' is the proper name for this discipline.

Key Terms
اللقب (al-laqab): A proper name that indicates praise or blame; used here for the name of a science.
الإضافة (al-iḍāfa): The construct state; the compound 'usul al-fiqh' where each word retains its lexical meaning.
المركب الإضافي (al-murakkab al-iḍāfī): The idafi compound; a grammatical construction consisting of two nouns in a possessive relationship.
العلم (al-ʿilm): Knowledge; in the laqab definition, it refers to a body of knowledge or a discipline.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Structure of Usul al-Fiqh and Its Definition
Explains book structure and defines usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of usul al-fiqh and explain the three-part structure of the discipline (introduction, first section on proofs, second section on rulings).

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is defined as the knowledge of principles leading to fiqh; its structure comprises an introduction, proofs (four pillars), and rulings (three pillars).

This passage from the commentary of Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih introduces usul al-fiqh as a science. It explains the overall structure of a standard usul text: an introduction defining the science and its subject matter, followed by two main sections — one dealing with the proofs (adilla: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and the other with the rulings (ahkam: hukm, mahkum bihi, mahkum 'alayhi). The commentary also clarifies that chapters on ijtihad and tarjih are subsumed under qiyas, not independent pillars. Understanding this structure prepares you to navigate any usul al-fiqh text with clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three major divisions
The book is divided into an introduction (muqaddima) and two sections (qism awwal and qism thani). Recognize that everything in the book is either one of these.
2
List the four pillars of the first section
The first section deals with proofs: Kitab (Quran), Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). Note that ijtihad and tarjih are not separate pillars but part of qiyas.
The commentator addresses a potential objection about why ijtihad and tarjih are not counted separately.
3
List the three pillars of the second section
The second section deals with rulings: hukm (the ruling itself), mahkum bihi (the thing ruled upon), and mahkum 'alayhi (the subject of the ruling).
These three cover all aspects of legal rulings.
4
State the definition of usul al-fiqh
The definition given is: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh' (العلم بالقواعد التي توصل بها إلى الفقه).
This definition emphasizes the instrumental role of usul as a tool for deriving fiqh.
5
Distinguish construct vs titular meanings
The term 'usul al-fiqh' has a construct meaning (plural: principles of fiqh) and a titular meaning (singular: the science). The author prioritizes the construct meaning as the original basis.
When referring to the science, it is treated as a singular laqab.

ہوئے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک معنی علمی وہ مقصود ہوتا ہے اعلام میں اور بے شک وہ اضافی سے بمنزلہ بسیط کے ہے مرکب سے اور مصنف نے مقدم کیا ہے اضافی کو نظر کرتے ہوئے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک منقول عنہ مقدم ہے۔ اور اسی بات کی طرف کہ بے شک فقہ ماخوذ ہے تعریف لقمی میں۔ پس بے شک مقدم کیا ہے اس کی تفسیر کوتا کہ ممکن ہو اس کا ذکر کرنا تھی میں جیسا کہ کہا مصنف نے ھو العلم بالقواعد التی توصل بھا الی الفقہ ۔ ور نہ احتیاجی اس کی تفسیر لانے کی طرف کبھی ہوگئی تھی میں اور کبھی ہوگی اضافی میں جیسا کہ اصول ابن حاجب میں ہے۔ اور جب ہے اصول فقہ معنی اضافی کے ارادے کرنے کے وقت جمع اور معنی لعظمی کے ارادے کے وقت مفرد جیسے عبد اللہ کہا اس نے فنعرفها اولا اضافت کے اعتبار سے ضمیر کے مونث لانے کے ساتھ اور کہا اس نے فالآن نعرفہ اس اعتبار سے کے بے شک وہ لقب ہے علم مخصوص کے لیے اس کے مذکر لانے کے ساتھ ، اور لقب ایسا علم ہے کہ وہ شعر ہوتا ہے مدح یا ذم کی طرف اور اصول فقہ علم ہے اس فن کے لئے جو مشعر ہے فقہ کے لیے مبنی علیہ ہونے کے ساتھ کہ جس کے ساتھ چلتا ہے معاش کا نظام اور کامل ہوتی ہے معاد کی نجات اور یہ مدح ہے۔
177
شرح تلویح: قولہ اصول الفقہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ اس کتاب ( تنقیح مع توضیح ) کے ارکان کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ کہ یہ کتاب ایک مقدمہ اور دو قسموں پر مشتمل ہے۔
وجه حصر ارکان ثلاثه
لان الا مذکور :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض ان ارکان ثالثہ کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا ہے کہ جو کچھ کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ۔ مقاصد کے قبیل سے ہوگا یا نہیں۔ پانی مقدمہ ہے۔ اگر اول ہے تو پھر اس کی بحث دلائل سے ہو گی۔ یا احکام سے ہوگی اگر اول ہے۔ تو قسم اول ہے اگر ثانی ہے تو قسم ثانی ہے۔ قسم الاول:۔ یہ شرح کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں قسم اول کے ارکان کو بیان کیا ہے کہ قتم اول چار ارکان پر (بنی ) ہے۔
ا۔ کتاب اللہ ۲ ۔ سنت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم -۳۔ اجماع امت ۴۔ قیاس ۔
وھو ندیل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال :۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم اول چار ارکان پرمبنی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس میں تو باب الاجتہاد اور باب الترجیح بھی بیان کیے گئے۔ ہیں ۔ گویا تم اول چھ ارکان پر بنی ہوئی۔
جواب:۔ ترجیح اور اجتہاد کے باب میں کوئی نئی چیز نہیں بلکہ قیاس کے تابع ہیں۔ اور قیاس کے ذیل میں بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔ والثانی علی ثلثہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض قسم ثانی کے ارکان کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ قسم ثانی میں تین امور بیان ہوں گے۔ (۱) حکم (۲) محکوم بہ (۳) محکوم عامیہ ۔
والمقدمہ: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ غرض مقدمہ کے اجزاء اور مضامین کو بیان کرنا ہے کہ اس میں دو امور بیان ہوں گے۔ (۱) تعریف۔ (۲) موضوع باقی غرض و غایت تعریف سے معلوم ہو جائے گی۔
تعریف، موضوع کا جاننا کیوں ضروری ہے؟
لان من حق الطالب:- یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ یہاں سے اس بات کی دلیل بیان فرمائی ۔ کہ مقدمہ میں تعریف اور موضوع کا جاننا کیوں ضروری ہے۔ دلیل کو سمجھنے سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے مقدمہ سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔
The book is arranged into an introduction and two sections: because whatever is mentioned in this book is either from the aims of the discipline or not; the latter is the introduction. The first is either discussion of proofs—that is the first section—or of rulings—that is the second section. Because in this discipline nothing else is discussed. The first section is based on four pillars: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger (peace be upon him), consensus, and analogy. And it includes under it the two chapters of preference and independent reasoning. And the second section comprises three chapters: the ruling, the thing ruled upon, and the subject of the ruling. And soon you will know the explanation of the dependence. And the introduction is conducted for the definition of this science and the investigation of its subject matter. It is part of the right of the seeker of a specific multiplicity with a specific direction that he recognizes that multiplicity with that direction, so that he is protected from losing his objective and being occupied with something else. And every science is that specific multiplicity by its definition; it becomes distinguished for the student, and through its subject matter it is actually distinguished from all sciences. So when the listener's soul desires the definition so that the science becomes distinguished for him, the author said: 'What I am mentioning is usul al-fiqh', removing the listener's need to ask, or he said with his tongue: 'What is usul al-fiqh?' Then he began its definition. And 'usul al-fiqh' is a title for this discipline; it is transferred from a construct compound. So for it, according to each consideration, there is a definition. Some have prioritized the titular definition, looking to the fact that the scientific meaning is intended in appellations, and that the construct is like a simple [term] from the compound. And the author prioritized the construct, looking to the fact that the thing transferred from is primary, and also because fiqh is derived in the titular definition. So he prioritized its interpretation so that it could be mentioned in it, as the author said: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh.' Otherwise, the need for its interpretation sometimes occurred in it and sometimes in the construct, as in the Usul of Ibn al-Hajib. And when it is 'usul al-fiqh' intending the constructive meaning, it is plural; and intending the titular meaning, it is singular, like 'Abdullah'. He said: 'So we know it first according to the construct, bringing a feminine pronoun; and he said: 'Now we know it' according to it being a title for a specific science, bringing a masculine pronoun. And a title is a sign that points to praise or blame. And 'usul al-fiqh' is a science for this discipline, which indicates that fiqh is built upon it, with which the system of livelihood and the salvation of the afterlife are perfected, and that is praise.
Commentary of Talwih: His statement 'usul al-fiqh': This is the first part of the expression. The purpose of the commentator of this book (Tanqih with Tawdih) is to explain its pillars: that this book consists of an introduction and two sections.
The reason for limiting to three pillars: 'Because what is mentioned' - this is the second part of the commentary's expression. Its purpose is to explain the reason for limiting these three pillars: whatever is mentioned in the book is not free from two states: either it is from the category of aims or not; the latter is the introduction. If it is the first, then its discussion is either from proofs or from rulings; if the former, it is the first section; if the latter, it is the second section.
The first section: This is the third part of the commentary. Here the pillars of the first section are explained: that the first section is based on four pillars: 1. The Book of Allah, 2. The Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), 3. Consensus of the Ummah, 4. Analogy.
'And it includes': This is the fourth part of the commentary. Its purpose is to answer an implied question. Question: You said the first section is based on four pillars, but it includes the chapters of ijtihad and tarjih, so it seems to be built on six pillars. Answer: The chapters of tarjih and ijtihad are not new things; rather, they are subordinate to qiyas and are mentioned under it.
'And the second on three': This is the fifth part of the commentary. Its purpose is to explain the pillars of the second section: that in the second section three matters will be discussed: (1) the ruling, (2) the thing ruled upon, (3) the subject of the ruling.
'And the introduction': This is the sixth part of the commentary. Its purpose is to explain the components and contents of the introduction: that two matters will be discussed in it: (1) definition, (2) subject matter. The remaining purpose and goal will be known from the definition.
'Definition, why is knowing the subject necessary?': 'Because it is the right of the seeker' - this is the seventh part of the commentary. From here the proof is given why it is necessary to know the definition and subject matter in the introduction. Before understanding the proof, it is necessary to understand the introduction as a preamble.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, introducing the structure of usul al-fiqh as a discipline. The author opens by stating that the book comprises an introduction (muqaddima) and two sections (qismayn). The first section deals with proofs (adilla) and is based on four pillars: the Quran, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). Importantly, the commentator clarifies that chapters on ijtihad and tarjih are not independent pillars but are subsumed under qiyas. The second section covers rulings (ahkam) and has three pillars: hukm (the ruling itself), mahkum bihi (the thing upon which the ruling is applied), and mahkum alayhi (the subject of the ruling). The introduction serves to define the science and investigate its subject matter (mawdu'). The commentator then explains why definition is necessary: so that the student knows exactly what he is seeking and does not become distracted. Every science is distinguished by its definition and subject matter. The term 'usul al-fiqh' is analyzed in two senses: as a construct (idafi) meaning 'the principles of fiqh' (plural), and as a title (laqab) meaning the specific science. The author prioritizes the construct meaning because it is the original basis. The definition given is: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh.' The commentator then quotes from the commentary of Talwih to break down the text piece by piece, reinforcing the structure and addressing a potential objection about why ijtihad and tarjih are not separate pillars. The passage concludes that the title 'usul al-fiqh' is praiseworthy because it indicates the foundation on which fiqh—and hence the system of worldly life and salvation—depends.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (uṣūl al-fiqh): العلم بالقواعد التي توصل بها إلى الفقه (the knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh)
مقدمہ (muqaddima): The introduction containing definition and subject matter of the science
قسم اول (qism awwal): The first section dealing with proofs (adilla) - four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas
قسم ثانی (qism thānī): The second section dealing with rulings (ahkam) - three pillars: hukm, mahkum bihi, mahkum 'alayhi

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pillars form the first section (qism awwal) of usul al-fiqh according to this passage?
A) Two pillars: Kitab and Sunnah
B) Four pillars: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas
C) Six pillars: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas, Ijtihad, Tarjih
D) Three pillars: Hukm, Mahkum bihi, Mahkum 'alayhi

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of principles that lead to fiqh; its standard structure includes an introduction, a section on proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas), and a section on rulings (hukm, mahkum bihi, mahkum 'alayhi).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Structure of Usul al-Fiqh: Preface, Two Sections, and the Four Sources
Explaining the book's tripartite structure and defending the number of sources in the first section.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three components of a classical Hanafi usul text and explain why only four sources are listed in the first section.

Core Idea
The first section of Usul al-Fiqh is built on four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas — ijtihad and tarjih are part of qiyas.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih lays out the skeleton of a typical Hanafi usul work. The author justifies why the book is divided into a preface and two sections, and why the first section — dealing with proofs — contains exactly four sources. Understanding this structure helps you see how later discussions on ijtihad and tarjih fit into the broader framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's three components
According to the commentator, the book consists of a muqaddimah (preface) and two qisms (sections). Confirm from the text that everything else falls under these three.
The muqaddimah covers preliminary matters, the first qism deals with proofs, and the second qism deals with rulings (ahkam).
2
Understand the division of the first qism
The first qism is based on four sources (arkan): Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. Note that these are considered the primary source categories.
The text explicitly lists them as: كتاب اللہ، سنت رسول اللہ، اجماع امت، قیاس.
3
Recognize the implied objection
The commentator anticipates an objection: why are ijtihad and tarjih not listed separately, since they appear in the book? Identify this objection and the reasoning behind it.
The objector counts six components, but the commentator argues these are subsidiary to qiyas.
4
Analyze the defense
The commentator responds that ijtihad and tarjih contain nothing new (not independent) and are subsumed under qiyas. This shows a systematic approach to categorizing usul topics.
This is a typical Hanafi way of streamlining the subject: qiyas encompasses analogical reasoning, ijtihad, and preference among conflicting proofs.

شرح تلویح: قولہ اصول الفقہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ اس کتاب ( تنقیح مع توضیح ) کے ارکان کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ کہ یہ کتاب ایک مقدمہ اور دو قسموں پر مشتمل ہے۔ وجه حصر ارکان ثلاثه لان الا مذکور :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض ان ارکان ثالثہ کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا ہے کہ جو کچھ کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ۔ مقاصد کے قبیل سے ہوگا یا نہیں۔ پانی مقدمہ ہے۔ اگر اول ہے تو پھر اس کی بحث دلائل سے ہو گی۔ یا احکام سے ہوگی اگر اول ہے۔ تو قسم اول ہے اگر ثانی ہے تو قسم ثانی ہے۔ قسم الاول:۔ یہ شرح کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں قسم اول کے ارکان کو بیان کیا ہے کہ قتم اول چار ارکان پر (بنی ) ہے۔ ا۔ کتاب اللہ ۲ ۔ سنت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم -۳۔ اجماع امت ۴۔ قیاس ۔ وھو ندیل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال :۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم اول چار ارکان پرمبنی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس میں تو باب الاجتہاد اور باب الترجیح بھی بیان کیے گئے۔ ہیں ۔ گویا تم اول چھ ارکان پر بنی ہوئی۔ جواب:۔ ترجیح اور اجتہاد کے باب میں کوئی نئی چیز نہیں بلکہ قیاس کے تابع ہیں۔ اور قیاس کے ذیل میں بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔
Commentary on al-Talwih: His statement 'Usul al-Fiqh': This is the first part of the text. The commentator intends to explain the components of this book (al-Tanqih ma'a al-Tawdih). That this book consists of a preface and two sections. The reason for restricting it to three components: Everything mentioned in the book is either from the category of objectives or not. If it is from the category of objectives, then its discussion will be about proofs or rulings. If it is about proofs, it is the first section; if about rulings, it is the second section. The first section: This is the third part of the commentary. Here the components of the first section are explained: that the first section is based on four components: 1) the Book of Allah, 2) the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, 3) the consensus of the Ummah, 4) Qiyas. 'And it is a proof': This is the fourth part of the commentary. It is the answer to an implied question. Question: You said that the first section is based on four components, whereas the chapters on ijtihad and tarjih are also mentioned, so it would seem to be based on six components. Answer: The chapters on tarjih and ijtihad do not contain anything new, but are subsidiary to qiyas and are discussed under qiyas.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the book's structure. It clarifies that the book consists of a muqaddimah (preface) and two qisms (sections). The commentator argues that these three divisions cover everything in the book. The first qism deals with proofs (adilla) and is based on four sources: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. An implied question asks why ijtihad and tarjih are not counted as separate sources; the answer is that they are subsumed under qiyas. This is a typical Hanafi structuring of usul al-fiqh, where the primary sources are limited to these four.

Key Terms
مقدمہ (muqaddimah): The preface of the book, containing definition and subject matter
قسم اول (qism al-awwal): The first section, discussing proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning, a primary source of law

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They belong to the second section

Key Takeaway
The first section of a Hanafi usul text is built on four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), with ijtihad and tarjih as subsets of qiyas.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Structure of Usul al-Fiqh: The Second Section and the Preface
Parsing the structural outline of a usul text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three components of the second qism and the two components of the muqaddimah in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is defined by its subject matter and its components: hukm, mahkum bih, mahkum alayh.

This lesson unpacks the structural framework of a classic Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author divides the book into a preface (muqaddimah) and two main sections (qism). Understanding this division is the first step in grasping the entire science: the preface defines what usul al-fiqh is and what it studies, while the second section introduces the three pillars that will be analyzed in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
Recognize that the passage describes two major parts: the second qism and the muqaddimah. The second qism itself contains three matters.
The first qism is presumed to have been covered earlier.
2
List the three components of the second qism
Note that the second section deals with (1) hukm (divine ruling), (2) mahkum bih (the act or thing ruled upon), and (3) mahkum alayh (the morally responsible person).
These three are the core topics of the remainder of the book.
3
List the two components of the muqaddimah
The preface contains (1) ta'rif (definition of usul al-fiqh) and (2) mawdu' (its subject matter).
The commentator notes that the ultimate purpose (ghayyah) is understood through the definition.
4
Understand the relationship between qism and muqaddimah
The muqaddimah sets the foundation by defining the science and its subject; the second qism then elaborates on the specific elements of rulings and their application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانی علی ثلثہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض قسم ثانی کے ارکان کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ قسم ثانی میں تین امور بیان ہوں گے۔ (۱) حکم (۲) محکوم بہ (۳) محکوم عامیہ ۔ والمقدمہ: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ غرض مقدمہ کے اجزاء اور مضامین کو بیان کرنا ہے کہ اس میں دو امور بیان ہوں گے۔ (۱) تعریف۔ (۲) موضوع باقی غرض و غایت تعریف سے معلوم ہو جائے گی۔
The second is based on three: This is the fifth part of the commentary. It aims to explain the components of the second section: that in the second section three matters will be discussed: (1) hukm, (2) mahkum bih, (3) mahkum alayh. And the preface: This is the sixth part of the commentary. It aims to explain the parts and contents of the preface: that in it two matters will be discussed: (1) definition, (2) subject. Commentary
This passage continues the structural outline of the book. The second qism deals with rulings (hukm), the subject of the ruling (mahkum bih), and the person bound by the ruling (mahkum alayh). The muqaddimah contains the definition of usul al-fiqh and its subject matter (mawdu'). The commentator notes that the ultimate purpose of the science is understood through its definition. This follows the standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh structure of first defining the discipline, then classifying its contents.

Key Terms
حکم (hukm): A ruling of the Lawgiver concerning the actions of the responsible person
محکوم بہ (mahkum bih): The act or thing that is the subject of the ruling
محکوم علیہ (mahkum alayh): The morally responsible person (mukallaf)
تعریف (ta'rif): Definition of the science
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of the science

Key Takeaway
The muqaddimah defines the science and its subject, while the second qism breaks down the components of rulings into hukm, mahkum bih, and mahkum alayh.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Defining Usul al-Fiqh: Universal Rules for Deriving Rulings
Defining usul al-fiqh and clarifying its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of usul al-fiqh, distinguish it from its preliminaries (like Arabic grammar and theology), and explain its subject matter as universal propositions for deriving particular fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that directly enable deriving particular rulings from detailed evidences.

What exactly is usul al-fiqh? Is it simply a collection of proofs like the Quran and Sunnah, or is it something more—a method, a framework? In this passage from al-Talwih, the author gives a precise definition: usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules (qawaʿid) that govern how we derive rulings from the four sources. It is not the same as its preliminaries, like Arabic grammar or theology, which are necessary but not directly part of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Understand the terminology
Recognize that 'usul al-fiqh' is a label for a specific science; adding 'ilm (science) is optional unless clarity is needed.
The term itself is sufficient, like 'arak tree'—no need to say 'arak tree tree'.
2
Define a qa'ida (rule)
A qa'ida is a universal judgment that applies to its particulars, e.g., 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.'
This is the core building block of usul.
3
Distinguish immediate means from preliminaries
Identify what is directly part of usul (immediate means to fiqh) vs. what is a preliminary (mabadi') like Arabic grammar and theology.
Grammar and theology are necessary tools but not part of the science itself.
4
Identify the subject matter
The subject is universal propositions about methods of deriving rulings from the four sources and about the five legal values.
These propositions allow deriving many particular rulings without needing to know each one individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ بَعْدَ مَا تَقَرَّرَ أَنَّ أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ لَقَبٌ لِلْعِلْمِ الْمَخْصُوصِ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى إِضَافَةِ الْعِلْمِ إِلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقْصَدَ زِيَادَةُ بَيَانٍ وَتَوْضِيحٍ كَشَجَرَةِ الْأَرَاكِ وَالْقَاعِدَةُ حُكْمٌ كُلِّيٌّ يَنْطَبِقُ عَلَى جُزْئِيَّاتِهِ لِيُتَعَرَّفَ أَحْكَامُهَا مِنْهُ كَقَوْلِنَا كُلُّ حُكْمٍ دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ الْقِيَاسُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ الْقَرِيبُ مُسْتَفَادٌ مِنَ الْبَاءِ السَّبَبِيَّةِ الظَّاهِرَةِ فِي السَّبَبِ الْقَرِيبِ وَمِنْ إِطْلَاقِ التَّوَصُّلِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ، إِذْ فِي الْبَعِيدِ يُتَوَصَّلُ إِلَى الْوَاسِطَةِ وَمِنْهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ فَيَخْرُجُ الْعِلْمُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ وَالْكَلَامِ؛ لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ مَبَادِئِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ بِهِمَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ لَيْسَ بِقَرِيبٍ، إِذْ يُتَوَصَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ إِلَى مَعْرِفَةِ كَيْفِيَّةِ دَلَالَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ عَلَى مَدْلُولَاتِهَا الْوَضْعِيَّةِ وَبِوَاسِطَةِ ذَلِكَ يَقْتَدِرُ عَلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ يُتَوَصَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْكَلَامِ إِلَى ثُبُوتِ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَوُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمَا لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ. وَالتَّحْقِيقُ فِي هَذَا الْمَقَامِ أَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَمْ يُخْلَقْ عَبَثًا وَلَمْ يُتْرَكْ سُدًى، بَلْ تَعَلَّقَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ أَعْمَالِهِ حُكْمٌ مِنْ قِبَلِ الشَّارِعِ مَنُوطٌ بِدَلِيلٍ يَخُصُّهُ لِيَسْتَنْبِطَ مِنْهُ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ وَيُقَاسُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ مَا يُنَاسِبُهُ لِتَعَذُّرِ الْإِحَاطَةِ بِجَمِيعِ الْجُزْئِيَّاتِ فَحَصَلَتْ قَضَايَا مَوْضُوعَاتُهَا أَفْعَالُ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ وَمَحْمُولَاتُهَا أَحْكَامُ الشَّارِعِ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ فَسُمِّيَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا الْحَاصِلُ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِقْهًا، ثُمَّ نَظَرُوا فِي تَفَاصِيلِ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَعُمُومِهَا فَوَجَدُوا الْأَدِلَّةَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ وَالْأَحْكَامَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْوُجُوبِ وَالنَّدْبِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ وَالْكَرَاهَةِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ وَتَأَمَّلُوا فِي كَيْفِيَّةِ الِاسْتِدْلَالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَظَرٍ إِلَى تَفَاصِيلِهِمَا إِلَّا عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْمِثَالِ فَحَصَلَ لَهُمْ قَضَايَا كُلِّيَّةٌ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِكَيْفِيَّةِ الِاسْتِدْلَالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا وَبَيَانِ طُرُقِهِ وَشَرَائِطِهِ لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا إِلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ عَنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ فَضَبَطُوهَا وَدَوَّنُوهَا وَأَضَافُوا إِلَيْهَا مِنَ اللَّوَاحِقِ
And the science of usul al-fiqh, after it has been established that usul al-fiqh is a title for the specific science, there is no need to add the word 'science' to it except if increased clarity and explanation is intended, like the arak tree. And the rule (qa'ida) is a universal judgment that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it, like our saying: Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established. And the immediate means (tawassul qarib) is derived from the preposition 'bi' indicating the immediate cause, and from the unrestricted phrase 'reaching fiqh', because in the mediate means, one reaches an intermediary and from it to fiqh. Thus, knowledge of Arabic grammar and theology is excluded, because they are from the preliminaries (mabadi') of usul al-fiqh, and reaching fiqh through them is not immediate. For by Arabic grammar one reaches knowledge of how words indicate their conventional meanings, and by that means one becomes able to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, by theology one reaches the establishment of the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness, in order to reach fiqh through that. The verification in this context is that man was not created in vain nor left neglected. Rather, each of his actions is attached a ruling from the Lawgiver, dependent on a specific evidence, so that he may derive it when needed, and analogize to that ruling what is suitable, due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars. Thus, propositions emerged whose subjects are the acts of the legally responsible and whose predicates are the rulings of the Lawgiver in detail. The knowledge obtained from those evidences was called fiqh. Then they examined the details of those evidences and rulings and their generality, and found that the evidences reduce to the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and qiyas, and the rulings reduce to obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, and permission. They contemplated the method of inferring those rulings from those evidences in a general way, without looking at their details except by way of example. So they obtained universal propositions related to the method of inferring those rulings from those evidences in general, and the explanation of its methods and conditions, in order to use each of those propositions to derive many of those particular rulings from their detailed evidences. So they recorded and compiled them and added to them appendices.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage from al-Talwih provides a comprehensive definition of usul al-fiqh as a science. It begins by noting that the term 'usul al-fiqh' is sufficient as a label, and adding 'ilm (science) is only for clarity. It then defines a qa'ida (rule) as a universal judgment applied to particulars, giving the example: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.' The author distinguishes between immediate means (tawassul qarib) and mediate means (tawassul ba'id) to reach fiqh. Arabic grammar and theology are classified as preliminaries (mabadi') because they do not directly lead to fiqh but through intermediaries. The core of usul al-fiqh is the universal propositions about the methods of deriving rulings from the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, consensus, qiyas) and the five legal values (obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, permissibility). The science was developed because humans cannot know every ruling individually, so they rely on these universal principles to derive particular rulings from detailed evidences.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qāʿida): A universal judgment (hukm kulli) that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it.
التوصل القريب (al-tawassul al-qarīb): The immediate means of reaching fiqh, without an intermediary, as with the direct application of usul al-fiqh propositions.
مبادىء أصول الفقه (mabādiʾ uṣūl al-fiqh): The preliminary sciences (like Arabic grammar and theology) that are not part of usul al-fiqh but are necessary for it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the immediate means (tawassul qarib) from the mediate means?
A) Immediate means does not require any prior knowledge.
B) Immediate means directly yields fiqh rulings without intermediaries.
C) Immediate means is derived from the Book and Sunnah only.
D) Immediate means refers to the use of qiyas only.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules (qawa'id) that directly govern the derivation of particular fiqh rulings from detailed evidences, excluding its preliminaries.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Why 'tawassul' is restricted to qarīb in the definition of Usul al-Fiqh
Justification for restricting 'tawassul' to immediate means in the definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and state the two qarīnahs that justify restricting tawassul to qarīb in the Hanafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh, and explain why remote means are excluded.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is defined as the means that directly reach fiqh – intermediary sciences are excluded because they do not yield rulings immediately.

In this short but crucial passage, the commentator of Al-Talwīḥ clarifies why the definition of Usul al-Fiqh specifies 'tawassul qarīb' (near means) rather than just 'tawassul'. The matn's broader term is narrowed by two linguistic and contextual indicators. Understanding this narrowing is essential for grasping the precise scope of the discipline: only those tools that directly enable the derivation of rulings from the primary sources qualify as usul al-fiqh. Sciences like Arabic grammar or kalam, while helpful, are not part of usul because they do not directly yield fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Implicit Objection
The matn defines usul as 'al-tawassul' (the means) absolutely. The commentator restricts it to 'qarīb'. The passage begins by noting this is an answer to an implied question: why the restriction? You should first identify that the commentator is resolving an apparent ambiguity.
The question might arise: why not include all sciences that help in understanding fiqh?
2
Analyze the First Qarīnah (Pronoun 'hā')
The object of tawassul is mentioned with the pronoun 'hā' referring to 'ahkām' (rulings). Since the pronoun directly refers to the rulings, it indicates that the means (sabab) is proximate – it reaches the rulings directly. A remote means would require an intermediary object.
This linguistic analysis uses the principle that a pronoun implies direct reference.
3
Analyze the Second Qarīnah (Idāfah to Fiqh)
The phrase 'tawassul ilā al-fiqh' (means to fiqh) uses a genitive construction that implies direct arrival. Literally, it means 'the means of reaching fiqh.' If the means were remote, it would reach something else first, and then fiqh. The idāfah stipulates immediate connection.
Compare: 'sabīl al-ḥajj' (path to Hajj) implies a direct route.
4
Distinguish Near vs Remote Means
Based on these qarīnahs, 'tawassul qarīb' means that usul al-fiqh itself gives you the ruling directly from the sources. 'Tawassul baʿīd' would be something like Arabic grammar: mastering grammar helps you understand the Qur'an, but it doesn't directly produce a fiqh ruling; you still need usul al-fiqh to derive that ruling.
Thus, grammar is a remote means and is not part of usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply to a Concrete Example
Consider the ruling 'Prayer is obligatory.' Usul al-fiqh directly uses the command 'aqimū al-ṣalāh' and principles of command to deduce wujub. Arabic grammar helps interpret 'aqimū' as imperative, but grammar is not the source of the ruling – it's an auxiliary tool. Hence, grammar is tawassul baʿīd, not qarīb.
This shows why the definition is precise: only the direct means count as usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتوصل القریب :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت سے شاریخ نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ متن کی تعریف میں مطلقا توصل کی قید ہے اور آپ نے توصل سے توصل قریب مراد لیا ہے اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ جواب:- شاریخ نے کہا کہ توصل قریب مراد لینے پر دو قرینے ہیں (۱) توصل کا صلہ (ہا) ذکر کیا ہے اور باسہیہ ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ سبب سے مراد سبب قریب ہے کیونکہ سبب قریب اصل ہے اور سبب بعید اس کی فرع ہے (۲) دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ توصل کی اضافت کی گئی ہے فقہ کی طرف توصل الیہ الی الی الفقہ کہ فقہ تک پہنچائے یعنی بلا واسطہ پہنچائے تو یہ تو صل قریب ہوا کیونکہ توصل بعید تو پہلے واسطہ کی طرف پہنچائے گا پھر واسطہ سے فقہ کی طرف پہنچائے گا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ توصل قریب میں توصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے اور توصل بعید میں توصل الی الفقہ نہیں ہوتا۔
And 'near means' (al-tawassul al-qarīb): This is the third part of the commentary's phrase. With this phrase, the commentator answers an implied question: The definition in the matn mentions 'tawassul' absolutely, but you (the commentator) take 'tawassul' as meaning 'near means' (tawassul qarīb). What is the reason? The commentator says there are two indicators for taking 'near means': (1) The object of 'tawassul' is mentioned with the pronoun 'hā', so it is clear that by 'sabab' (means) what is meant is 'qarīb' (near), because the near cause is original and the remote cause is a branch. (2) The second proof is that 'tawassul' is genitively attached to 'fiqh' — it reaches fiqh, meaning it reaches without an intermediary. So this is near means, because remote means would first reach an intermediary and then through that intermediary reach fiqh. The summary is that in near means, there is direct reaching of fiqh, but in remote means there is no direct reaching of fiqh.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential ambiguity in the definition of usul al-fiqh: why is 'tawassul' (means) qualified as 'qarīb' (near/immediate)? The commentator provides two rational arguments. First, the object of 'tawassul' is expressed with the suffix 'hā' referring to 'ahkām' (rulings), implying the cause is proximate. Second, the idāfah (construct) 'tawassul ilā al-fiqh' indicates direct arrival at fiqh without intermediary steps. This distinction is crucial because many sciences (like Arabic grammar or kalām) lead to fiqh only indirectly. Usul al-fiqh directly enables deduction of rulings from the primary sources.

Key Terms
توسل قریب (tawassul qarīb): A means that directly reaches the end (fiqh) without intermediaries.
توسل بعید (tawassul ba'īd): A means that reaches the end only through an intermediate step.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is 'tawassul' restricted to 'qarīb' (near means) in the definition of usul al-fiqh according to this passage?
A) Because remote means are invalid for deriving rulings
B) Because the object of tawassul is mentioned with the pronoun 'hā', indicating a near cause
C) Because usul al-fiqh excludes all intermediary sciences
D) Because the matn explicitly says 'near means'

Key Takeaway
The definition of Usul al-Fiqh is narrowed to 'near means' via two linguistic indicators, ensuring that only the direct tools for deriving rulings are included, not auxiliary sciences.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Defining Usul al-Fiqh: Only Direct Means to Fiqh
Clarifying that Arabic linguistics and kalam are not part of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Arabic linguistic sciences (sarf, nahw) and kalam (theology) are excluded from the definition of usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi method.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is only the methodology that DIRECTLY leads to fiqh rulings from sources.

This passage refines the definition of usul al-fiqh by clarifying what it does NOT include. While Arabic grammar and theology are essential prerequisites, they do not themselves constitute usul because they require an extra step to reach fiqh. Understanding this boundary prevents confusion between foundational sciences and the distinct discipline of usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restriction
The passage discusses a restriction ('qayd') in the definition of usul al-fiqh. Determine what this restriction is—the condition that 'tawassul' (the means to reach fiqh) must be direct (qarib).
The term 'tawassul' is key.
2
Understand the excluded sciences
List the sciences explicitly excluded: Arabic sciences (sarf, nahw) and kalam (theology). They are not part of usul.
These are often mistakenly considered part of usul by beginners.
3
Explain the indirectness of Arabic sciences
Arabic sciences only clarify how words indicate lexical meanings (dalalat wad'iyyah). That understanding is a prerequisite, but it does not directly give fiqh rulings. An additional step (istinbat using usul principles) is needed.
Thus Arabic sciences are 'tawassul bi al-wasitah'—indirect.
4
Explain the indirectness of kalam
Kalam proves the authenticity (thubut) of the Quran and Sunnah. However, even after establishing that the sources are revealed, one still needs usul to derive rulings from those sources. So kalam is also indirect.
Kalam is a prerequisite for the authority of the sources, not for derivation.
5
Conclude the definition
Only a science that directly and immediately leads from scriptural sources to fiqh rulings qualifies as usul al-fiqh. Everything else is a separate, supporting discipline.
This exclusion helps keep usul focused on its unique methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فیچر ج العلم : ۔ یہ عبارت شرح کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شارع فوائد قیود کی طرف اشارہ کرنا ہے توصل کی قید سے علوم عربیہ مثلا صرف و نحو اور علم کلام وغیرہ خارج ہو نگے کیونکہ ان سے فقہ تک توصل حاصل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ ان علوم عربیہ سے پہلے توصل ہوتا ہے کہ الفاظ کی مدلولات وضعیہ پر دلالت کی کیفیت کیا ہے؟ پھر اس کے واسطہ سے فقہ تک توصل ہوتا ہے یعنی پھر کتاب و سنت سے احکام کے استنباط پر قدرت حاصل ہوتی ہے تو ان میں توصل بالواسطہ ہوتا ہے بلا واسطہ نہیں ہوتا اور علم کلام سے توصل ہوتا ہے کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت رسول اللہ سے ثابت ہیں یا نہیں یعنی دلائل کے ثبوت کی طرف پھر اس کے واسطہ سے فقہ کی طرف توصل ہوتا ہے تو یہ توصل بھی بالواسطہ ہے نہ کہ بلا واسطہ۔
The benefit of the restriction: This is the fourth part of the commentary's phrase. The aim is to indicate the benefits of the restrictions. The restriction of 'tawassul' excludes Arabic sciences such as morphology and syntax (sarf wa nahw) and kalam (theology), because from them, reaching fiqh is not achieved directly. Because from these Arabic sciences, first there is reaching (tawassul) regarding how words indicate their lexical meanings; then through that intermediary, reaching to fiqh occurs — that is, one attains the ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. So in these, the means is indirect, not direct. And from kalam, there is reaching (tawassul) to whether the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger are established — that is, to the proofs of their authenticity — then through that intermediary, reaching to fiqh occurs. So these means are also indirect, not direct.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage explains the practical implication of restricting 'tawassul' to 'qarīb' (direct means). Sciences like Arabic grammar (sarf, nahw) and theology (kalam) are not part of usul al-fiqh because they do not directly lead to fiqh rulings. Grammar helps understand the meaning of words, but that understanding still needs a further step to extract legal rules from the sources. Similarly, kalam establishes the authenticity of revelation, but does not itself yield fiqh rulings. Only the methodology that directly takes one from the sources to specific rulings qualifies as usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
علوم عربیہ (ulum arabiyyah): Sciences of the Arabic language, such as morphology (sarf) and syntax (nahw).
علم کلام (ilm al-kalam): Theology that discusses the proofs for the truth of Islam and the authenticity of revelation.
توصل بالواسطہ (tawassul bi al-wasitah): Indirect means requiring an intermediary step before reaching fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why are Arabic sciences (sarf, nahw) excluded from the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) They are not useful for fiqh
B) They only lead to understanding word meanings, not directly to fiqh rulings
C) They are considered part of fiqh itself
D) They are too detailed for usul al-fiqh

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh includes only the methodology that directly yields fiqh rulings from the sources, not its prerequisite sciences.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Necessity and Definition of Fiqh
Explaining why fiqh is needed and defining it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of fiqh as knowledge of universal propositions and explain why fiqh is necessary for human action.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of universal rulings on actions, each tied to a specific proof.

This passage establishes the fundamental purpose of fiqh: mankind is created for actions, and every action carries a ruling from Allah. Fiqh is not a random collection of laws but a systematic knowledge of universal propositions linking actions to rulings. The passage contrasts this with the need for specific proofs for each ruling, setting the stage for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of creation
Understand that humans were created for actions, not idleness. Every action has a corresponding ruling from the Shari'ah.
This is the premise: actions are the locus of rulings.
2
Recognize the connection between actions and rulings
Each ruling (hukm) has a specific proof (dalil). Rulings are not derived from a single proof but from individual proofs tailored to each act.
This justifies the need for multiple proofs and a methodology to link them.
3
Define fiqh as universal propositions
Fiqh is the knowledge of universal propositions (qadaya kulliyyah) where the subject is the action of the mukallaf and the predicate is a ruling (e.g., Zina is haram).
The example 'zina is haram' illustrates: subject = action of zina, predicate = haram.
4
Contrast fiqh with specific fatwas
Fiqh is not about isolated cases but general principles that apply to all instances within a category.
This sets fiqh apart from case-by-case fatwas.

فعل اور محمول احکام میں سے کوئی حکم ہے جن کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے تو پھر علماء نے غور کیا کہ احکام کتنے ہیں؟ تو معلوم ہوا کہ احکام کل چھ ہیں واجب ، مستحب ، مباح حرام، مکروہ تحریمی اور مکروہ تنزیہی اور ان کے دلائل میں غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ دلائل کل چار ہیں کتاب وسنت اور اجماع اور قیاس پھر غور کیا کہ یہ احکام دلائل اربعہ سے کیسے ثابت ہوتے ہیں ؟ اولہ کی احکام پر دلالت کی کیفیت کیا ہے؟ اب سوچا کہ
