کا ۔ ولفظ القواعد: ماقبل میں یہ بیان کیا کہ علماء کو ایسے قضا یا وقواعد حاصل ہوئے کہ جن سے اجمالاً کیفیت استدلال حاصل ہوتی ہے یہ اجمال کی قید اس لئے ہے کیونکہ تعریف میں لفظ قواعد کا ہے اور قواعد میں احکام کو اجمالاً ذکر کیا جاتا ہے ان میں
And the investigation (al-tahqīq): This is the fifth part of the commentary's phrase. The aim is to explain the necessity of fiqh. Its summary is that man was not created in vain, but for actions. Every action is associated with a ruling (hukm). And for every ruling there is a separate proof (dalīl), because it is difficult for all rulings to be derived from a single proof. So each ruling has its specific proof, so that when needed, the ruling can be derived from that proof, and appropriate rulings can be analogized (qiyās) to it. Now, upon reflection, universal propositions (qaḍāyā) were found whose subject is the action of the obligated person (mukallaf) and whose predicate is one of the rulings. For example, 'Zina is harām' is a proposition: the action of the mukallaf (zina) is harām. This ruling (harām) is established from the Book of Allah. Similarly, 'Salat is fard', 'Zakat is fard' — these are rulings of wajib or harām on the action of the mukallaf. Now, knowledge of such universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and whose predicate is one of the rulings is called fiqh. 'Then they considered' (thumma nazharū): This is the sixth part of the commentary's phrase. The commentator explains the necessity of usul al-fiqh. When in fiqh such rules (qawā‘id) were obtained whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and predicate is one of the rulings — the knowledge of which is called fiqh — then scholars pondered: How many rulings are there? They found that rulings are six: wājib, mustahabb, mubāḥ, harām, makrūh tahrīmī, and makrūh tanzīhī. They considered their proofs (adillah) and found they are four: the Book, Sunnah, Ijmā‘, and Qiyās. Then they considered how these rulings are established from the four proofs — what is the manner of their indication (dalālah) of the rulings? They asked: What are the conditions (shurūṭ) and methods (ṭuruq) for the rulings? Then such rules were obtained by which the manner of deriving rulings from the four proofs and the conditions and methods are known. Scholars collected these rules, codified them, and along with them mentioned their corollaries (lawāḥiq) and completions (mutammimāt), and stated the disagreements. The knowledge derived from these rules was named 'usul al-fiqh'. Now usul al-fiqh is the name of 'knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh'. And the word 'qawā‘id': earlier it was explained that scholars obtained such universal propositions and rules by which the manner of inference (kayfiyyat al-istidlāl) is known in brief (ijmālan). The qualification 'ijmālan' is because the definition includes the word 'qawā‘id', and in rules, rulings are mentioned briefly.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage explains the foundational necessity of fiqh and how usul al-fiqh emerged. Humans are created for actions, and each action has a ruling from the divine law. These rulings are derived from specific proofs (Quran, Sunnah, etc.). Fiqh is defined as knowledge of universal propositions where the subject is the mukallaf's action and the predicate is a ruling (e.g., 'Zina is haram'). Later, scholars systematically investigated the number and types of rulings (six), the sources of proof (four), and the methods of derivation. This led to the formulation of general rules (qawā‘id) that facilitate deriving rulings from the primary sources. These collected rules, along with their details and disputes, constitute the science of usul al-fiqh. The passage emphasizes that these rules are presented in a concise manner (ijmāl) because they are general principles, not detailed rulings.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and whose predicate is one of the rulings (wājib, harām, etc.).
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): Knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh (derives rulings from the four proofs).
قضایا کلیہ (qadaya kulliyyah): Universal propositions that apply to all instances of a category (e.g., 'All acts of worship are to be performed with intention').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of fiqh?
A) Knowledge of specific rulings for particular actions
B) Knowledge of universal propositions whose subject is the mukallaf's action and predicate is a ruling
C) Knowledge of the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas)
D) Knowledge of the six types of rulings

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is the knowledge of universal rulings on actions, derived from specific proofs.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Emergence of Usul al-Fiqh
Explaining the origin and formulation of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the scholarly process that led to the formulation of usul al-fiqh as the methodology for deriving rulings from the four proofs.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the codified methodology for deriving rulings from the four proofs.

After fiqh itself was recognized as a body of universal propositions, scholars investigated further: How many types of rulings are there? What are the proofs? How do proofs indicate rulings? This inquiry produced the rules (qawā'id) of derivation, which were then compiled into the discipline of usul al-fiqh. The passage describes this systematic reflection.

Guided Path
1
Recognize that fiqh consists of universal propositions
Scholars first had the raw material of fiqh: universal propositions linking actions to rulings.
This was the starting point for deeper investigation.
2
Identify the six types of rulings (ahkām)
Scholars determined that rulings are of six kinds: wājib, mustahabb, mubāḥ, harām, makrūh tahrīmī, and makrūh tanzīhī.
This classification is essential for understanding the scope of fiqh.
3
Identify the four proofs (adillah)
They found that rulings are derived from four primary sources: the Book, Sunnah, Ijmā‘, and Qiyās.
These are the agreed-upon sources in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the role of qawā‘id in usul al-fiqh
Scholars formulated general rules (qawā‘id) that explain how proofs indicate rulings, including conditions and methods. These rules, collected and codified, constitute usul al-fiqh.
The rules are presented concisely (ijmāl) because they are general principles.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Definition and Necessity of Fiqh and Usul al-Fiqh
Commentary defining fiqh and usul al-fiqh and their necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fiqh and usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school, explain their necessity, and apply the definition to classify propositions.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of universal propositions about actions; usul al-fiqh is the tool to derive that knowledge.

This passage from a classical commentary establishes the foundation of the Islamic legal tradition. It begins by justifying why fiqh is necessary—humans are created for actions, and every action requires a ruling derived from specific proofs. It then precisely defines fiqh as knowledge of universal propositions whose subject is the mukallaf's act and predicate is one of the six shar'i rulings. The passage then shows how scholars, after mastering fiqh, turned to study the proofs and the method of derivation, leading to the discipline of usul al-fiqh. Finally, it refines the definition by addressing an objection about the scope of usul al-fiqh, confirming that it is a tool exclusively for the mujtahid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the necessity of fiqh
The passage argues that humans are created for actions, and each action has a ruling. Fiqh is needed to know these rulings. This step frames fiqh as a practical necessity.
Contrast with the idea that fiqh is purely theoretical.
2
Extract the definition of fiqh
Look for the sentence: 'Now, knowledge of such universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and whose predicate is one of the rulings is called fiqh.' This defines fiqh precisely.
The definition emphasizes 'universal propositions' (qadaya kulliyya) – not just individual rulings.
3
Understand the six rulings and four proofs
Scholars found that rulings are six (wajib, mustahabb, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) and proofs are four (Qur'an, Sunnah, ijma', qiyas). This sets the scope of fiqh and usul.
These numbers are foundational in Hanafi usul.
4
Define usul al-fiqh
After gathering the rules for deriving rulings from proofs, scholars named the body of those rules 'usul al-fiqh'. The definition: 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh.'
Note that usul al-fiqh is a meta-discipline – it does not contain rulings, but tools to derive them.
5
Analyze the objection and response
An objector claims the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq is redundant. The commentator answers that it excludes the science of debate, which might be confused with fiqh. This clarifies the boundaries of usul.
This shows the rigorous analytical method of the Hanafi school.

وزاد: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے مصنف نے علی وجہ تحقیق کی قید لگائی علم مناظرہ وعلم جدل وغیرہ کو خارج کرنے کیلئے۔
ولقائل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ اعتراض کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض: ۔ یہ ہے کہ علی وجہ التحقیق کی قید کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ توصل سے توصل قریب مراد ہے اور علم مناظرہ سے توصل بعید ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جدلی یا تو اپنے حکم اور اصل کی حفاظت کرے گا یا مخالف کے حکم کو توڑے گا پھر اس کے بعد فقہ تک توصل ہوگا تو علم خلاف سے جب توصل بعید ہوتا ہے تو علی وجہ التحقیق کی ضرورت ہی نہیں تھی کیونکہ علم خلاف تو توصل کی قید ہی سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔
جواب: ٹھیک ہے تو صل قریب سے علم جدل و مناظرہ نکل گیا لیکن علم مناظرہ میں فقہ کے مسائل اتنی کثرت سے ہوتے ہیں کہ و ہم ہونے لگا ہے کہ شاید یہ فقہ میں داخل ہیں تو قید لگائی کہ یہ فقہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں۔
ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ أَنَّ كُلَّ دَلِيلٍ مِنَ الأدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ إِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ بِهِ الْحُكْمُ إِذَا كَانَ. مُشْتَمِلا عَلَى شَرَائِط تُذْكَرُ فِي مَوْضِعِهَا ، وَلَا يَكُونُ الدَّلِيلُ مَنْسُوحًا ، وَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ مُعَارِضٌ مُسَاوِ أَوْ رَاجِحٌ . وَيَكُونُ الْقِيَاسُ قَدْ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأَى مُجْتَهِدٍ حَتَّى لَوُ خَالَفَ إِجْمَاعَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ يَكُونُ بَاطِلا فَالْقَضِيَّةُ الْمَذْكُورَةُ سَوَاءٌ جَعَلْنَاهَا كُبْرَى أَوْ مُلازِمَةً إِنْمَا تَصُدُقُ كُلِّيَّةٌ إذَا اشْتَمَلَتْ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْقُيُودِ فَالْعِلْمُ بِالْمَبَاحِثِ المُتَعَلَّقَةِ بِهَذِهِ الْقُيُودِ يَكُونُ عِلْمًا بِالْقَضِيَّةِ الكُليّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ إحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَى الدَّلِيل عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ فَتَكُونُ تِلْكَ الْمَبَاحِتُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَقَوْلُنَا يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَيْهِ . الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّ هَذَا يَخْتَصُّ بِالْمُجْتَهِدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَبْحُوتَ عَنْهُ فِى هَذَا الْعِلْمِ قَوَاعِدُ يَتَوَصَّلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ فَإِنَّ الْمُتَوَصِّلَ إلَى الْفِقْهِ لَيْسَ إِلَّا الْمُجْتَهِدُ فَإِنَّ الْفِقْهَ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالأحْكامِ مِنَ الأدِلَّةِ الَّتِي لَيْسَ دَلِيلُ الْمُقَلِّدِ مِنْهَا فَلِهَذَا لَمْ
Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ: From Sunnah, ability to derive rulings occurs, but in them, access is indirect, not direct. And from kalām, access occurs to whether they are established from the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah or not, i.e., towards the proofs' establishment, then through that, access to fiqh occurs. So this access is also indirect, not direct. Necessity of fiqh. And al-taḥqīq: This is the fifth part of the commentator's expression. The aim is to explain the necessity of fiqh, the outcome of which is that man was not created idle but for actions, and every action has a ruling attached, and every ruling has a separate proof, because deriving all rulings from one proof is difficult. Thus, each ruling has a specific proof so that at the time of need, the ruling can be derived from that proof, and similar rulings can be analogized to it. Now, when considered, such universal propositions are known whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and predicate is one of the rulings. For example, 'fornication is forbidden' is a proposition: the action of the mukallaf, fornication, is forbidden; this is the ruling of forbiddance, established from the Book of Allah. Prayer is obligatory, zakāt is obligatory. This being wajib or haram for the action of the mukallaf is the ruling. Now, knowledge of such universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and whose predicate is one of the rulings is called fiqh. 'Thumma naẓarū' (then they looked): This is the sixth part of the commentator's expression. The commentator explained the necessity of uṣūl al-fiqh: When such rules were attained in fiqh whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and predicate is one of the rulings, the knowledge of which is fiqh, then the scholars looked: How many rulings are there? It became known that rulings are six: wājib, mustaḥabb, mubāḥ, ḥarām, makrūh taḥrīmī, and makrūh tanzīhī. And they looked at their proofs; it became known that proofs are four: Book, Sunnah, ijmāʿ, and qiyās. Then they looked: How are these rulings established from the four proofs? What is the manner of their indication of rulings? Then they thought: What are the conditions and methods for rulings? Then such rules were attained by which the manner and conditions of deriving rulings from the four proofs are known, and the methods are known. So the scholars collected these rules, codified them, mentioned their appendices and completions, and explained differences. The knowledge obtained from these rules is named uṣūl al-fiqh. Thus uṣūl al-fiqh is the name for 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh.' And the word 'al-qawāʿid': earlier it was stated that the scholars attained such propositions and rules from which the manner of inference is obtained in summary. This qualification of summary is because the definition has the word 'rules', and in rules, rulings are mentioned summarily; details are not mentioned. So the word 'rules' itself indicates summary. 'Wa zād' (and he added): This is the seventh part of the commentator's expression. The author added the restriction 'alā wajh al-taḥqīq' to exclude the science of debate and argumentation. 'Wa liqā'il' (and for one who says): This is the last part of the commentator's expression. The aim is to raise an objection and answer it. Objection: The restriction 'alā wajh al-taḥqīq' is unnecessary because 'tawassul' here means close access, and from the science of debate, access is distant, because the debater either defends his own ruling and principle or breaks the opponent's ruling; then after that, access to fiqh occurs. So when from the science of disagreement, access is distant, the restriction 'alā wajh al-taḥqīq' was not needed, because the science of disagreement is excluded by the condition 'tawassul' itself. Answer: True, close access excludes debate and argumentation, but in the science of debate, issues of fiqh occur so frequently that suspicion arises that they might be included in fiqh. So the restriction was added that they are not included in fiqh. Then know: Every proof from the legal proofs only establishes the ruling when it includes conditions mentioned in their place, the proof is not abrogated, and it has no counter-proof equal or preponderant, and qiyās has led to it by the opinion of a mujtahid, such that if it contradicts the consensus of mujtahids, it is void. So the mentioned proposition, whether we make it a major premise or a concomitant, is only true universally when it includes these restrictions. Thus, knowledge of the inquiries related to these restrictions is knowledge of the universal proposition which is one of the two premises of the proof for issues of fiqh. Therefore, those inquiries are among the issues of uṣūl al-fiqh. And our statement 'by it one arrives at it' apparently is specific to the mujtahid, for what is investigated in this science are rules by which the mujtahid arrives at fiqh, since the one who arrives at fiqh is none other than the mujtahid, for fiqh is knowledge of rulings from proofs that are not from the proof of the muqallid. Thus, this is why...
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the definition and necessity of fiqh and usul al-fiqh. The commentator first justifies the necessity of fiqh: humans are created for actions, each action has a ruling, and each ruling requires a specific proof because deriving all rulings from one proof is impractical. Fiqh is then defined as knowledge of universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and whose predicate is one of the six shar‘i rulings (wajib, mustahabb, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi). The passage then explains that scholars, after establishing fiqh, examined the rulings and found them to be six, and the proofs to be four (Qur’an, Sunnah, ijma‘, qiyas). They then investigated how these proofs indicate rulings, leading to the formation of rules for derivation. These rules were collected and codified as usul al-fiqh, defined as knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh. The commentator then addresses an objection about the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq (on the basis of verification), explaining that it is needed to exclude the science of debate and argumentation, which might be confused with fiqh due to their frequent mention of fiqhi issues. The final Arabic passage emphasizes that a legal proof only establishes a ruling if it meets conditions (not abrogated, no equal or preponderant counter-proof, qiyas based on mujtahid’s opinion, not contradicting ijma‘), and that these conditions are studied in usul al-fiqh. The commentator also clarifies that usul al-fiqh is specifically for the mujtahid, not for the muqallid, since fiqh itself is knowledge derived from proofs that a muqallid does not possess.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of universal propositions whose subject is the action of the mukallaf and predicate is one of the six shar‘i rulings.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): Knowledge of the rules by which the mujtahid arrives at fiqh from the four proofs.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who is able to derive fiqh rulings directly from proofs using the tools of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for the necessity of fiqh?
A) Because every action has a specific legal ruling that must be known.
B) Because the Prophet commanded seeking knowledge.
C) Because usul al-fiqh cannot function without fiqh.
D) Because scholars needed to write books.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is the systematic knowledge of universal propositions about Islamic rulings, and usul al-fiqh provides the methodological tools to derive that knowledge from sources.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh: Evidences and Rulings
Defines subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh and distinguish between the essential attributes of evidences and rulings.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh studies both evidences AND rulings, focusing on how each relates to the other.

Every science is defined by its subject. This passage from a classical Hanafi usul text clarifies exactly what Usul al-Fiqh investigates: the Shar'i evidences and the rulings they produce. It is not enough to study one without the other; the essential accidents (awarid dhatiyya) of each—how evidences prove rulings and how rulings depend on evidences—are what make this discipline distinct from Fiqh itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two elements
The passage states that the subject includes both al-adilla al-shar'iyya (evidences) and al-ahkam al-shar'iyya (rulings).
Don't confuse with Fiqh, which studies the rulings themselves.
2
Understand 'essential accidents'
The phrase al-awarid al-dhatiyya refers to intrinsic properties: for evidences, it is their capacity to establish rulings; for rulings, it is their being established by evidences.
This is what distinguishes Usul from other sciences.
3
Recognize the bidirectional relation
The text emphasizes that evidence are 'producers' of rulings, and rulings are 'products' of evidence. This interdependence is the core of Usul.
Some scholars mistakenly think Usul only covers evidence.
4
Apply the definition
Given a sample issue, determine whether it belongs to Usul al-Fiqh or Fiqh by checking if it deals with the essential properties of evidence/ruling relation.
For example, 'Is this prayer valid?' is Fiqh; 'What type of evidence proves its validity?' is Usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَمَوْضُوعُ هَذَا العِلم الأدلّة الشَّرْعِيَّةُ وَالْأحْكَامُ إِذْ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ الْعَوَارِضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ لِلْأدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَهِيَ إثباتُهَا لِلْأحْكامِ وَعَنْ الْعَوَارِضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ لِلْأحْكامِ وَهِيَ ثُبُوتُهَا بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ.
ترجمہ : یہ جسے ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ یہ دلیل کی طرف دیکھتے ہوئے ہے ۔ بہر حال مدلول کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے بیشک قضیہ مذکورہ سوائے اس کے نہیں ہوگا اس کا ثابت کرنا کلی طور پر جبکہ پہچانی جائیں حکم کی اقسام اور یہ بات کہ بیشک احکام کی کونسی قسم ادلہ کی کونسی قسم سے ثابت ہے ایسی خصوصیت کیسا تھ جو پیدا ہونے والی ہے حکم سے مثل ہونا شے کا علت اس کے لئے۔ کیونکہ یہ حکم کہ نہیں ہے ممکن اس کو ثابت کرنا قیاس کیا تھ ۔ بلکہ نص کیساتھ ۔ پھر وہ مباحث جن کا تعلق محکوم یہ سے ہے اور وہ فعل مکلف ہے مثل ہونا اس کا عبادت یا عقوبت اور اس کی مثل ان میں سے جو داخل ہوتی ہیں اس قضیہ کے کلیہ ہونے میں پس بے شک مکلفین کے افعال کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے احکام مختلف ہو جاتے ہیں کیونکہ عقوبات کو قیاس سے ثابت کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پھر وہ مباحث جن کا تعلق محکوم علیہ سے ہے اور وہ مکلف ہے اور اہلیت کا پہچاننا اور وہ عوارض جو پیش آتے ہیں اہلیت پر سماوی ہوں یا کسی ہوں وہ بھی اسی قضیہ کلیہ کے تحت مندرج ہیں بوجہ مختلف ہونے احکام کے محکوم علیہ کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور نظر کرتے ہوئے عوارض کے وجود اور عدم وجود کی طرف۔ پس ہو گا دلیل کو مرکب کرنا مسائل فقہ کو ثابت کرنے پر شکل اول کے ذریعہ سے اس طرح هذا الحكم ثابت لانه حكم هذا شانه متعلق بفعل هذا شانه هذا الفعل صادر من مكلف هذا شانه ولم توجد العوارض المانعة من ثبوت هذا الحكم ويدل على ثبوت هذا الحكم قياس هذا شانه هہ صغریٰ ہے پھر کبری ہمارا یہ قول ہے وکل حکم موصوف بالصفات المذكوره يدل على ثبوته القياس الموصوف فهو ثابت پس یہ قضیہ اخیرہ اصول فقہ کے مسائل میں سے ہے اور ملازمہ کلیہ کے طریقہ پر اس طرح ۔ کلما وجد قیاس موصوف بهذه الصفات ثبت ذلك الحكم لكنه وجد القياس الموصوف وجدا الخ ۔۔۔۔۔ پس جان لیا گیا کہ بیشک تمام وہ مباحث جو مقدم ہیں وہ داخل ہیں اس قضیہ کلیہ مذکورہ کے تحت جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک ہوتا ہے مسائل فقہ پر ۔ پس یہی معنی ہے مذکورہ تو صل قریب کا پس جب جان لیا گیا کہ بیشک اصول فقہ کے مسائل لوٹنے والے ہیں ہمارے قول کل حکم کذایدل علی ثبوته دلیل کذا فهو ثابت یا کلما وجد دلیل کند ادال علی حکم کذا ثبت ذلک الحکم کی طرف ۔ تو معلوم ہوگی یہ بات کہ بیشک بحث کی جاتی ہے اس علم میں ادلہ شرعیہ اور احکام شرعیہ دونوں سے اس حیثیت سے کہ اولی (ادلہ ) منت ہیں ثانیہ (احکام) کے لئے اور ثانیہ (احکام ) ثابت ہیں اولی (ادلہ ) کیسا تھ ۔ اور وہ مباحث جو لوٹتی ہیں اس بات کی طرف کہ اول مثبت ہے دوسرے کے لئے اور دوسرا ثابت ہے اول سے بعض پیدا ہونے والے ہیں دلائل سے اور بعض مباحث ناشی ہیں احکام سے پس اس علم کا موضوع ادلہ شرعیہ اور احکام ہیں کیونکہ بحث کی جاتی ہیں اس میں ادلہ شرعیہ کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے اور وہ ادلہ کا ثابت کرتا ہے احکام کو اور احکام کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے اور وہ احکام کا ثابت ہونا ہے ان ادلہ سے۔
So the subject of this science is the Shar'i evidences and the rulings, for inquiry is made in it about the essential accidents of the Shar'i evidences, which are their establishment of the rulings, and about the essential accidents of the rulings, which are their being established by those evidences.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh. The author states that it deals with two things: (1) Shar'i evidences (adillah) and their essential attributes, particularly how they prove rulings; (2) Shar'i rulings (ahkam) and their essential attributes, particularly how they are proven by evidences. The Urdu commentary expands: the general proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) that underlies all fiqh issues is about linking rulings to evidences via analogy (qiyas). It then explains that the conditions for this proposition involve knowing the types of rulings, the act of the mukallaf (mahkum bih), the mukallaf himself (mahkum alayh), and the accidents (awarid) that affect the ruling. All these are covered under the general proposition. The passage concludes by reaffirming the subject.

Key Terms
العوارض الذاتية (al-ʿawāriḍ al-dhātiyya): Essential accidents or inseparable attributes of a thing that are intrinsic to its nature.
الأدلة الشرعية (al-adilla al-sharʿiyya): The Shar'i evidences: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, etc.
الأحكام الشرعية (al-aḥkām al-sharʿiyya): Shar'i rulings: wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh, haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the 'essential accidents' of the Shar'i evidences?
A) Their textual wording
B) Their historical accuracy
C) Their establishment of the rulings
D) Their classification as mutawatir or ahad

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is defined by its dual subject: evidences and rulings, studied through their essential mutual relationship.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
12 min
Subject and Essential Accidents in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the subject and essential accidents of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of essential accidents in usul al-fiqh and identify how they define the scope of the science.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh does not study evidence and rulings directly, but their essential accidents.

This lesson clarifies what precisely usul al-fiqh studies. The commentators emphasize that every science examines the essential accidents of its subject, not the subject itself. We will explore how this applies to usul and why certain proofs like ijma' and qiyas are discussed while Quran and Sunnah are not.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of mawdu' and arad dhati
Define the subject of a science as the thing whose essential accidents are studied. An essential accident (arad dhati) is a predicate that attaches to a thing due to its essence.
The Hanafi classification distinguishes three types of essential accidents based on the cause of attachment.
2
Identify the three types of essential accidents
1) Direct attachment, e.g., perception to man. 2) Through an equal cause, e.g., wonder to man through wonder. 3) Through a more general cause, e.g., motion to man through animal.
The commentator's examples are later critiqued for precision.
3
Apply to usul al-fiqh
The subject is adillah and ahkam, but we study their states (e.g., how a daleel establishes a hukm). Discussions like 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' predicate essential accidents on types of evidence.
All issues in usul return to establishing these essential accidents.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction about Quran and Sunnah
Usul does not explicitly discuss Quran and Sunnah because their authority is self-evident (badihah) to the usuli, unlike ijma' and qiyas which require proof.
This explains why only proof-needy sources are treated as explicit topics.

Source Text

قالوا: بحث فی هذا العلم یعنی ان دونوں کے احوال سے۔ مضاف کو حذف کرنے پر کیونکہ نہیں بحث کی جاتی علم میں نفس موضوع سے بلکہ اس (موضوع) کے احوال اور عوارض سے۔ مگر بیشک اس مضاف کو حذف کرنا شائع ہے۔ قوم کی عبارت میں۔ قوله: فموضوع هذا العلم مراد علم کے موضوع سے وہ چیز ہوتی ہے کہ بحث کی جائے علم میں اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے اور مراد عرض سے یہاں وہ ہے جو شی پر محمول ہو کر خارج ہو اس (شی) ہے۔ اور مراد عرض ذاتی سے وہ ہے جو اس کا منشاء ذات بنے بایں طور کہ لاحق ہو وہ شی کو اس ذات کی وجہ سے جیسے ادراک انسان کے لئے یا ایسے امر کے واسطے سے جو اسکے مساوی ہو جیسے تعجب انسان کیلئے تعجب کے واسطہ سے یا ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو شی سے اہم ہو کہ شی میں داخل ہو جیسے حرکت انسان کیلئے اس کے حیوان ہونے کے واسطہ سے۔ اور اعراض ذاتیہ سے بحث کرنے سے مراد ان (اعراض) کو محمول بنانا ہے علم کے موضوع پر جیسے ہمارا قول الکتاب یثبت الحکم قطعا یا اس (موضوع) کی انواع پر جیسے ہمارا قول الأمر یفید الوجوب یا اس (موضوع) کے اعراض ذاتیہ پر جیسے ہمارا قول العام یفید القطع یا اعراض ذاتیہ کی انواع پر جیسے ہمارا قول العام الذي خص منه یفید البعض یفید الظن۔ اور اصول فقہ کی تمام مباحث لوٹنے والی ہیں ادلہ اور احکام کے اعراض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کی طرف۔ ادلہ کے احکام کو ثابت کرنے کی حیثیت سے اور احکام کا ادلہ سے ثابت ہونے کی حیثیت سے اس معنی کہ بیشک اس فن کے مسائل کے تمام محمولات وہ اثبات اور ثبوت ہیں اور وہ چیزیں ہیں جن کو اس (اثبات و ثبوت) میں نفع اور دخل ہے پس ہوگا اس کا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام۔ ادلہ کا احکام کو ثابت کرنے کی حیثیت سے اور احکام کا ادلہ سے ثابت ہونے کی حیثیت ہے۔ پس اگر تو اعتراض کرے کہ کیا حال ہے ان کا کہ وہ بناتے ہیں اصول فقہ کے مسائل میں سے اجماع و قیاس کے احکام کو ثابت کرنے کو۔ اور نہیں بناتے اس میں سے کتاب و سنت کے احکام کو ثابت کرنا۔ تو میں کہتا ہوں کہ کیونکہ مقصود فن میں نظر کرنے سے وہ ایسی چیزیں ہیں جو محتاج ہوں دلیل کی طرف اور کتاب و سنت کا حجت ہونا بداہت کے مرتبہ میں ہے اصولی کی نظر میں۔ بوجہ اس کے ثابت ہونے کے کلام میں اور بوجہ اس کے مشہور ہونے کے لوگوں کے درمیان بخلاف اجماع اور قیاس کے اور اسی وجہ سے وہ درپے ہوئے ہیں اس چیز میں جس میں حکم کو ثابت کرنا واضح نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کہ قرائت شازہ اور خبر واحد ہے۔

تشریح قوله: علم انه۔ اس قولہ میں شاریخ نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔

سوال: یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے کہا اور ماقبل کی تفصیل سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اس علم میں ادلہ اور احکام سے بحث ہوگی اور اسکا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام ہیں حالانکہ ضابطہ ہے کہ کسی علم کے نفس موضوع سے بحث نہیں ہوتی اور اس سے لازم آتا ہے کہ نفس موضوع سے بحث ہو حالانکہ بحث عوارض سے ہوتی ہے۔ جواب: دیا یہاں مضاف محذوف ہے اور یہ حذف مضاف کلام عرب میں کثیر ہے اب عبارت ہوگی بحث عن احوال الأدلة والأحکام فلا اعتراض۔

قوله: فموضوع هذا العلم - یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے شاریخ نے اس عبارت میں مطلق موضوع کی تعریف اور عوارض ذاتیہ کی بحث بیان کی ہے۔ تو مطلق موضوع کہتے ہیں جس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی جائے وہ شی اس علم کا موضوع کہلاتی ہے۔ 

عوارض ذاتیہ: عوارض جمع ہے عارض کی اور عارض وہ ہے جو شی کی حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر شی پر محمول ہو مثلا یہ ٹوپی سر پر عارض ہے حقیقت سے خارج ہو کر محمول ہے یہ حسی مثال ہے عوارض کی چھے قسمیں ہیں۔ تمام عوارض کی وجہ حصر: عارض معروض کو لاحق ہو گا بلا واسطہ یا بالواسطہ اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے وہ واسطہ معروض کا جز ہوگا یا امر خارج ہوگا پھر اگر امر خارج ہو تو چار حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ امر خارج معروض کے مساوی ہوگا یا اخص ہوگا یا معروض سے اہم ہوگا یا معروض کے مبائن ہوگا۔ ان میں سے پہلی تین اقسام عوارض ذاتیہ کی ہیں اور باقی اقسام عوارض غریبہ کی ہیں۔ اس وجہ حصر سے ہر ایک کی تعریف بھی معلوم ہوگئی۔ 

تعریفات عوارض ذاتیہ: پہلی قسم: عرض ذاتی شی کا وہ اثر اور حال ہے جو شی سے خارج ہو کر شی پر محمول ہو محض اس کی ذات کی وجہ سے بغیر کسی واسطہ کے جیسے ادراک برائے انسان کہا جاتا ہے الانسان مدرک۔ اب ادراک عارض ہے اور انسان معروض ہے اور ادراک کا عارض ہونا بلا واسطہ ہے۔

فائدہ: پہلی قسم کی جو شاریخ نے مثال دی ہے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ انسان یا تو حیوان ناطق کا نام ہے یا نفس ناطق کا نام ہے اگر اول ہے جیسا کہ مشہور ہے تو پھر ادراک انسان کو بالذات (حیوان ناطق کے مجموعہ کے واسطہ سے) لاحق نہیں ہوسکتا بلکہ ناطق کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہے تو ادراک بواسطہ جز کے انسان کو لاحق ہوا۔ اور اگر انسان صرف ناطق کا نام ہے تو پھر آگے یہ تمثیل کہ حرکت انسان کو حیوان کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہے یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ انسان فقط ناطق کا نام ہے تو حیوان انسان...
They said: The discussion in this science is about the states of the two (i.e., evidence and rulings). With the deletion of the mudhaf, because one does not discuss the subject itself in a science but rather its states and accidents. However, this deletion of mudhaf is widespread in the speech of the people. He said: So the subject of this science - by 'subject of a science' is meant the thing whose essential accidents are discussed in the science. And by 'accident' here is meant that which is predicated on a thing and is external to it. And by 'essential accident' is meant that whose cause is the essence itself, such that it attaches to the thing due to its essence, like perception for man, or through something equal to it, like amazement for man through amazement, or through something more general that enters into the thing, like motion for man through his being an animal. And the purpose of discussing essential accidents is to predicate them on the subject of the science, like our saying 'The Book definitively establishes the ruling' or on its types, like our saying 'The command indicates obligation' or on its essential accidents, like our saying 'The general indicates definitiveness' or on the types of essential accidents, like our saying 'The general that has been specified indicates probability for some part.' And all discussions of usul al-fiqh return to establishing the essential accidents of evidence and rulings: evidence in terms of establishing rulings, and rulings in terms of being established by evidence. In the sense that all predicates of the issues of this art are those establishments and established things, and they are things that have benefit and intervention in that establishment and being established. So its subject becomes evidence and rulings: evidence in terms of establishing rulings, and rulings in terms of being established by evidence. Then if you object: What about them making the establishment of rulings of ijma' and qiyas part of the issues of usul al-fiqh, and not making the establishment of rulings of the Book and Sunnah part of it? I say: Because the purpose of looking into the art is those things that need proof, and the authoritativeness of the Book and Sunnah is at the level of self-evidence in the view of the usuli, due to its being established in speech and due to its being well-known among people, unlike ijma' and qiyas. That is why they engaged in that which is not clear in establishing a ruling, like the irregular recitation and the solitary report. 

Explanation of his statement: 'علم انه' - In this statement, the commentator answered an implicit question. 

Question: The matn said and from the preceding explanation it also became known that in this science one discusses evidence and rulings, and its subject is evidence and rulings, even though the rule is that a science does not discuss the subject itself, and this implies that the subject itself is discussed, while discussion is of accidents. Answer: Here there is a deleted mudhaf, and this deletion of mudhaf is frequent in Arabic speech. Now the expression becomes 'discussion of the states of evidence and rulings', so no objection. 

He said: 'فموضوع هذا العلم' - This is the first part of the commentator's expression. In this expression, the commentator explained the definition of absolute subject and the discussion of essential accidents. So 'absolute subject' is that thing whose essential accidents are discussed; that thing is called the subject of that science. 

Essential accidents: 'عوارض' is the plural of 'عارض', and 'عارض' is that which is external to the reality of a thing and is predicated on it. For example, this cap is an accident on the head; external to the reality and predicated. This is a sensory example. Accidents have six types. The cause of all accidents: an accident will attach to the subject either without mediation or with mediation. If with mediation, the mediation is either a part of the subject or an external matter. Then if external, it is either equal to the subject, or more specific, or more general, or opposite. Among these, the first three types are essential accidents, and the remaining types are accidental accidents. From this cause of division, the definition of each becomes known. 

Definitions of essential accidents: First type: essential accident is that effect and state of a thing that is external to the thing and predicated on it solely due to its essence without any mediation, like perception for man, as it is said 'al-insan mudrik'. Now perception is the accident and man is the subject, and perception's being an accident is without mediation. 

Benefit: The example that the commentator gave for the first type is not correct, because 'insan' either means 'hayawan natiq' or 'nafs natiq'. If the first, as is well-known, then perception does not attach to man essentially (through the combination of hayawan natiq) but rather attaches through natiq, so perception attaches to man through a part. And if 'insan' means only 'natiq', then the later example that motion attaches to man through animal is not correct, because man is only 'natiq', so animal and man...
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Altarweeh on the matn of Al-Tawdih. It begins by addressing the definition of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains that when we say the science discusses 'adillah and ahkam', it actually discusses their states and accidents, not the things themselves. This is a standard principle: every science examines the essential accidents (al-‘awarid al-dhatiyyah) of its subject, not the subject per se. The commentator then defines 'essential accident' as an attribute that attaches to a thing due to its essence, either directly (like perception to man) or through something equal (like wonder through wonder) or something more general (like motion through animal). He then links this to usul al-fiqh: the discussions all revolve around establishing the essential accidents of adillah (e.g., 'the Book definitively establishes a ruling') and ahkam (e.g., 'the command indicates obligation'). A question arises: why do usul scholars discuss ijma' and qiyas but not the Book and Sunnah as sources? The answer: the authority of the Book and Sunnah is self-evident (badihah) to the usuli, whereas ijma' and qiyas require proof, so only the latter are discussed. The passage then moves to a critique of the commentator's example for the first type of essential accident. The critic (likely from al-Talwih) points out that if 'insan' means 'hayawan natiq', then perception attaches through the part 'natiq', not directly, so it is not a valid example of a non-mediated essential accident. If 'insan' means only 'natiq', then the later example of motion through animal fails because man is not animal. This shows the rigorous analytical method of Hanafi usul, where even examples are scrutinized for logical consistency.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, i.e., the thing whose essential accidents are studied.
عرض ذاتی (arad dhati): An essential accident: a predicate that attaches to a thing due to its essence, either without mediation or through an equal or more general cause.
مضاف محذوف (mudaf mahdhuf): A deleted genitive construct; here, the word 'ahwal' (states) is deleted before 'adillah wa ahkam' to avoid implying discussion of the subjects themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does usul al-fiqh not explicitly discuss the establishment of rulings from the Quran and Sunnah as part of its issues?
A) Because those are not evidence.
B) Because their authority is self-evident to the usuli.
C) Because they are only discussed in fiqh, not usul.
D) Because they are subject to naskh.

Key Takeaway
The subject of usul al-fiqh is adillah and ahkam, but the science investigates their essential accidents, not the entities themselves.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs and Rulings
Defining the subject of usul al-fiqh as both proofs and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi view on the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh and evaluate the opposing opinion that limits it to proofs alone.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh studies both proofs and rulings; limiting it to proofs alone is incorrect.

In this passage from Al-Talwih, the author clarifies the proper scope of Usul al-Fiqh. While some scholars restrict its subject to the four proofs, the correct view—and the one adopted by the Hanafi school—includes the five categories of rulings as well. Understanding this definition is essential because it determines which topics belong to the science and how we approach the derivation of fiqh from its sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing views
Note that one view limits the subject to the four proofs, while the correct view includes both proofs and rulings. The author cites the source of the opposing view (sahib al-Ahkam).
2
Analyze the reasoning behind the correct view
The passage argues that investigations in Usul al-Fiqh pertain to both the states of proofs and the states of rulings. The author uses the analogy of logic, whose subject includes both conceptions and assentations, to illustrate that a science can have two components.
3
Understand the practical consequence
If rulings were excluded, discussions about the division into wajib, haram, etc. would not belong in Usul. By including them, the Hanafi school legitimizes such discussions within the discipline.
4
Synthesize the definition
Articulate the correct definition: the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is the four proofs and the five rulings, studied in relation to how proofs establish rulings in general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلويح
قوله ) أن يذكر مباحث الحكم بعد مباحث الأدلة ؛ لأن الدليل مقدم بالذات والبحث عنه أهم في فن الأصول
قوله ( كما أن الخ ( موضوع المنطق التصورات والتصديقات لأنه يبحث عن أحوال التصور من حيث إنه حد أو رسم فيوصل إلى تصور ومن حيث إنه جنس أو فصل أو خاصة فيتركب منها حد أو رسم وعن أحوال التصديق من حيث إنه حجة توصل إلى تصديق ومن حيث إنه قضية أو عكس قضية أو نقيض فيؤلف منها حجة وبالجملة جميع مباحثه راجعة إلى الإيصال وما له دخل في الإيصال وقد يقع البحث عن أحوال التصور الموصل إليه بأنه إن كان بسيطا لا يحد ، وإن كان مركبا من الجنس والفصل يحد ، وإن كان له خاصة لازمة بينة يرسم وإلا فلا ويمكن أن يجعل ذلك راجعا إلى البحث عن أحوال التصور المؤصل بأن يقال : معناه أن الحد يوصل إلى المركب دون البسيط فيكون من المسائل قوله ( لكن الصحيح ) ذهب صاحب الأحكام إلى أن موضوع أصول الفقه هو الأدلة الأربعة ولا يبحث فيه عن أحوال الأحكام ، بل إنما يحتاج إلى تصورها ليتمكن من إثباتها ونفيها لكن الصحيح أن موضوعه الأدلة والأحكام ؛ لأنا رجعنا الأدلة بالتعميم إلى الأربعة والأحكام إلى الخمسة ونظرنا في المباحث المتعلقة بكيفية إثبات الأدلة للأحكام إجمالا فوجدنا بعضها راجعة إلى أحوال الأدلة وبعضها راجعة إلى أحوال الأحكام كما ذكره المصنف في تحصيل القضية الكلية التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه فجعل أحدهما من المقاصد والآخر من اللواحق تحكم غاية ما في الباب أن مباحث الأدلة أكثر وأهم لكنه لا يقتضي الأصالة والاستقلال .
Al-Talwih: His statement: 'That the discussions of rulings are mentioned after the discussions of proofs' because the proof is prior by essence and the investigation of it is more important in the field of Usul. His statement: 'Just as...' The subject of logic is tasawwurat (conceptions) and tasdiqat (assentations) because it investigates the states of conception in that it is a definition (hadd) or a description (rasm) so it leads to conception, and in that it is genus (jins) or differentia (fasl) or property (khasah) so a definition or description is composed from them; and it investigates the states of assent in that it is an argument (hujjah) that leads to assent, and in that it is a proposition (qadiyyah) or the converse of a proposition or its contradictory, so an argument is composed from them. In summary, all its investigations relate to that which leads and that which has a role in leading. And research may occur on the states of the conception being led to: if it is simple, it is not defined; if it is composite of genus and differentia, it is defined; if it has a necessary and evident property, it is described; otherwise not. It is possible to make that revert to the investigation of the states of the leading conception by saying: its meaning is that the definition leads to the composite, not the simple, so it is among the issues. His statement: 'But the correct view': The author of al-Ahkam held that the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is the four proofs only, and it does not investigate the states of rulings; rather, it only needs to conceive them to be able to affirm or negate them. But the correct view is that its subject is the proofs and the rulings; because we have reduced the proofs by generalization to four, and the rulings to five, and we have considered the investigations related to the manner of the proofs establishing the rulings in summary. We find that some of them relate to the states of the proofs, and some relate to the states of the rulings, as the author mentioned in obtaining the universal proposition by which fiqh is reached. He made one of them among the objectives and the other among the attachments governing. The utmost in the matter is that the discussions of proofs are more numerous and important, but that does not require originality and independence.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh. The author, in the commentary (Talwih), begins by explaining why discussions of rulings come after discussions of proofs: proofs are inherently prior and their study is more important. Then a comparison is made to logic: logic's subject is conceptions (tasawwurat) and assentations (tasdiqat). This serves as an analogy. The main point is the correct view of the subject of Usul al-Fiqh. A differing opinion from the author of al-Ahkam (likely al-Amidi or another scholar) is cited: he held that the subject is only the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), and that rulings are only needed for affirmation or negation, not as part of the subject. However, the correct view (al-sahih) according to the author is that the subject includes both the proofs and the rulings. The reasoning is that when we analyze the discussions, some pertain to the proofs and some to the rulings. Both are needed to achieve the goal of Usul al-Fiqh: establishing a universal proposition that leads to fiqh. The author of the original (al-Musannif) in Tahsil al-Qadiyyah al-Kulliyyah considered one of them as the objective (maqsid) and the other as the attendant (lahiq). The passage concludes by acknowledging that discussions of proofs are more numerous and important, but that does not give them sole originality or independence as the subject.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science; the things it investigates.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The science of the proofs of fiqh and the manner of deriving rulings from them.
أدلة أربعة (adillah arba'ah): The four proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
أحكام خمسة (ahkam khamsah): The five legal classifications: wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh, haram.
منطق (mantiq): The science of logic, whose subject is conceptions and assentations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view presented in this passage, what is the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Only the four proofs (adillah arba'ah).
B) Only the five rulings (ahkam khamsah).
C) Both the proofs and the rulings.
D) The universal propositions that lead to fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh studies both the proofs (adillah) and the rulings (ahkam) — excluding either would make the science incomplete.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Unity of Subject in a Science
Definitional clarification on the subject of a science

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the subject (mawdu') of a science and explain why a single science cannot have multiple unrelated subjects.

Core Idea
The unity of a science demands a single subject; if the investigation concerns a relation, both relata form that subject.

This passage tackles a foundational principle: what defines a science? The author argues that a science cannot have multiple subjects; if it studies a relation, both relata together constitute the subject. Understanding this clarifies how usul al-fiqh is a unified science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Note the assertion that some sciences (like medicine) appear to have multiple subjects. The author says this is incorrect.
The claim is that a single science can have more than one mawdu'.
2
Understand the exception: relation (idafah)
If the investigated matter is a relation between two things, then both relata together constitute the subject. Example: in usul al-fiqh, the relation between proofs and rulings.
The subject is both relata, but the science remains one.
3
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Usul al-fiqh investigates the establishment of evidences for rulings. This is a relation (idafah) between dalil and hukm, so both are the subject.
This unifies the science.
4
Apply to the counterexample: medicine
Medicine discusses drugs, but only in relation to their effect on the human body. Thus the subject remains the human body alone, not multiple subjects.
The apparent multiplicity is resolved by the relational nature.
5
Conclude the principle
If the investigated matter is not a relation, the subject must be one; otherwise, the science would split into multiple sciences.
Unity of science is by unity of its masail, which derive from the subject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمُ أَنِّى لَمَّا وَقَعَت فِي مَبَاحِثِ الْمَوْضُوعِ وَالْمَسَائِلِ أَرَدْت أَنْ أُسْمِعَك بَعْضَ مُبَاحِثِهَا الَّتِي لَا يَسْتَغْنِى الْمُحَصِّلُ عَنْهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يَلِيقُ بِهَذَا الْفَنْ مِنْهَا أَنَّهُمْ قَدْ ذَكَرُوا أَنَّ الْعِلْمَ الْوَاحِدَ قَدْ يَكُونُ لَهُ أَكْثَرُ مِنْ مَوْضُوعِ وَاحِدٍ كَالطَّبٌ مَثَلاً يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ بَدَن الْإِنْسَانِ وَعَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْأدْوِيَةِ وَنَحُوهَا ، وَهَذَا غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ وَالتَّحْقِيقُ فِيهِ أَنَّ الْمَبْحُوتَ عَنْهُ فِي الْعِلْمِ إِنْ كَانَ إِضَافَةَ شَيْءٍ إِلَى آخَرَ كَمَا أَنَّ فِي أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ يُبْحَثُ عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ الأَدِلَّةِ لِلْحُكْمِ وَفِي الْمَنْطِقِ يُبْحَثُ فِيهِ عَنْ إِيصَالِ تَصَوُّرٍ أَوْ تَصْدِيقٍ ، إلَى تَصَوُّرٍ أَوْ تَصْدِيقٍ وَيَكُونُ بَعْضُ الْعَوَارِضِ الَّتِي لَهَا مَدْخَلٌ فِي الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهُ نَاشِئَةٌ عَنْ أَحَدِ الْمُضَافَيْنِ وَبَعْضُهَا عَنْ الْآخَر فَمَوْضُوعُ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ كَلَا الْمُضَافَيْنِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنُ الْمَبْعُوثُ عَنْهُ الْإِضَافَةَ لَا يَكُونُ مَوْضُوعُ الْعِلْمِ الْوَاحِدِ أَشْيَاء كَثِيرَةٌ ؛ لأنَّ اتِّحَادَ الْعِلْمِ وَاخْتِلَافَهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِاتِّحَادِ الْمَعْلُومَاتِ أَى الْمَسَائِل وَاخْتِلافِهَا فَاخْتِلَافُ الْمَوْضُوعِ يُوجِبُ اخْتِلافَ الْعِلْمِ وَإِنْ أُرِيدَ بِالْعِلْمِ الوَاحِدٍ مَا وَقَعَ الاصْطِلاحُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ عِلْمٌ وَاحِدٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ رِعَايَةِ مَعْنَى يُوجِبُ الْوَحْدَةَ فَلَا اعْتِبَارَ بِهِ عَلَى أَنَّ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ أَنْ يَصْطَلِحَ حِينَئِذٍ عَلَى أَنَّ الْفِقْهَ وَالْهَنْدَسَةَ عِلْمٌ وَاحِدٌ وَمَوْضُوعَهُ شَيْئَانِ فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ وَالْمِقْدَارُ وَمَا أَوْرَدُوا مِنَ النَّظِيرِ ، وَهُوَ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ وَالْأدْوِيَةُ فَجَوَابُهُ أَنَّ الْبَحْتَ فِي الْأَدْوِيَةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ بَدَنَ الْإِنْسَانِ يَصِحُ بِبَعْضِهَا وَيَمْرَضُ بِبَعْضِهَا فَالْمَوْضُوعُ فِي الْجَمِيعِ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ .
ترجمہ: اور جان لے تو کہ بیشک جب واقع ہوا موضوع اور مسائل کی مباحث میں تو میں نے ارادہ کیا یہ کہ سناؤں تجھ کو ان دونوں کی بعض وہ مباحث کہ نہیں ہے مستغنی علم حاصل کرنے والا ان سے اگر چہ نہیں ہیں لائق وہ (ابحاث) اس فن کے ۔
Know that when I embarked on the discussions of the subject and the issues, I desired to let you hear some of its discussions which the researcher cannot do without, even though they may not befit this field. Among them: they have mentioned that a single science can have more than one subject, like medicine for example, wherein one investigates the states of the human body and the states of drugs and the like. This is incorrect. The verified position is that the investigated matter in a science, if it is the relation of one thing to another—as in usul al-fiqh one investigates the establishment of evidences for rulings, and in logic one investigates the conveyance of a concept or judgment to a concept or judgment—and some of the accidental attributes that have a role in the investigated matter arise from one of the two relata and some from the other, then the subject of this science is both relata. If the investigated matter is not the relation, then the subject of a single science cannot be multiple things, because unity and difference of a science are only by the unity and difference of the known objects (i.e., the issues). Difference in subject necessitates difference in science. If by 'single science' is meant merely what is conventionally agreed to be one science without regard to a meaning that necessitates unity, then it is not valid; otherwise anyone could then conventionally agree that fiqh and geometry are one science with two subjects—the actions of the mukallaf and quantity. As for the example they gave—the human body and drugs—the response is that the investigation into drugs is only insofar as the human body becomes healthy by some and sick by others, so the subject in all is the human body.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a definitional clarification about the subject (mawdu') of a science. The author refutes the claim that a single science can have multiple unrelated subjects. He explains that if the investigation is about a relation between two things (like adillah to ahkam), then both relata constitute the subject. If it is not about a relation, then the subject must be one, because the identity of a science is determined by its masail (issues). The example of medicine is addressed: even though medicine discusses drugs, it does so only in relation to their effect on the human body, so the subject remains the human body alone. This principle applies to usul al-fiqh, where the subject is the relation between evidences and rulings.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject of a science; what the science investigates primarily.
مسائل (masa'il): The issues or particular problems within a science.
اضافة (idafah): Relation between two things; if the investigated matter is an idafah, both relata form the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A single science cannot have multiple unrelated subjects; if the investigation concerns a relation, both relata form the subject.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Two Parts and Four Pillars of Usul al-Fiqh
Explains the division of the book's subject matter into two parts based on four sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main divisions of usul al-fiqh subject matter and state the four pillars of the first division in the Hanafi order.

Core Idea
The subject of usul al-fiqh is divided into two parts: the four sources (adilla) and the rulings (ahkam), with the four sources ordered by priority.

This passage explains the organizational framework of a classic Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. It clarifies what constitutes the main subject matter and how the material is structured. Understanding this division is essential for navigating usul works and appreciating the systematic approach of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions
The author states that the purposes of the book are placed into two divisions: first, the evidences (adilla), and second, the rulings (ahkam). The introduction on definition and subject matter is auxiliary, not part of these main divisions.
This is a common structural feature in Hanafi usul texts.
2
Recognize the four pillars of the first division
The first division is arranged upon four pillars: the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. These correspond to the four primary sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi school.
The order reflects priority in essence and honor.
3
Understand the rationale for ordering
The Book is placed first because it is prior in essence (qidam) and honor (sharaf). The Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas follow in descending order of authority. This ordering is not arbitrary but based on intrinsic properties.
The Hanafi school emphasizes this hierarchical arrangement.
4
Note the placement of tarjih and ijtihad
The chapters on tarjih (preference among conflicting evidences) and ijtihad (independent reasoning) are appended to the pillar of Qiyas. They are considered a completion (tatimmah) and appendix (tadhayyul) to the section on Qiyas.
This reflects the practical need to resolve conflicts and derive new rulings from qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلويح
قَوْلُهُ ) فَتَضَعُ تَفْرِيحٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ فَيَبْحَثُ عَنْ كَذَا وَكَذَا يَعْنِي بِسَبَبٍ أَنْ الْبَحْتَ فِى هَذَا الْفَنْ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ نَضَعُ الْكِتَابَ أَيْ مَقَاصِدَهُ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ وَإِلَّا فَبَحْتُ التَّعْرِيفِ وَالْمَوْضُوعِ أَيْضًا مِنْ الْكِتَابِ مَعَ أَنَّهُ خَارِجٌ عَن الْقِسْمَيْنِ لِكَوْنِهِ غَيْرَ دَاخِلٍ فِى الْمَقَاصِدِ وَالْقِسْمُ الْأَوَّلُ مُرَتِّبٌ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَرْكَانِ فِي الْأَدِلَّةِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْكِتَابُ ، ثُمَّ السُّنةَ ثُمَّ الْإِجْمَاعُ ثُمَّ الْقِيَاسُ تَقْدِيمًا للإقدَامِ بِالذَّاتِ وَالشَّرَفِ . وَأَمَّا بَابَا التَّرْجِيحِ وَالِاجْتِهَادِ فَكَأَنَّهُ جَعَلَهُمَا تَتِمَّةٌ وَتَذْيِلا لِرُكُنِ الْقِيَاسِ .
ترجمہ:۔ تفریح ہے اس کے قول فیحث عن کذا و کذا پر یعنی اس سبب سے کہ بے شک بحث اس فن میں جزی نیست کہ وہ اولہ اور احکام کے احوال سے ہے ہم رکھتے ہیں کتاب کو یعنی اس کے مقاصد کو دو قسموں پر وگر نہ تو تعریف اور موضوع کی بحث بھی کتاب میں سے ہے باوجود یکہ وہ خارج ہے دونوں قسموں سے بوجہ داخل نہ ہونے کے مقاصد میں اور قسم اول مرتب ہے چار ارکان پر ادلہ اربعہ میں یعنی کتاب پھر سنت پھر اجماع پھر قیاس مقدم کرتے ہوئے اقدم واشرف کو اور بہر حال ترجیح و اجتہاد کے دو باب پس گویا کہ بنایا ہے ان دونوں کو تتمہ اور دامن رکن قیاس کیلئے۔ تشريح بعضع الكتاب: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں ماتن نے ماقبل والے متن سے ربط بیان کیا ہے فنضع میں فا تفریحیہ ہے اور یہ تفریح ہے فیحت سے اور ٹیحث سے سمجھ میں آیا تھا کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام ہیں

پربطور تفریح کے ماتن" نے فنضع الكتاب علی قسمین کہا اور قسم اول میں اول اور قسم ثانی میں احکام بیان ہوں گے۔ کتاب سے مراد مقاصد کتاب ہیں
ای مقاصدہ: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ مانتی نے کہا ہے کہ فنضع الكتاب على قسمين قسم اول اولہ اور قسم ثانی احکام کے بیان میں ہے اب سوال یہ ہے کہ مقدمہ جس میں تعریف موضوع وغیرہ کو بیان کیا ہے بھی تو کتاب میں داخل ہے تو مصنف نے اس کا ذکر نہیں کیا خلاصہ یہ کہ کتاب دو قسموں پر مشتمل نہیں ہے بلکہ تین اقسام پر مشتمل ہے۔
جواب: فنضع الکتاب میں مضاف محذوف ہے ای فلنضع مقاصد الکتاب علی قسمین یعنی مقاصد کتاب دو قسموں پر ہیں باقی تو تم اور موضوع وغیرہ مقاصد کیلئے معاون و محمد ہیں لیکن مقاصد میں سے نہیں اس پر ۔
سوال: - شارع نے کہا کہ کتاب سے مراد مقاصد کتاب ہیں اور مقاصد دو قسموں پر ہیں اولہ اور احکام سوال یہ ہے کہ کتاب میں نقوش اور الفاظ ہیں نہ کہ ادلہ یہ کیسے کہا گیا کہ مقاصد بیان کئے گئے ہیں؟
جواب:۔ یہ مجاز کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی دال بول کر مدلول مراد لیا ہے کیونکہ نقوش دلالت کرتے ہیں معانی و مقاصد پر تو نقوش
بول کر انکے معانی و مقاصد مراد لئے گئے ہیں۔
الاول:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع قسم اول کی تقسیم کو بیان کرنا ہے تم اول کے چار اجزاء ہیں
کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اللہ و اجماع اور قیاس۔
تقدیم اللا قدم:۔ یہ شرح کی عبات کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شارح سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال: بی ترتیب کیوں رکھی؟ کہ کتاب اللہ کو مقدم کیا ؟
جواب:۔ چونکہ کتاب اللہ رتبہ کے اعتبار سے مقدم ہے تو جو چیز رتبہ کے اعتبار سے مقدم ہو اس کو ذکر میں بھی مقدم کر دیا
تاکہ ذکر طبع کے موافق ہو جائے۔
اجتہاد و ترجیح قیاس کا تمہ ہیں
و اماما با اترجیح ۔ بی شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شارح سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے
Talwih: His statement 'fa-tada'u' is a tafrih (elaboration) on his saying 'yabhatu 'an kadha wa kadha', meaning that because the investigation in this field is only about the states of the evidences and the rulings, we place the book, i.e., its purposes, into two divisions. Otherwise, the discussion of definition and subject matter is also part of the book, although it falls outside the two divisions because it is not among the purposes. The first division is arranged upon four pillars concerning the four evidences: the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas, giving precedence to that which is prior in essence and honor. As for the two chapters of tarjih (preference) and ijtihad (independent reasoning), it is as if he made them a completion and an appendix to the pillar of Qiyas.
Translation: It is an elaboration on his statement 'yabhatu 'an kadha wa kadha', i.e., because the investigation in this field is only about the states of the evidences and the rulings, we place the book, i.e., its purposes, into two divisions. Otherwise, the discussion of definition and subject matter is also part of the book, although it falls outside the two divisions because it is not among the purposes. The first division is arranged upon four pillars concerning the four evidences: the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas, giving precedence to that which is prior in essence and honor. As for the two chapters of tarjih and ijtihad, he made them a completion and an appendix to the pillar of Qiyas.
First part of the commentary: In this phrase, the matn author explains the connection to the previous text. The 'fa' in 'fanaḍa'u' is an elaborative 'fa', and it is an elaboration of 'yabhatu'... and from this it was understood that the subject matter of usul al-fiqh is evidences and rulings.
... [Page 429] ... As an elaboration, the matn author said 'fanaḍa'u al-kitāb 'alā qismayn', and in the first division he will explain the addresses (evidences) and in the second division the rulings. By 'kitāb' is meant the purposes of the book.
Second part of the commentary: This answers an implied question. Question: The author said we place the book into two divisions: first for evidences and second for rulings. But the introduction, which includes definition and subject matter, is also part of the book; the author did not mention it. So the book does not consist of two divisions but three.
Answer: In 'fanaḍa'u al-kitāb', there is an omitted genitive construction, i.e., we place the purposes of the book into two divisions. The introduction and subject matter are aids to the purposes, not among them.
Question: The commentator said that by 'kitāb' is meant the purposes of the book, and the purposes are two: evidences and rulings. But the book consists of scripts and words, not evidences. How can it be said that the purposes are expressed?
Answer: This is metaphorical: the signifier (scripts) is used to mean the signified (meanings and purposes), because the scripts indicate the meanings and purposes.
Third part: The commentator intends to explain the division of the first division. It has four parts: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
Fourth part: The commentator answers an implied question. Question: Why is this order given? Why is the Book of Allah placed first?
Answer: Because the Book of Allah is prior in rank, so in mentioning it is also given priority, so that the mention corresponds to the natural order.
Ijtihad and tarjih are the appendix of Qiyas.
The last part: The commentator answers an implied question.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage explains the structure of a typical Hanafi usul al-fiqh text (specifically Al-Tawdih). The subject matter is divided into two main parts: the four sources of evidence (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the rulings derived from them. The introductory material on definition and subject matter is not considered part of the core purposes but rather an aid. The order of the four sources reflects their priority in essence and honor: the Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. The chapters on tarjih (preference among conflicting evidences) and ijtihad (independent reasoning) are placed as a supplement to the section on Qiyas, since they are most relevant there. The commentary also addresses potential objections: why the introduction is not counted as a separate division, and why the book's scripts are referred to as 'evidences' (a metonymy). This clarifies the pedagogical organization of the science.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The science that deals with the evidences of fiqh in a general way and how to derive rulings from them.
الأدلة الأربعة (al-adilla al-arba'a): The four primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one evidence over another when they conflict.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent reasoning by a qualified jurist to derive rulings.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from a known ruling to a new case based on shared illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author place the chapters on tarjih and ijtihad after the section on qiyas?
A) Because they are less important.
B) Because they serve as an appendix and completion to the pillar of qiyas.
C) Because they only apply to the Quran and Sunnah.
D) Because they are part of the second division on rulings.

Key Takeaway
The subject of usul al-fiqh is organized into two parts—sources and rulings—with the four sources ordered by priority, and tarjih/ijtihad appended to qiyas.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Criteria for Topics in the First Chapter of Usul
Defining the scope of the first chapter's topics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two criteria (special connection to rulings and not covered elsewhere) to determine whether a given topic belongs in the first chapter of a Hanafi usul work.

Core Idea
Only topics with a special link to rulings and not already covered elsewhere belong in usul's first chapter.

The first chapter of a Hanafi usul text is not a catch-all for every topic related to conveying meanings. The commentator establishes rigorous criteria to filter out purely linguistic matters and topics exhaustively treated elsewhere. Understanding this scope sharpens your ability to identify the distinct domain of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general subject
The chapter discusses states (ahwal) of the Quran that have a connection to conveying meanings (ifadat al-ma'ani) and establishing rulings (ithbat al-ahkam). Note that definition of the Quran itself is excluded.
The definition is excluded because it is not an essential attribute (arad dhati) that can be predicated on the Quran.
2
Extract the first key criterion
Topics must have a 'special connection' (ta'alluq khas) to establishing rulings. This is more than a distant connection; it must be directly relevant to legal inference.
Examples given: khusus (specificity), umum (generality), ishtirak (commonality).
3
Extract the second key criterion
The topic must not have been independently and exhaustively covered in another science (e.g., Arabic grammar). Even if a topic has some connection, if it belongs to 'ilm al-arabiyya, it is excluded.
Examples of excluded Arabic topics: i'rab (declension), bina' (construction), ta'rif/tankir (definiteness/indefiniteness).
4
Apply the criteria to objections
The commentator answers two objections: (1) why definition is not included – because it is not an essential attribute; (2) why not all linguistic topics – because they either lack a special connection or are covered elsewhere.
This step shows the criteria in action: they serve to delimit the scope precisely.
5
Justify the placement of the arrangement discussion
Although one might think the chapter should come after discussing the Quran and Sunnah, the discussion of arrangement (nazm) is placed immediately after because the Quran's arrangement is mutawatir and preserved, making it more fitting.
This shows that criteria are not rigid; appropriateness (liyaqat) also plays a role.

وَإِثْبَاتِ الْأَحْكَامِ فَالْكَلَامُ فِي تَعْرِيفِهِ خَارِجٌ عَنْ ذَلِكَ ، وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْأَبْحَاثِ الْمُتَعَلَّقَةِ بِإِفَادَةِ الْمَعَانِى مَا لَهُ مَزِيدُ تَعَلَّقِ بِإِفَادَةِ الْأَحْكَامِ وَلَمْ يُبَيَّنُ فِي عِلْمِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ مُسْتَوفّى كَالْخُصُوصِ ، وَالْعُمُومِ وَالِاشْتِرَابِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ لَا كَالْإِعْرَابِ وَالْبِنَاءِ وَالتَّعْرِيفِ وَالتَّنْكِيرِ وَغَيْر ذَلِكَ مِنْ مَبَاحِثِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ ، وَإِنْ تَعَلَّقَتُ بِإِفَادَةِ الْمَعَانِي لَا يُقَالُ الْمُرَادُ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِإِفَادَةِ الْكِتَابِ الْمَعْنَى وَهَذِهِ تَعُمُّ الْكِتَابَ وَغَيْرَهُ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ وَكَذَلِكَ الْمَبَاحِبُّ الْمُورَدَةُ فِي الْبَابِ الْأَوَّلِ بَلُ الثَّانِي أَيْضًا ، وَلِهَذَا قِيلَ كَانَ حَقُهَا أَنْ تُؤَخَّرَ عَنْ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ إِلَّا أَنَّ نَظْمَ الْكِتَابِ لَمَّا كَانَ مُتَوَاتِرًا مَحْفُوظًا كَانَتْ مَبَاحِثُ النَّظْمِ بِهِ أَلْيَقَ وَالْصَقَ فَذُكِرَ عَقِيبَهُ.
ترجمہ: یعنی بیان ہے اس کی اقسام کا اور اس کے ان احوال کا جو متعلق ہیں معانی کا فائدہ دینے اور احکام کو ثابت کرنے کے ساتھ پس کلام اس کی تعریف میں خارج ہے اور مراد ابحاث المتعلقہ بافادة المعانی سے وہ ابحاث ہیں جن کو افادہ معانی میں مزید تعلق ہے اور ان کو پورا پورانہیں بیان کیا گیا علم عربیت میں مثل خصوص اور عموم اور مشترک ہونے اور اس کی مثل کے نہ کہ مثل معرب و اور مبنی ہونے اور معرفہ ونکرہ ہونے کے اور اس کے علاوہ مباحث عربیات میں سے اگر چہ ان کا تعلق ہے افادہ معانی کے ساتھ ۔ نہ کہا جائے کہ مراد وہ ابحاث ہیں جن کا تعلق کتاب کے معنی کے افادہ کے ساتھ ہو اور یہ شامل ہے کتاب اور اس کے غیر کو کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں اور اسی طرح ہیں وہ مباحث جوذ کر کی گئی ہیں باب اول میں بلکہ باب ثانی میں بھی اور اسی وجہ سے کہا گیا ہے کہ ان کا حق یہ تھا کہ ان کو مؤخر کیا جاتا کتاب وسنت سے مگر بیشک نظم کتاب جب متواتر اور محفوظ تھی تو ہیں نظم کی مباحث اس کے زیادہ لائق اور زیادہ قریب (ملی ہوئی ) پس ذکر کیا گیا اس (کتاب) کے بعد ۔
بحث عن الشئ کا کیا معنی ہے؟
تشریح : قولہ نور دا حاشہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارح دوسوالوں کا جواب ہے۔
سوال اول: یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا کہ باب اول کتاب اللہ کے افادہ معنی کے بیان میں ہے اور معنی کا فائدہ تو تعریف بھی دیتی ہے تو پھر تعریف کتاب کو بھی باب اول میں ذکر کر دیتے اس تعریف کو مقدم کیوں ذکر کیا ؟
سوال ثانی:۔ مصنف کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ باب اول میں جمیع مسائل کا محمول نفس افادہ بنے گا حالانکہ بہت سارے مسائل کا محمول افادہ واقع نہیں ہوتا تو نورد ابحاثہ کا مطلب ہوگا کہ ہم کتاب اللہ کے ایسے احوال سے بحث کرینگے جو نفس افادہ کے قبیل سے ہیں حالانکہ کتاب اللہ کے بہت سے احوال باب اول میں ایسے مذکور ہوتے ہیں جو افادہ معنی سے متعلق ہوتے ہیں لیکن نفس افادہ نہیں بنتے۔
جواب سوال اول:۔ اس طرح دیا کہ موضوع سے بحث کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو موضوع پر محمول کیا جا سکے تو کتاب اللہ کی ابحاث سے مراد اس کے احوال اور اقسام ہونگے کیونکہ احوال اور اقسام کتاب اللہ کے ایسے عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں جو اس پر محمول ہو سکتے ہیں باقی رہی تعریف تو اس کو کتاب اللہ کا عرض ذاتی بنا کر اس پر کیونکہ محمول نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے اس لئے باب اول کی مباحث سے یہ خارج ہے اس لئے اس کو مقدمہ میں ذکر کیا۔
جواب سوال ثانی:۔ اس طرح دیا کہ باب اول میں ان احوال سے بحث ہو گی جن کو افادہ معنی میں تعلق ہو نفس افادہ واقع ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ۔ فلا اعتراض فاحفظ خانہ دقیق ۔
والمراد بالابحاث:۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال:- یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا ہے کہ باب اول میں ان احوال سے بحث ہو گی جو افادہ معنی کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں یا ان کا اثبات احکام سے تعلق ہو تو پھر صرف ونحو کے قانون بھی باب اول میں ذکر کرنے چاہئیں کیونکہ وہ بھی افادہ معنی کے ساتھ ہیں اور ان کا اثبات احکام کے ساتھ تعلق بھی ہے کیونکہ صرف و نحو غیرہ میں جن امور سے بحث ہوتی ہے ان کو افادہ معنی اور اثبات احکام کے ساتھ تعلق قریب اگر چہ نہیں تعلق بعید ضرور حاصل ہے۔
جواب:۔ باب اول میں جو دو شرطیں ذکر کی گئی ہیں ان کے علاوہ دوشرطیں اور ہیں (۱) اثبات احکام کے ساتھ گھر اتعلق ہو یعنی خاص تعلق ہو (۲) ان کو کسی علم میں علیحدہ مستقلاً بیان نہ کیا گیا ہو اور علوم عربیت کے بعض قواعد کو اثبات احکام سے خاص تعلق نہیں ہے اور بعض کو تعلق ہے لیکن وہ دوسرے علم میں مستقلاً بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔
کیا ابحاثہ کی اضافت تخصیص کے لئے ہے؟
لا يقال:۔ یہ شرح کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔
[Arabic] And establishing rulings – so speech about its definition is outside of that. And what is meant by 'discussions related to conveying meanings' is that which has an additional connection to conveying rulings and was not fully explained in the science of Arabic, like specificity, generality, and commonality and the like, not like declension, construction, definiteness, indefiniteness, and other Arabic topics, even if they are related to conveying meanings. It should not be said: 'What is meant is that which is related to conveying the meaning of the Book, and these (topics) include the Book and other than it,' because we say: 'Similarly, the topics presented in the first chapter, indeed also in the second chapter, and for this reason it was said: Their right was that they be postponed after the Book and the Sunnah, except that since the arrangement of the Book was mutawatir and preserved, the topics of arrangement are more fitting and more attached to it, so they were mentioned after it.' [Urdu translation of the above] [Urdu] What is the meaning of 'discussion about a thing'? Explanation: His saying 'Nur Da's gloss': This is the first part of the expression; the commentator intends to answer two questions. First question: You said that the first chapter is about conveying the meaning of the Book of Allah, and definition also conveys meaning, so why did you not include the definition in the first chapter and instead mention it earlier? Second question: From the author's expression it appears that in the first chapter the predicate of all issues will be the very conveying, whereas many issues do not have conveying as predicate, so 'the topics of his discussion' would mean that we will discuss those states of the Book of Allah that are of the category of conveying itself, while many states in the first chapter are related to conveying meaning but do not themselves become conveying. Answer to first question: It is given that the meaning of discussing a subject is that its essential attributes can be predicated on the subject. So 'the discussions of the Book of Allah' refer to its states and divisions because states and divisions are essential attributes of the Book that can be predicated on it. As for definition, it cannot be made an essential attribute of the Book and predicated on it, so it is excluded from the discussions of the first chapter and therefore mentioned in the introduction. Answer to second question: It is given that the first chapter discusses states that have a connection to conveying meaning; it is not necessary that they themselves be conveying. So no objection. Preserve this precise point. 'And what is meant by discussions': This is the second part of the expression; the commentator intends to answer an implicit question. Question: You said that the first chapter discusses states that are related to conveying meanings or have a connection to establishing rulings. Then why not include the rules of morphology and syntax in the first chapter? Because they are also related to conveying meanings and have a connection to establishing rulings, since morphology and syntax discuss matters that have a close connection to conveying meanings and establishing rulings, even if not close, a distant connection certainly exists. Answer: In addition to the two conditions mentioned for the first chapter, there are two more: (1) a special connection to establishing rulings, and (2) they have not been independently explained in some other science. Some rules of the Arabic sciences do not have a special connection to establishing rulings, and some do have a connection but have been independently explained in another science. 'Is the idafa of 'abhasth' for specification?' 'La yuqalu': This is the third part of the commentary; the intention is to mention a question and answer it.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, explaining the scope of the first chapter of a standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. The author defines 'discussions related to conveying meanings' as those topics that have an additional connection to conveying rulings (as opposed to just linguistic meaning) and that were not exhaustively covered in Arabic grammar. Examples include generality, specificity, and commonality—topics directly needed for usul, unlike pure grammar like declension or definiteness. The commentator addresses two objections: (1) why the definition of the Quran was not included in the first chapter (answer: it is not an essential attribute that can be predicated on the Quran, so it belongs in the introduction), and (2) why not all topics related to conveying meanings are included (answer: only those with a special connection to rulings and not already covered elsewhere qualify). The passage clarifies the Hanafi methodological principle that the first chapter focuses on the Quran's own qualities (its arrangement being mutawatir) rather than on linguistic rules found in other sciences.

Key Terms
الأبحاث (al-abhath): The states and divisions that pertain to the Quran and can be predicated as essential attributes.
إفادة المعاني (ifadat al-ma'ani): Conveying meanings, i.e., the communicative function of language, especially as it relates to deriving rulings.
عوارض ذاتية (awarid dhatiyya): Essential attributes that can be predicated on a subject (here, the Quran) in a discussion.
تعلق خاص (ta'alluq khas): A special connection to establishing rulings, as opposed to a distant or general connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the definition of the Quran excluded from the first chapter?
A) It is not related to conveying meanings.
B) It is not an essential attribute (arad dhati) that can be predicated on the Quran.
C) It is already covered in Arabic grammar.
D) The first chapter only deals with rulings, not definitions.

Key Takeaway
The first chapter of a Hanafi usul work includes only topics that have a special connection to establishing rulings and are not fully covered elsewhere, reflecting the discipline's focused methodology.
